Sunnah Method of Stoning
Ruling that the stoning should be with the right hand and placing the pebble on the back of the thumb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method of rami according to the Hanafi school and identify the correct placement of the pebble.

Core Idea
The sunnah for stoning is to use the right hand and place the pebble on the back of the thumb, aided by the index finger.

The act of stoning (rami) during Hajj has specific recommended methods. This lesson covers the second sunnah method: using the right hand and placing the pebble on the thumb's back. While the general ruling is that rami is wajib, the specific manner described here is sunnah—performing it brings reward, omitting it does not incur sin. Understanding this distinction helps the pilgrim follow the Prophet's practice precisely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage describes the recommended (masnūn) method of stoning, not the obligatory (wajib) part. The act itself is rami, and the ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
Sunnah here means the Prophet's consistent practice; omitting it does not invalidate the stoning.
2
Understand the hand and finger placement
Note that the pebble is placed on the back of the thumb (the nail area) and the index finger is used to help flick it. This is a specific technique distinct from the other method (using the middle of the thumb).
The Urdu commentary mentions this method is more difficult and the pebble won't travel far, but it is sunnah.
3
Locate the lexical terms
Learn the Arabic terms 'ibhām' (thumb) and 'sabābah'/'musabbihah' (index finger). The index finger is named for its use during cursing, but in rami it assists the throw.
Understanding these terms helps in reading classical fiqh texts.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
While the Hanafi school adopts this method as sunnah, other schools may not specify the exact hand or placement. The practical difference is that a Hanafi pilgrim should prefer this method to earn the reward of following the sunnah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (difference of opinion) within the mercy of the Ummah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۵۸) والمسنون الـرمـى باليد اليمنى . ويضع الحصاة على ظهر ابهامه ويستعين بالمسبحة . ترجمه : (۱۳۵۸) اور رمی کا مسنون طریقہ یہ ہے کہ داہنے ہاتھ سے ہو، اور کنکری کو انگوٹھے کے سرے پر رکھے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے مدد لے۔ تشريح : [۲] یہ رمی کا دوسرا طریقہ ہے کہ انگوٹھے کے اوپر جو ناخن ہے اس پر کنکری رکھے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے مدد لیکر پھینکے۔ یہ طریقہ تھوڑا مشکل ہے اور کنکری دور تک نہیں جائے گی ۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ طریقہ مسنون ہے۔ فائدہ: ابھام : انگوٹھا۔ سبابہ : سب سے مشتق ہے، گالی دینا ، گالی دیتے وقت شہادت کی انگلی بار بار اٹھاتے ہیں اس لئے اس کو سبابہ کہتے ہیں، اسی کو مسبحة بھی کہتے ہیں۔ الخذف بپھینکنے کی کنکری حصی الخذف: ایسی چھوٹی کنکری جوانگلیوں سے پھینکی جائے۔
And the sunnah is to throw with the right hand. And he places the pebble on the back of his thumb and seeks help with the index finger. Translation: (1358) And the sunnah method of stoning is that it should be with the right hand, and he places the pebble on the tip of the thumb and takes help from the index finger. Explanation: [2] This is the second method of stoning: he places the pebble on the top part of the thumb (where the nail is) and takes help from the index finger to throw. This method is a bit difficult and the pebble will not go far. He says that this method is sunnah. Benefit: 'ibham' means thumb. 'sabābah' is derived from 'sabb' (to curse); because when cursing one repeatedly raises the index finger, it is called 'sabābah'; it is also called 'musabbihah'. al-khadhf: a pebble thrown by the fingers; hasā al-khadhf: a small pebble that is thrown with the fingers.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This lesson presents the second aspect of the stoning ritual: the use of the right hand and the specific placement of the pebble. The author states that the sunnah (recommended) method is to throw with the right hand. Additionally, the pebble should be placed on the back (zahr) of the thumb (the nail area), and the index finger is used to aid the throw. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this method is more difficult and the pebble won't travel far, but it is the sunnah. A lexical benefit explains the terms: 'ibhām' means thumb, and 'sabābah' (index finger) is derived from 'sabb' (cursing) because the finger is often raised during curses. The term 'khadhf' refers to the pebble used for flinging with the fingers. No explicit proof (dalil) is given in this passage, but it is understood to be based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as transmitted in reliable hadith.

Key Terms
مسنون (masnūn): An act established as a sunnah (recommended practice) of the Prophet; performing it earns reward, omitting it does not incur sin.
مسبحة (musabbihah): The index finger, so called because it is raised while saying 'subḥān Allāh' or during curses.
ابهام (ibhām): Thumb; the finger on which the pebble is placed.
سبابة (sabābah): Index finger; derived from 'sabb' (to curse).
خذف (khadhf): A pebble thrown by the fingers; used in rami.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the sunnah regarding the hand used for stoning?
A) Use the left hand
B) Use the dominant hand
C) Use the right hand
D) Use both hands

Key Takeaway
The sunnah for stoning is to use the right hand and place the pebble on the back of the thumb with the help of the index finger; following this earns reward, but the stoning itself remains valid without it.

Distance of Five Cubits for Stoning
Ruling on the required distance for rami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required distance for rami in the Hanafi school and identify the proofs from the Sunnah that establish it.

Core Idea
Rami requires a throw, not a drop — five cubits ensures the pebble is thrown.

Stoning the jamarat is a key ritual of Hajj, but its validity depends on proper execution. The Hanafi school specifies a minimum distance between the thrower and the jamrah to ensure the act is considered throwing (ramy) rather than merely placing. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled? The distance between the thrower and the jamrah. The hukm is that there should be five cubits (approximately 7.5 feet).
The text states 'yakun' (there should be), which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub when related to a condition of validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two narrations: (1) the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar in Bukhari and Ibn Majah describing throwing from the bottom of the valley, and (2) a narration from Ibn Abi Shaybah about throwing from under a tree.
Both are ahādith with zanni thubut, but they are relied upon in the school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith mentions throwing from batn al-wadi, which is about 4-5 cubits from the jamrah. The tree narration specifies a distance of 4-6 cubits. These prove that the Prophet (peace be upon him) threw from such a distance.
The distance ensures the pebble is thrown, not placed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may not require a specific distance, but the Hanafis consider it a condition for valid rami.
The Hanafi position is based on the literal understanding of 'ramy' as throwing.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is that five cubits is necessary. This is derived from the explicit narrations and the principle that a condition must be met for validity.
There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this; it is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۵۹) ويكون بين الرامى وموضع السقوط خمسة اذرع . ترجمه : (۱۳۵۹) رمی کرنے والے اور گرنے کی جگہ کے درمیان پانچ ہاتھ کا فاصلہ ہو۔ تشريح : آدمی اور جمرہ کے درمیان تقریبا پانچ ہاتھ کا فاصلہ ہونا چاہئے ، پانچ ہاتھ کا فاصلہ ساڑھے سات فٹ ہوگا۔ اس سے کم فاصلہ سے کنکری مارے گا تو مارنا نہیں ہوگا وہ تو کنکری ڈالنا ہوگا ، اور رمی کا معنی مارنا اور پھینکنا ہے اس لئے ساڑھے سات فٹ کے فاصلے سے کنکری مارے۔ وجه : (ا) عن ابن عمر انه كان يرمي الجمرة الدنيا بسبع حصيات... ثم يرمي جمرة ذات العقبة من بطن الوادى ولا يقف عندها ثم ينصرف ويقول هكذا رايت النبى الله الله يفعله ( بخاری شریف، باب اذار مى الجمر تين يقوم مستقبل القبلة ويسهل ،ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۷۵ ارابن ماجہ شریف، باب اذار می الحجمرة العقبة لم يقف عندها،ص ۲۳۹، نمبر ۳۰۳۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بطن وادی سے کنکری مارے، اور جمرہ عقبہ سے بطن وادی کا فاصلہ چار پانچ ہاتھ ہو گا ، اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ چار پانچ ہاتھ کی دوری سے کنکری مارے۔ (۲) اس اثر میں بھی اس کی وضاحت ہے۔ عن عبد الرحمن بن الاسود قال اذا جاوز الشجرة رمي الجمرة العقبة من تحت غصن من اغصانها . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ما قالوانی ای موضع یرمی من الشجرة ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۹۳، نمبر ۱۳۲۲۳) حضور کے زمانے میں جمرہ عقبہ کے پاس وادی میں کوئی درخت تھا، جو بھی نہیں ہے ، راوی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس درخت کے نیچے جا کر وہاں سے رمی کرے، یہ درخت چار چھ ہاتھ کی دوری پر ہوگا۔ اس لئے اتنی دوری سے کنکری مارے۔
And there should be between the thrower and the place of falling five cubits. Translation: (1359) There should be a distance of five cubits between the thrower and the place of falling. Explanation: There should be approximately a distance of five cubits between the person and the jamrah. Five cubits equals seven and a half feet. If he throws from a shorter distance, it will not be 'throwing' but rather 'placing' the pebble, and the meaning of ramy is to hit and throw, so he should throw from a distance of seven and a half feet. Proof: (1) From Ibn ‘Umar that he used to throw the first jamrah with seven pebbles... then he would throw Jamrat al-‘Aqabah from the bottom of the valley (batn al-wadi) and would not stand by it, then he would leave and say, 'Thus I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) doing.' (Bukhari, Bab idha rama al-jamratayn yaqoom mustaqbil al-qiblah wa yus’hil, p. 236, no. 1751; Ibn Majah, Bab idha rama al-jamrat al-‘aqabah lam yaqif ‘indaha, p. 239, no. 3032) This hadith indicates that he threw from the bottom of the valley, and the distance between Jamrat al-‘Aqabah and the valley bottom is about four or five cubits, so from this it is also understood that he threw from a distance of four or five cubits. (2) This is also clarified in the next narration: From ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad who said: 'When he passed the tree, he would throw from under one of its branches.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab ma qalu fi ayy mawdi‘ yarmi min al-shajarah, vol. 3, p. 193, no. 13223) At the time of the Prophet, there was a tree near Jamrat al-‘Aqabah in the valley; the narrator says: go under that tree and throw from there; that tree was about four or six cubits away. So he should throw from that distance.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on the distance required between the thrower and the jamrah for a valid stoning. The author states that there should be five cubits (approximately 7.5 feet) between the thrower and the spot where the pebble lands. The Urdu commentary explains that if the distance is less, the action would be considered 'placing' (dalna) rather than 'throwing' (phainkna), and the essence of rami is to hit and throw. Therefore, the minimum distance ensures that the pebble is thrown, not just dropped. Two proofs are cited: first, from Ibn ‘Umar’s practice of throwing Jamrat al-‘Aqabah from the bottom of the valley, which is about four or five cubits away; second, from a narration of Ibn Abi Shaybah about throwing from under a tree that was about four to six cubits from the jamrah. Both indicate that this distance is part of the Prophetic practice. The Hanafi school adopts this as a condition (shart) for the validity of the rami, though some scholars consider it merely a sunnah.

Key Terms
ذراع (dhirā‘): A cubit; approximately 18 inches (forearm length). Here, five dhirā‘ is about 7.5 feet.
بطن الوادي (baṭn al-wādī): The bottom or interior of the valley; a location used for throwing the jamrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended distance between the thrower and the jamrah according to this passage?
A) Two cubits
B) Five cubits
C) Ten cubits
D) No specific distance

Key Takeaway
For a valid rami in the Hanafi school, the thrower must be approximately five cubits (7.5 feet) from the jamrah, as established by the Prophetic practice.

If the Pebble Hits an Obstacle and Stops
Ruling on pebble hitting obstacle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a pebble that contacts an obstacle is considered a valid throw in rami and identify when repetition is required.

Core Idea
A pebble that stops after impact is not counted; it must reach the jamrah directly from the throw.

In the stoning ritual (Rami al-Jamarat), it is essential that the pebble reaches the target directly from the thrower's force. This passage from the Hanafi fiqh corpus addresses a subtle scenario: when the pebble hits an obstacle such as a person or a camel litter. The ruling hinges on whether the pebble stops after impact or continues on its original path. Understanding this distinction ensures the validity of this obligatory Hajj rite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is throwing a pebble during rami. The ruling here concerns validity: if the pebble stops after impact, the throw is invalid (requires repetition); if it continues, it is valid.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
The pebble hits an obstacle and either stops (thabata) or continues on its original path (sanna). The text specifies two cases: falling on a person or a camel litter.
3
Apply the condition to each scenario
If the pebble stops, the throw must be repeated because the thrower's force did not carry it directly to the jamrah. If it continues without stopping, the throw counts and suffices.
4
Understand the reasoning
Stopping indicates that the thrower's action was not the direct cause of the pebble reaching the target. Later external movement (e.g., litter shifting) does not restore the validity.
5
Note the practical consequence
The mufta bihi position is clear: if the pebble stops, repetition is wajib. This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۶۰) ولو وقعت على رجل او محمل ثبتت اعادها وان سقطت على سننها ذلك اجزاه . ترجمه : (۱۳۶۰) اگر کنگری کسی آدمی یا کجاوہ پر گر کر رکی رہی تو اس کا اعادہ کرنا ہو گا اور اگر اپنی رفتار پر چلتے ہوئے گری تو کافی ہے۔ تشريح : آدمی نے کنکری پھینکی وہ کسی آدمی پرگری، یا کجاوہ پر گری اور تھوڑی دیر تک وہیں رکی رہی پھر کجاوہ یا کسی اور چیز کی حرکت سے جمرات کے اندر گری تو چونکہ پھینکنے والے کے پھینکنے سے جمرات میں نہیں گری ہے اس لئے اس کنکری کو دوبارہ مارنا ہوگا، اور اگر کجاوہ پر یا آدمی پر گرنے کے بعد ٹھہری نہیں بلکہ اپنی رفتار سے چلتی رہی تو چونکہ اس کے پھینکنے سے جمرات میں گری ہے اس لئے یہ رمی شمار کی جائے اور دوبارہ مارنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ لغت: مجمل : کجاوہ۔ ثبت : بٹھہر گئی۔ سنن : طریقہ، یہاں مراد ہے پہلی رفتار سے چلتے رہنا۔ اجزاء: کافی ہے۔
And if it (the pebble) falls on a person or a litter (camel saddle) and stops, he repeats it; but if it falls following its path and continues, that suffices him. Translation: (1360) If the pebble falls on a person or a camel litter and stops, he has to repeat it; and if it continues on its own path (i.e., keeps moving with its momentum), then it is sufficient. Explanation: A person throws a pebble; it falls on a person or on a camel litter and stops there for a while, then by the movement of the litter or something else it later falls into the jamrah area. Since it did not enter the jamrah directly from the thrower's throw, he must re-throw that pebble. But if after falling on the litter or person it does not stop but keeps rolling on its own motion, then since it enters the jamrah by his throw, it is counted and there is no need to repeat. Vocabulary: 'mujmal' means camel litter; 'thabata' means it stopped; 'sanans' means its path, here meaning continuing with the first momentum; 'ajza'ahu' means it suffices him.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario during the stoning ritual: what happens if the thrown pebble hits an obstacle before reaching the jamrah. The ruling distinguishes two situations based on whether the pebble stops after impact. If the pebble hits a person or a camel litter (mahmil) and stops (thabata), then it must be thrown again because the thrower's action did not directly cause it to reach the jamrah. If the pebble continues on its course (sanna, i.e., its original momentum) after hitting the obstacle, then the throw is valid and suffices. The Urdu commentary clarifies that if the pebble stops and later moves due to external movement (like the litter shaking), it still does not count because the continuation was not from the original throw. The lexical notes define key terms. No explicit proof (dalil) is given; the ruling is based on the principle that the act of rami requires the pebble to reach the target (jamrah) as a direct result of the throw. This ruling is part of the detailed fiqh of Hajj in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ثبتت (thabatat): The pebble stopped after impact, i.e., it did not continue moving on its own.
سننها (sunanihā): Its original path and momentum; the pebble continues moving as thrown without stopping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when must a thrown pebble be repeated?
A) If it hits a person and keeps rolling
B) If it hits a camel litter and stops
C) If it falls short of the jamrah without hitting anything
D) If it misses the jamrah entirely

Key Takeaway
The validity of rami depends on the pebble reaching the jamrah directly from the thrower's force; if the pebble stops after impact, the throw must be repeated.

Pebble Hitting Obstruction Before Jamarat: Valid Throw Conditions
States ruling on pebble hitting obstruction during rami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a pebble that hits an obstacle before the jamarat and apply the condition of continuity to determine whether the throw counts.

Core Idea
A rami counts only if the pebble's momentum carries it directly into the jamarat without stopping.

When stoning the jamarat, it is essential that the throw itself brings the pebble to the target. This lesson examines the scenario where the pebble hits an intermediate object — a person or a saddle — before reaching the jamarat. The ruling depends on whether the pebble stops or continues in its course.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two possibilities: the pebble either stops (thabatat) on the obstacle, or it continues in its natural course (sunnaha) without stopping. Recognize these as distinct cases.
The Arabic terms are key: 'thabatat' vs 'sunnaha'.
2
Apply the ruling to each scenario
If the pebble stops, the throw is not valid and must be repeated. If it continues without stopping, the throw is valid and no repetition is required.
The text uses 'a'ada' (repeats) for the first case and 'ajzahu' (suffices) for the second.
3
Identify the underlying condition
The critical condition is the continuity of motion from the thrower's hand to the jamarat. If the pebble's momentum is interrupted, the throw is not considered the direct cause of reaching the jamarat.
This condition is derived from the requirement that the pebble be thrown directly to the target.
4
Consider the rationale
The ruling ensures that the act of rami is completed by the thrower's own action without reliance on external factors. A stopped pebble that later moves due to other causes is not attributed to the throw.
This reflects the principle of direct causation (mubashara) in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۶۰) ولو وقعت على رجل او محمل ثبتت اعادها وان سقطت على سننها ذلك اجزاه ترجمه (۱۳۶۰) اگر کنگری کسی آدمی یا کجاوہ پر گر کر رکی رہی تو اس کا اعادہ کرنا ہو گا اور اگر اپنی رفتار پر چلتے ہوئی گری تو کافی ہے تشریح : آدمی نے کنکری پھینکی وہ کسی آدمی پرگری، یا کجاوہ پر گری اور تھوڑی دیر تک وہیں رکی رہی پھر کجاوہ یا کسی اور چیز کی حرکت سے جمرات کے اندر گری تو چونکہ پھینکنے والے کے پھینکنے سے جمرات میں نہیں گری ہے اس لئے اس کنکری کو دوبارہ مارنا ہوگا، اور اگر کجا وہ پر یا آدمی پر گرنے کے بعد کی نہیں بلکہ اپنی رفتار سے چلتی رہی تو چونکہ اس کے پھینکنے سے جمرات میں گری ہے اس لئے یہ رمی شمار کی جائے اور دوبارہ مارنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ لغت مجمل : کجاوہ ۔ ثبت بٹھہر گئی۔ سنن : طریقہ، یہاں مراد ہے پہلی رفتار سے چلتے رہنا۔ اجزاہ: کافی ہے۔
And if it falls on a man or a saddle and stops, he repeats it; and if it falls in its course, that suffices him. Translation (1360): If a pebble falls on a person or a saddle and remains stationary, then he must repeat it; and if it falls while continuing on its course, it is sufficient. Explanation: A person throws a pebble, it falls on a person or a saddle and remains there for a little while, then due to movement of the saddle or something else, it falls within the jamarat. Since it did not fall into the jamarat from the thrower's throw, this pebble must be thrown again. And if it does not stop after falling on the saddle or person but continues at its own speed, then since it fell into the jamarat from his throw, this throw will count and there is no need to throw again. Glossary: Saddle. 'Thabata' means became stationary. 'Sunan' means way, here intended is continuing with the initial speed. 'Ajzah' means sufficient.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This is a ruling from Thamaratun Najah on the validity of rami when a pebble hits an obstacle before reaching the jamarat. The text presents two scenarios. First, if the pebble hits a person or a saddle and stops there, then even if it later falls into the jamarat through secondary movement, it does not count because the throw did not directly deliver it. The rami must be repeated. Second, if the pebble hits the obstacle but continues in its natural trajectory without stopping, then it is counted as a valid throw because the momentum of the throw carried it into the jamarat. The glossary clarifies key terms: 'thabata' means to stop, 'sunah' means the original course or momentum, and 'ajzah' means it suffices. This distinction hinges on the continuity of the pebble's motion from the thrower's hand to the jamarat.

Key Terms
ثبتت (thabatat): became stationary, stopped
سننها (sunanuha): its course, natural path or momentum
اجزاه (ajzahu): it suffices him, counts as valid
محمل (mahmil): saddle or houdah (conveyance on a camel)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a person throws a pebble that hits a person's head and stops there, then later falls into the jamarat when the person moves, is the throw valid?
A) Yes, because it eventually reaches the jamarat.
B) No, because it stopped before reaching the jamarat.
C) Yes, as long as the person intended the jamarat.
D) No, unless the person picks it up and throws it again.

Key Takeaway
A rami is valid only if the pebble's momentum carries it directly into the jamarat without stopping on an intermediate object.

Takbir with Each Pebble During Rami
Commands saying takbir with each pebble and provides proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying takbir with each pebble during rami, identify the proofs from hadith, and explain the wisdom behind it.

Core Idea
Say 'Allahu Akbar' with every pebble—a confirmed sunnah (or wajib) based on the Prophet's practice.

In the ritual of rami (stoning the jamarat), the pilgrim throws seven pebbles at each jamrah. This lesson examines the command to recite takbir (Allahu Akbar) with each pebble. The text presents an imperative, supported by hadith evidence, and adds a profound wisdom: to avoid inadvertently praising the devil and instead glorify Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The text opens with the imperative 'And say takbir with every pebble.' This is the primary ruling: the pilgrim should utter takbir when throwing each pebble.
The imperative form (كبّر) is key; in Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the command indicates obligation) unless there is a countervailing factor.
2
Examine the Proofs
Two hadith are cited: (1) from Jabir ibn Abdullah describing the Prophet's Hajj— he threw seven pebbles and said takbir with each; (2) from Ibn Umar— he threw the first jamrah with seven pebbles and said takbir after each. Both demonstrate the Prophetic practice.
The hadith are from Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Bukhari. They are ahad (solitary) in transmission, which affects the hukm level.
3
Reflect on the Wisdom
The text gives a rationale: when stoning the devil, one should not be silent (lest it appear as praise of shaytan) but rather extol Allah's greatness.
This wisdom (hikmah) reinforces the desirability of the act, though it is not a legal proof.
4
Consider the Hanafi Nuance
While the imperative suggests wujub (obligation), later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya) adopt the view that it is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
The difference arises because the proofs are ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the imperative is not strong enough to establish wujub in the later view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۶۱) وكبّر بكل حصاة ترجمه (۱۳۶۱) اور ہر کنکری کے ساتھ تکبیر کہتا ر ہے۔ وجه (۱) قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... فرماها بسبع حصيات يكبر مع كل حصاة منها مثل حصى الخذف رمى من بطن الوادى ثم انصرف الى المنحر ۔ (مسلم شریف ، باب حجه النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر کنکری کے ساتھ تکبیر کہے۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے جسکو صاحب ہدایہ نے پیش کی ہے عن ابن عمر انه كان يرمى الجمرة الدنيا بسبع حصيات يكبر على اثر كــل حـصـاـة . (بخاری شریف، باب اذار ی الجمر تین یقوم مستقبل القبلة ويسهل ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۷۵۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر کنکری کے ساتھ تکبیر کہے ۔(۳) اس میں حکمت یہ ہے کہ شیطان کو کنکری مارنے کے ساتھ شیطان کی تعریف نہ کرے بلکہ اللہ کی بڑائی بیان کرے۔
And say takbir with every pebble. Translation (1361): And say takbir with every pebble. Proof (1): He said: We visited Jabir ibn Abdullah... he threw seven pebbles, saying takbir with each pebble, like small pebbles, he threw from the bottom of the valley, then went to the place of sacrifice. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p.515, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p.278, no.1905). In this hadith, it is that he said takbir with every pebble. (2) The hadith that the author of al-Hidayah presented: from Ibn Umar that he used to throw the first jamrah with seven pebbles and say takbir after each pebble. (Bukhari, Bab Idha Rama al-Jamratayn, p.236, no.1751). In this hadith, it is that he said takbir with every pebble. (3) The wisdom in this is that when throwing pebbles at shaytan, he should not praise shaytan but rather extol Allah's greatness.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the recitation of takbir during rami. The text commands saying 'Allahu Akbar' with each pebble. It then provides two hadith proofs: the first from Jabir ibn Abdullah describing the Prophet's Hajj, where he threw seven pebbles and said takbir with each; the second from Ibn Umar, who also said takbir after each pebble. The commentary adds a point of wisdom: since the act of throwing pebbles symbolizes stoning shaytan, one should not inadvertently praise shaytan by remaining silent, but rather should praise Allah. This indicates that saying takbir is a sunnah or wajib act; the command form suggests obligation, though many Hanafi scholars consider it sunnah. The text does not explicitly state the hukm level, so the emphasis is on the action's desirability and its basis in the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): saying 'Allahu Akbar' (God is Greatest)
حصاة (hasah): pebble, plural hasayat

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the wisdom behind saying takbir with each pebble during rami, as mentioned in the text?
A) To distract oneself from the heat.
B) To avoid praising shaytan and instead praise Allah.
C) To count the pebbles.
D) To increase the volume of the stoning.

Key Takeaway
Saying takbir with each pebble during rami is a confirmed practice (sunnah mu'akkadah) based on the Prophet's action and command, and it serves to glorify Allah and avoid any semblance of praising the devil.

The Ruling on Sacrifice for the Mufrid
States the ruling on sacrifice for the mufrid (ifrad pilgrim)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sacrifice for the mufrid and explain the evidence from the Prophet's action.

Core Idea
For the mufrid, sacrifice is mustahab — recommended but not required.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on whether a pilgrim performing Hajj al-Ifrad (mufrid) must offer a sacrificial animal. The text distinguishes the mufrid from the qarin and mutamatti', for whom sacrifice is wajib. We will look at the proofs cited and understand why the Hanafi school considers it optional.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering a sacrificial animal (Hadi) by the mufrid. The ruling is explicitly stated as optional: 'if he wishes'.
The phrase 'in ahabbah' indicates non-obligation.
2
Recognize the hukm level
The Hanafi school classifies this as mustahab (recommended), not wajib. The commentary confirms it is supererogatory (nafl).
Contrast with qarin and mutamatti' for whom sacrifice is wajib.
3
Examine the proof
The text cites two hadith: Anas ibn Malik and Jabir ibn Abdullah, showing that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) sacrificed during his Hajj.
The Prophet's Hajj was Ifrad according to the Hanafi view.
4
Understand the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The Prophet's action establishes permissibility and desirability (istihbab), but the phrase 'if he wishes' limits it to mustahab. It does not indicate obligation because there is no command to do so for the mufrid.
The dalala of the hadith is zanni (speculative) and overridden by the explicit text of the matn.
5
Distinguish from other Hajj types
For mutamatti' and qarin, Hadi is wajib due to combining 'Umrah and Hajj or the Shimr rule. The mufrid is not combining, so no wajib.
This distinction is key to understanding the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۶۲) ثم يذبح المُفرد بالحجّ ان احبه ترجمه : (۱۳۶۲) پھر حج افراد کرنے والا چاہے تو قربانی کرے۔ تشریح : حج افراد کرنے والے پر ہدی واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے چاہے تو نفلی طور پر کرے، اور چاہے تو نہ کرے۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے ہدی ذبح کی . عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله أتى منى فأتى الجمرة فرما ها ثم أتى منزله بمنى و نحر ثم قال للحلاق خذ و أشار الى جانبه الأيمن ، ثم الايسر ثم جعل يعطيه الناس - ( مسلم شریف ، باب السنة يوم النحر ان بر می ثم یخر ثم تحلق ، ص ۵۴۸ نمبر ۳۱۵۲/۱۳۰۵ ابوداود شریف، باب الحلق والتقصیر ،ص ۲۸۸، نمبر (۱۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہدی ذبح کی ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے تحر فرمایا۔ دخلنا عـلـى جـابـر بـن عبـد الله ... ثم انصرف الى المنحر فنحر ثلاثا و ستين بيده ثم اعطى عليا فنحر ما غبر و واشركه في هديه - ( مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ، ص ۵۱۵ نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابوداود شریف، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمی کے بعد مفرد کو ہو سکے تو ذبح کرنا چاہئے (۳) یہ ہدی حج کرنے کے شکریہ کے طور پر ہے۔ اس لئے اللہ کا شکر یہ ادا کرنے کے لئے ہدی ذبح کرنا چاہئے ۔
Then the one performing Hajj al-Ifrad slaughters if he wishes. Translation (1362): Then the one performing Hajj al-Ifrad sacrifices if he wishes. Explanation: Hadi is not obligatory upon the one performing Hajj al-Ifrad, so if he wishes, he may do it as a supererogatory act; and if he wishes, he may not do it. Proof (1): In a hadith, the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) slaughtered Hadi. From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah came to Mina, then came to the jamrah and threw, then came to his dwelling in Mina and sacrificed, then said to the barber: 'Take' and pointed to his right side, then left side, then began giving the people. (Muslim, Bab al-Sunnah Yawm al-Nahr, p.548, no.3152/1305; Abu Dawud, Bab al-Halq wa al-Taqsir, p.288, no.198). In this hadith, he slaughtered Hadi. (2) In this hadith, he slaughtered: We visited Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he turned to the place of sacrifice and sacrificed sixty-three with his hand, then gave to 'Ali who sacrificed the remaining and shared in his Hadi. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p.515, no.2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p.278, no.1905). This hadith shows that after rami, the mufrid should slaughter if possible. (3) This Hadi is as a thanksgiving for performing Hajj, so one should slaughter Hadi to thank Allah.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This is a ruling regarding sacrifice for the pilgrim performing Hajj al-Ifrad (mufrid). The text states that it is optional: 'if he wishes'. The commentary explains that Hadi (sacrificial animal) is not obligatory for the mufrid, unlike the qarin (one performing tamattu') who must sacrifice. The proofs provided are hadith showing that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) sacrificed during his Hajj, which was Hajj al-Ifrad according to the Hanafi view. The text cites the hadith of Anas and Jabir to show that the Prophet did sacrifice, and this is recommended as a gesture of gratitude. The key takeaway is that for the mufrid, sacrifice is mustahab (recommended) but not wajib.

Key Terms
مفرد (mufrid): one performing Hajj al-Ifrad (Hajj only, without 'Umrah)
يذبح (yadhabah): he slaughters (an animal for sacrifice)
ان احبه (in ahabbah): if he wishes
هدي (hady): sacrificial animal brought to the Haram

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which type of pilgrim is sacrifice (Hadi) not obligatory?
A) Mutamatti' (performing 'Umrah then Hajj)
B) Qarin (performing 'Umrah and Hajj together)
C) Mufrid (performing Hajj only)
D) All pilgrims must sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufrid pilgrim's sacrifice is mustahab — recommended but not obligatory.

Shaving or Trimming After Rami: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on shaving or trimming hair after rami, with proof and definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving or trimming after rami, identify the minimum requirement for halq, and explain why shaving is afdal using the dalil.

Core Idea
Shaving or trimming is wajib; one-quarter of the head suffices for halq; shaving is better due to prophetic supplication.

After completing the rami of Jamarat al-Aqabah, the pilgrim must perform halq (shaving) or taqsir (trimming) as a wajib rite of Hajj. This lesson presents the Hanafi position on the minimum requirement and the virtue of shaving, grounded in Quranic and hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is halq (shaving) or taqsir (trimming) after rami. The Hanafi school holds it as wajib (obligatory). Choose one of the two; both fulfill the obligation.
If omitted, a dam (sacrifice) is required but Hajj remains valid.
2
Understand the minimum for halq
The text states that shaving one-quarter (rub') of the head is sufficient. This is analogized from the rule of wiping the head in wudu, where one-quarter suffices.
Shaving less than one-quarter does not fulfill the wajib.
3
Examine the Quranic dalil
Surah al-Fath 48:27 mentions pilgrims entering the Haram with heads shaved (muhalliqin) and trimmed (muqassirin). This indicates that both acts are valid ways of completing the rites.
The verse shows permission, not obligation, but combined with other evidences it becomes wajib.
4
Examine the hadith dalil
A hadith from Abu Hurayra records the Prophet praying three times for those who shave and then including those who trim. This shows the virtue of shaving over trimming.
The triple supplication indicates greater reward for shaving.
5
Define taqsir
Taqsir (trimming) is defined as cutting hair from the ends to the length of a fingertip (approximately one knuckle). This applies to the entire head, not just a part.
For women, cutting a lock of hair is sufficient; they do not shave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۶۳) ثم يحلق أو يقصر والحلق افضل ويكفي فيه ربع ترجمه : (۱۳۶۳)، پھر حلق کرائے یا قصر، اور حلق کرانا افضل ہے۔ اور چوتھائی سرکا حلق بھی کافی ہے۔ تشریح : رمی کے بعد سر منڈائے یہ بہتر ہے، اور قصر کرائے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے، البتہ سرمنڈوانا اس لئے افضل ہے کہ اس میں گندگی بھی پوری ختم ہو جاتی ہے اور حضور نے تین مرتبہ اس کے لئے دعا کی اور چوتھی مرتبہ میں قصر کرانے والوں کے لئے دعا کی ۔ اگر چوتھائی سر حلق کرالیا تب بھی کافی ہے، کیونکہ مسح میں چوتھائی سر کو پورے سر کے قائم مقام قرار دیا ہے۔ وجه : (۱) حلق کرانے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ لتدخلن المسجد الحرام ان شاء الله آمنين محلقين رء وسكم و مقصرين . ( آیت ۲۷، سورة الفتح ۴۸ ) اس آیت میں اشارہ ہے کہ عمرہ یا حج کے بعد حلق کرائے یا قصر کرائے (۲) عن ابی هريرة قال قال رسول الله الله الله اللهم اغفر للمحلقين قالوا و للمقصرين، قال اللهم اغفر للمحلقين قالوا و الـمـقـصــريــن ، قال اللهم اغفر للمحلقين قالوا و المقصرين قالها ثلاثا - قال : و للمقصرين (بخاری شریف، باب الحلق والتقصير عند الاحلال ، ص ۲۷۹، نمبر ۱۷۲۸ار مسلم شریف ، باب تفضیل الحلق على التقصير وجواز التقصير ، ص ۵۴۷، نمبر ۳۱۴۶/۱۳۰۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین مرتبہ حلق کرانے والوں کے لئے دعا کی اور تیسرے مرتبہ میں قصر کرانے والے کے لئے دعا کی ، اس لئے حلق افضل ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۶۴) اور تقصیر یہ ہے کہ اپنے انگلی کے سرے سے پوروں کی مقدار کاٹ لے۔
Then shave or trim, and shaving is better, and one-quarter suffices for shaving. Translation (1363): Then shave or trim, and shaving is better. And one-quarter of the head suffices. Explanation: After rami, he should shave the head – this is better; and if he trims, that is also permissible. However, shaving is better because it removes dirt completely, and the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) prayed three times for those who shave, and on the fourth time for those who trim. If he shaves one-quarter of the head, it is sufficient, because in wiping (masah), one-quarter of the head is considered equivalent to the whole head. Proof (1): The evidence for shaving is this verse: 'You will surely enter the Sacred Mosque, if Allah wills, in safety, with your heads shaved and trimmed.' (Surah al-Fath 48:27). This verse indicates that after 'Umrah or Hajj, one should shave or trim. (2) From Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah said: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: 'And those who trim?' He said: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: 'And those who trim?' He said: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: 'And those who trim?' He said it three times, then said: 'And those who trim.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Halq wa al-Taqsir, p.279, no.1728; Muslim, Bab Tafdil al-Halq, p.547, no.3146/1301). In this hadith, he prayed three times for those who shave and on the third time for those who trim, so shaving is better. Translation (1364): And taqsir (trimming) is that one cuts the amount of a fingertip from the ends.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the shaving or trimming of hair after rami in Hajj. The text states that after rami, one may either shave (halq) the entire head or trim (taqsir). Shaving is better (afdal). The minimum required for shaving is one-quarter of the head; this is analogized from the ruling of wiping the head in wudu, where one-quarter is sufficient. The proofs include the Quranic verse (48:27) which mentions both shaving and trimming, and a hadith where the Prophet prayed three times for those who shave and on the third time for those who trim, showing the virtue of shaving. The text then defines taqsir: cutting hair from the ends to the length of a fingertip (approximately one knuckle). This definition is specific to the legal meaning in Hajj. Shaving is better because it is more complete in removing impurity and because of the Prophet's specific supplication.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): shaving the head completely
قصر (qasr): trimming the hair, cutting from the ends
تقصير (taqsir): the act of trimming hair to the length of a fingertip
ربع (rub'): one-quarter (of the head)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount of head that must be shaved for the rite of halq to be sufficient according to this text?
A) The entire head
B) Half of the head
C) One-quarter of the head
D) A few hairs

Key Takeaway
Shaving or trimming after rami is wajib; one-quarter of the head shaved suffices; shaving is afdal due to prophetic supplication.

Ruling on Sacrifice for the Ifrad Pilgrim
Ruling on optional sacrifice after rami for ifrad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sacrifice for the ifrad pilgrim and explain why it is sunnah ghayr muakkadah.

Core Idea
Sacrifice for the ifrad pilgrim is recommended but not wajib.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on whether an ifrad pilgrim (one performing Hajj without Umrah) must sacrifice an animal. While many assume sacrifice is obligatory for all Hajj types, the Hanafi school distinguishes between types. Here, the ruling is derived from the Prophet's own practice and is understood as a voluntary act of gratitude, not a binding duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sacrificing an animal (hady) after stoning the Jamrah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The matn says 'then the ifrad pilgrim slaughters, if he wishes,' indicating it is not obligatory.
Focus on the phrase 'if he wishes' – this signals option, not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadiths: the Prophet's own sacrifice as narrated by Anas, and the detailed account from Jabir showing the Prophet sacrificed 63 animals himself.
These are ahad hadiths – zanni al-thubut, which aligns with the non-wajib ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action is a proof, but without an explicit command for the ifrad pilgrim, it cannot establish obligation. In Hanafi usul, a deed of the Prophet without a command indicates recommendation (nadb), not wujub.
The Prophet's sacrifice was his own practice; he did not command the ifrad pilgrim to do the same.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers sacrifice wajib for the ifrad pilgrim based on a different interpretation of the same or additional proofs. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
The difference lies in how each school weighs the Prophet's action and other evidences.

Section: Composition of actions of Hajj. (1362) Then the ifrad pilgrim slaughters, if he wishes. Explanation: (1362) Then the one performing ifrad Hajj, if he wishes, sacrifices. Commentary: The ifrad pilgrim is not obligated to sacrifice, therefore he may do it as a voluntary act, or he may not. Evidence: (1) In a hadith, the Prophet sacrificed. From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah came to Mina, then came to the Jamrah and stoned it, then came to his residence in Mina and sacrificed, then said to the barber, 'Take,' and pointed to his right side, then his left, then began giving (hair) to the people. (Muslim, Book of ... ; Abu Dawud, Book of shaving and trimming). This hadith shows that the Prophet sacrificed. (2) Another hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he went to the place of sacrifice and sacrificed sixty-three with his own hand, then gave (the rest) to Ali who sacrificed the remaining, and made him a partner in his sacrifice. (Muslim, Book of the Prophet's Hajj; Abu Dawud, Book of description of the Prophet's Hajj). This hadith shows that after rami, the ifrad pilgrim, if possible, should sacrifice. (3) This sacrifice is as a thanks for performing Hajj. Therefore, to give thanks to Allah, one should sacrifice.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning the sacrifice (hady) for the pilgrim performing ifrad Hajj (Hajj alone without combining Umrah). The Arabic matn states: 'Then the ifrad pilgrim slaughters, if he wishes.' The Urdu commentary clarifies that the sacrifice is not obligatory (wajib) for the ifrad pilgrim; it is a voluntary (nafl) act. The author provides three proofs: (1) The Prophet himself sacrificed after stoning the Jamrah, as narrated by Anas. (2) The Prophet sacrificed sixty-three animals with his own hand and delegated the rest to Ali. (3) The sacrifice is a form of gratitude for performing Hajj. Therefore, while not required, it is recommended (mustahabb) for the ifrad pilgrim to sacrifice if able.

Key Terms
مفرد بالحج (mufrid bil-hajj): A pilgrim who performs Hajj only, without combining it with Umrah (ifrad).
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal offered in the precincts of the Haram during Hajj or Umrah.

Key Takeaway
The ifrad pilgrim is not obligated to sacrifice; it remains a recommended sunnah, and omitting it does not affect the validity of Hajj.

Ruling on Shaving or Trimming Hair after Rami
Ruling on shaving or trimming hair and its minimum requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on halq and taqsir after rami, identify the minimum amounts required for each, and explain the preference for shaving based on the supplied proofs.

Core Idea
Shaving a quarter of the head suffices for halq; taqsir requires cutting at least a fingertip length; shaving is superior.

After stoning the Jamrah, the pilgrim must perform halq (shaving) or taqsir (trimming) as a wajib act of Hajj. This lesson clarifies the minimum requirements for each and why shaving is considered more virtuous, grounded in Quranic verse and Prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that after rami, the pilgrim should shave or trim. This is a wajib (obligatory) act; omission requires a dam.
2
Determine the minimum for shaving
The matn says 'wa yakfi fihi rub' al-ra's' – a quarter of the head suffices for halq. This is analogized to the masah rule in wudu.
3
Determine the minimum for trimming
Taqsir is defined as cutting at least the length of a fingertip (anmulah) from the ends of the hair.
4
Understand the preference for shaving
The hadith shows the Prophet made three supplications for those who shave and one for those who trim, indicating that shaving is afdal (superior).
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Hanafi: quarter of head suffices for halq. Shafi'i: three hairs suffice. The practical consequence is a difference in the minimum threshold.

(1363) Then he shaves or trims, and shaving is better, and a quarter of the head suffices. (1364) And trimming is that he takes from the ends of his hair the measure of a fingertip. Translation: (1363) Then he has his head shaved or trimmed, and shaving is superior. And shaving a quarter of the head is sufficient. Commentary: After rami, shaving the head is better, and trimming is also permissible. However, shaving is superior because it completely removes dirt, and the Prophet prayed three times for those who shave and in the fourth time for those who trim. If one shaves a quarter of the head, it is sufficient, because in wiping (masah) a quarter of the head is considered equivalent to the whole head. Evidence: (1) The proof for shaving is the verse: 'You shall enter the Sacred Mosque, if Allah wills, secure, having your heads shaved and trimmed.' (Surah al-Fath 48:27). This verse indicates that after Umrah or Hajj, one should shave or trim. (2) From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah said, 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said, 'And those who trim?' He said, 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said, 'And those who trim?' He said, 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said, 'And those who trim?' He said it three times, then said, 'And those who trim.' (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith shows that he prayed three times for those who shave and in the third instance for those who trim, so shaving is superior. Translation: (1364) And trimming is that he cuts from the tips of his hair the amount of a fingertip. Commentary: This is the definition of taqsir: cutting the hair of the head at least the length of a fingertip is called taqsir; it is called 'cutting hair'. Al-anmulah: fingertip.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the requirement of shaving (halq) or trimming (taqsir) after stoning the Jamrah. The matn states: 'Then he shaves or trims, and shaving is better, and a quarter of the head suffices.' The Urdu commentary explains that shaving is preferable because it ensures complete removal of impurity and because the Prophet made more supplications for those who shave. The minimum requirement for shaving is a quarter of the head, analogized to the rule of wiping (masah) in wudu. Trimming (taqsir) is defined as cutting at least the length of a fingertip from the hair. The proof includes the Quranic verse (48:27) that mentions both shaving and trimming, and the hadith where the Prophet prayed three times for those who shave and once for those who trim, establishing the superiority of shaving.

Key Terms
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the hair of the head completely or at least a quarter.
التقصير (al-taqsir): Trimming the hair by cutting at least the length of a fingertip from the ends.
الانملة (al-anmulah): The tip of the finger, used as a measure for the minimum length of hair to be cut in taqsir.

Partial Tahallul: After Rami and Halq, All But Women
Ruling with proof on partial tahallul after ramy and halq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what becomes permissible after ramy and halq, and identify the hadith evidence that supports the exception of women.

Core Idea
After ramy and halq, everything except women becomes permissible — women remain haram until tawaf al-ziyarah.

After completing the ramy of Jamrat al-Aqaba and shaving or trimming, the pilgrim enters a state of partial tahallul. Many prohibitions of ihram are lifted, but marital relations remain forbidden. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The matn states: 'And everything becomes permissible for him except women.' This is the partial tahallul after ramy and halq.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadiths are cited: from Ibn Abbas and Aisha, both explicitly excluding women. The hadith also confirms perfume is included.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted for this ruling.
3
Understand the exception's significance
Women remain forbidden because complete tahallul requires the tawaf al-ziyarah. The pilgrim is still in ihram for sexual relations.
This is a key distinction between partial and complete tahallul.
4
Apply to practical prohibitions
After ramy and halq, the pilgrim may use perfume, wear stitched clothes, trim nails, etc., but cannot engage in marital relations.
Also hunting, cutting trees, etc. become permissible as part of 'everything except women'.

Ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Its Timing
Ruling with proof on Tawaf al-Ziyarah and its timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, identify its timing flexibility, and explain the dalil from Quran and Sunnah that establishes its obligation.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a fard pillar of Hajj, and its time extends from the 10th to the 12th of Dhul Hijjah.

In this passage, we learn about Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah), the obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba that every pilgrim must perform during Hajj. The text gives the pilgrim a choice to perform it on the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhul Hijjah, with the 10th being superior. The evidence from the Quran and the Prophet's practice is presented to establish its obligation and timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal classification (fard, wajib, etc.) according to the Hanafi school.
The act is Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and it is ruled as fard (obligatory).
2
Understand the timing options
The text states the pilgrim may perform it on the same day (10th), or the next day (11th), or after that (12th). Recognize the flexibility within the days of tashriq.
The 10th is considered better (afdal).
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse (22:29) commands tawaf of the Ancient House. Analyze how the imperative (li-yattawwafu) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The verse is interpreted to refer specifically to Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
4
Examine the Prophetic proof
Two hadiths show that the Prophet performed this tawaf on the 10th. Note that this establishes the permissibility and timing flexibility, not a strict obligation to do it on the 10th.
The hadiths from Jabir and Ibn Umar are cited.
5
Note the Hanafi position on priority
The commentary emphasizes that performing on the 10th is better, but delaying to the 11th or 12th is permissible without penalty.
This shows the balance between obligation and convenience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٣٦٦ ) ثم ياتي مكة من يومه ذلك او من الغد او بعده فيطوف بالبيت طواف الزيارة
ترجمه : (۱۳۶۶) پھر اسی دن مکہ مکرمہ آئے یا کل، یا کل کے بعد اور بیت اللہ کا طواف زیارت کرے سات چکر ۔
تشریح : حاجی کو اختیار ہے کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کورمی ، ذبیح اور حلق کے بعد مکہ مکرمہ آکر طواف زیارت جو فرض ہے وہ کرے اور یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ گیارہویں یا بارہویں کو آئے۔ البتہ دسویں کو آنا زیادہ بہتر ہے۔
وجه : (۱) ثم ليقضوا تفثهم و ليوفوا نذورهم و ليطوفوا بالبيت العتيق ۔ ( آیت ۲۹ ،سورۃ الحج ۲۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ بیت اللہ کا طواف کرے اور اس سے طواف زیارت مراد ہے، اسی لئے طواف زیارت حج میں فرض ہے۔ (۲) دخلنا علی جابـر بـن عبـد الـلـه... ثم ركب رسول الله فافاض الى البيت فصلى بمكة الظهر - (مسلم شریف، باب حجۃ النبی ه، ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ دسویں ذی الحجہ کو ظہر تک مکہ مکرمہ تشریف لے گئے تھے (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابن عـمـران رسول الله الله افاض يوم النحر ثم رجع فصلى الظهر بمنی ۔ (مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب طواف الا فاضۃ یوم النحر ص ۵۵۰ نمبر ۳۱۶۵/۱۳۰۸ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الا فاضتہ فی الحج ص ٢٨١ نمبر ۱۹۹۸) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے طواف دسویں ذی الحجہ کو کیا ہے۔
(1366) Then he comes to Mecca on that day, or on the next day, or after that, and performs tawaf of the House, the Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Translation: (1366) Then he goes to Mecca on the same day, or the next day, or after that, and performs the Tawaf al-Ziyarah of the House, seven circuits. Commentary: The pilgrim has the choice: on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, after ramy, sacrifice, and shaving, he may go to Mecca and perform Tawaf al-Ziyarah, which is fard. Or he may go on the 11th or 12th. However, going on the 10th is better. Evidence: (1) Then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows and circumambulate the Ancient House. (Quran 22:29). This verse commands tawaf of the House, and it refers to Tawaf al-Ziyarah, therefore Tawaf al-Ziyarah is fard in Hajj. (2) We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then the Messenger of Allah mounted and went to the House (ifada), and prayed Zuhr in Mecca. (Muslim, Abu Dawud). This shows that the Prophet went to Mecca on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah by Zuhr time. (3) From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah performed ifada on the Day of Nahr (10th), then returned and prayed Zuhr in Mina. (Muslim, Abu Dawud). This also shows that the Prophet performed tawaf on the 10th.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah), which is the obligatory tawaf of Hajj. The matn gives the pilgrim the option to perform it on the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhul Hijjah. The Urdu commentary clarifies that it is fard (obligatory) and that performing it on the 10th is better. The evidence includes the Quranic verse (22:29) which commands tawaf of the Ancient House, interpreted as Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Additionally, two hadiths show that the Prophet performed this tawaf on the 10th. The timing is flexible within the days of tashriq, but delaying unnecessarily is not recommended.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed after ramy on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah or during the days of tashriq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 10th of Dhul Hijjah
B) 11th of Dhul Hijjah
C) 12th of Dhul Hijjah
D) 13th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a fard pillar of Hajj, and its allowed time extends from the 10th to the 12th of Dhul Hijjah.

The Partial Release from Ihram After Stoning and Shaving
Ruling-with-proof on post-stoning permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what becomes permissible after stoning and shaving during Hajj, identify the evidence from hadith, and explain the exception regarding women.

Core Idea
After stoning and shaving, everything except women becomes permissible; women remain prohibited until Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

After performing the stoning of the Jamrah and shaving or trimming the hair, the pilgrim enters a state of partial release from ihram. This lesson examines the specific ruling: which prohibitions are lifted and which remain, supported by clear hadith evidence. It also outlines the next required action, Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The ruling is that after stoning the Jamrah and shaving or trimming (halq/taqsir), the pilgrim is partially released from ihram: everything that was prohibited during ihram becomes permissible except women.
This is a consequence of completing two wajib actions of Hajj.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one from Ibn Abbas and one from Aisha. Both state explicitly: 'When you have stoned the Jamrah, everything becomes permissible for you except women.'
These are ahad hadith, but they are accepted as evidence in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'إلا النساء' (except women) is an explicit exception, establishing that women remain prohibited. This exception is definitive in its indication.
The exception is not open to interpretation; it directly excludes women from the general permission.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The Shafi'i school does not accept this exception and holds that women also become permissible after stoning and shaving. This leads to different rulings on when marital relations are allowed.
The Hanafi school adheres to the explicit wording of the hadith.
5
Connect to the next action: Tawaf al-Ziyarah
After achieving partial release, the pilgrim must perform Tawaf al-Ziyarah (seven circuits around the Kaaba). It is a fard (pillar) of Hajj, based on Quran 22:29 and the Prophet's practice.
Performing Tawaf completes the release; after it, women also become permissible.

Chapter on the Arrangement of Hajj Actions. The head (1364) and taqsir: that he takes from the hair of his head the amount of a fingertip (1365). And everything has become permissible for him except women (1366). Then he comes to Mecca on that same day or the next day or after, and performs circumambulation of the House, the Visitation Tawaf. Commentary: This is an explanation of taqsir: cutting the hair of the head to at least the amount of a fingertip is called taqsir; shaving is called halq. ... Translation (1395): Now all those things that were prohibited have become permissible for him except women. Commentary: Many permissible things were forbidden due to entering ihram; now after shaving, perfume, sewn clothing, etc., all become permissible except women. Proof (1): Hadith from Ibn Abbas: He said, 'When you have stoned the Jamrah, everything becomes permissible for you except women.' A man said, 'O Ibn Abbas, and perfume?' He said, 'As for me, I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ anointing his head with musk; is that perfume or not?' (Ibn Majah, etc.) From this hadith, it is known that all things that were forbidden due to ihram become permissible except women. (2) From Aisha, she said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, 'When one of you stoned the Jamrah of Aqaba, everything becomes permissible for him except women.' (Abu Dawud) In this hadith also, after stoning the Jamrah, women become permissible. Translation (1366): Then he comes to Mecca on that same day or the next day or after, and performs seven circuits of the Visitation Tawaf. Commentary: The pilgrim has the choice to come to Mecca on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah after stoning, sacrifice, and shaving to perform the obligatory Visitation Tawaf; and he also has the choice to come on the 11th or 12th. However, coming on the 10th is better. Proof: (1) Then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows and circumambulate the Ancient House. (Quran 22:29) In this verse, circumambulation of the House is commanded, and by it the Visitation Tawaf is meant; therefore, the Visitation Tawaf is obligatory in Hajj. (2) We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then the Messenger of Allah ﷺ rode and went to the House and prayed Zuhr in Mecca. (Muslim) From this hadith, it is known that he went to Mecca on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah until Zuhr. (2) Also in this hadith: from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ went to the House on the Day of Nahr and then returned and prayed Zuhr in Mina. (Muslim) From this hadith, it is also known that he performed Tawaf on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah is a ruling-with-proof exposition on the Hajj actions after stoning the Jamrah and shaving/trimming. The text first clarifies the definition of taqsir (trimming hair) versus halq (shaving), then states the core ruling: after these acts, everything that was prohibited during ihram becomes permissible except women. This is supported by two hadiths: one from Ibn Abbas and one from Aisha, both explicitly stating that after stoning, everything except women is allowed. The commentary in Urdu explains that perfume, sewn clothing, and other prohibited items become halal, but marital relations remain forbidden. The passage then introduces the next action: the pilgrim performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah (Visitation Tawaf) on the same day (10th) or later, with preference for the 10th. The proof for the obligation of Tawaf al-Ziyarah is derived from Quran 22:29 (interpreted as referring to this Tawaf) and the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as reported by Jabir and Ibn Umar, showing that he performed it on the Day of Nahr (10th). Thus, the ruling establishes the sequence: after stoning and shaving, the pilgrim is partially released from ihram (everything except women), and then he performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah, which is a pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms
الرأس (حلق) (al-ra's (halq)): Shaving the entire head; one of the obligatory acts of Hajj after stoning the Jamrah.
التقصير (al-taqsir): Trimming the hair by at least the length of a fingertip; an alternative to shaving for those who prefer not to shave.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The circumambulation of the Kaaba performed on the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhul Hijjah as an obligatory part of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
After stoning and shaving, the pilgrim is partially released from ihram: all restrictions except women are lifted, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah remains obligatory as a pillar of Hajj.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Its Effect, Timing, and Penalty for Delay
Explains the effect, timing, and penalty for delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah, explain its effect of making women permissible, identify its time window, and apply the penalty for delaying it according to the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Delay Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the 13th of Dhul Hijjah — a dam (sheep) is wajib in the Hanafi school.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a central pillar of Hajj that completes the pilgrim's state of ihram. In this lesson, we examine its timing, its effect of making women permissible, and the consequence of delaying it according to Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its effect
Recognise that Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the Visit Tawaf) is the obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed during the Days of Nahr. Its primary effect is that it makes women permissible for the pilgrim, as stated in the passage from the hadith of Ibn Umar.
The passage (1367) explicitly states: 'And women become permissible for him.'
2
Determine the time window
Note that the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah begins at dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and ends at sunset of the 13th (the end of the Days of Tashriq). Performing it on the first day (10th) is the best.
The passage (1368) says: 'And the best of these days is the first of them.'
3
State the Hanafi ruling on delay
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the 13th (i.e., after the Days of Tashriq) necessitates a dam (sacrifice of a sheep). This is a wajib penalty for delaying a time-bound wajib act.
The text says: 'if he delays it, a sheep (as a sacrifice) is incumbent upon him.'
4
Examine the evidence
The passage provides two types of evidence: (a) sayings of Ibn Abbas that omitting or delaying any Hajj ritual requires a dam, and (b) qiyas because these acts are time-bound.
The sayings are quoted: 'Whoever forgets any of his rituals or leaves it, let him spill blood.'
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that if the Tawaf is performed within the month of Dhul Hijjah, it is still considered ada (valid performance) and no dam is required. However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Imam Abu Hanifa's view.
The passage presents this as a 'faa'idah' (benefit), indicating it is a secondary opinion.

Source Text

ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ ۳۸۳ فصل تركيب افعال الحج سبعة اشواط (۱۳۶۷) وحلّت له النساء. (۱۳۶۸ ) وافضل هذه الايام اولها وان اخره عنها لزمه شاة لتاخير الواجب (١٣٦٩ ) ثم يعود الى منى فيقيم بها ترجمه : (۱۳۶۷) اب عورتیں بھی اس کے لئے حلال ہو گئیں۔ شریح: طواف زیارت سے پہلے بیوی حرام تھی لیکن طواف زیارت کیا تو اس طواف کی وجہ سے اب بیویاں حلال ہو گئیں۔ وجه : (ا) ان عبد الله بن عمر قال فذكر الحديث ... حتى قضى حجه و نحر هديه يوم النحر وافاض فطاف بالبيت ثم حل من كل شيء حرم منه - ( سنن سبیھقی ، باب التحلل بالطواف اذا کان قدسعی عقیب طواف القدوم ج خامس ص ۲۳۷، نمبر ۹۶۴۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف زیارت کے بعد عورت بھی حلال ہو جائے گی۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۶۸) اور طواف زیارت کے لئے ان دنوں میں پہلا دن افضل ہے، اگر مؤخر کیا تو تاخیر کی وجہ سے ایک بکری ( دم میں ) واجب ہے۔ تشریح : او پر آیا کہ طواف زیارت کا وقت دسویں تاریخ کے فجر کے وقت سے شروع ہوتا ہے،اور بارویں ذی الحجہ کے بعد جو شام ہے، یعنی تیرویں تاریخ کی شام وہاں تک وقت رہتا ہے، اس کے بعد مؤخر کرنا مکروہ ہے، چنانچہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی رائے ہے کہ ایام النحر کے بعد کوئی طواف زیارت کرے گا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا ۔
وجه : (۱) کیونکہ یہ چیزیں وقت کے ساتھ موقت ہیں اس لئے ان کو وقت سے مؤخر کرنے پر دم لازم ہوگا (۲) قول صحابی میں ہے ان عبد الله بن عباس قال من نسى من نسكه شيئا او تركه فليهرق دما سنن ، بھٹی ، باب من ترک شیئا من الرمی حتی یذ ہب ایام منی ، ج خامس ، ص ۲۴۸ نمبر ۹۶۸۸) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ کچھ بھول جائے یا چھوڑ دے تو دم لازم ہوگا ۔ اور چونکہ اس نے وقت پر طواف زیارت کو چھوڑ دیا چاہے بعد میں ادا کیا اس لئے اس کو دم لازم ہوگا۔ (۳) ایک اور قول صحابی ہے۔ عن عباس قال من قدم شيئا من حجه او اخره فليهرق لذلك دما (مصنف ابن ابی هیه ۳۵۳ فی الرجل يحلق قبل ان يذبح، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۴۵، نمبر ۱۴۹۵۴) اس قول صحابی سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقت سے مؤخر کیا تو دم لازم ہوگا۔ فائدہ: صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ عمر میں کبھی بھی طواف کرے گا وہ ادا ہی ہو گا اس لئے تاخیر کرنے سے دم لازم نہیں ہو گا۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۶۹) پھر منی آکر مقیم رہے۔
تشریح دسویں ذی الحجہ کو طواف زیارت کر کے واپس منی آئے اور وہاں ٹھہرار ہے اور رمی جمار کرتا رہے۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان رسول الله افاض يوم النحر ثم رجع فصلى الظهر بمنی (مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب طواف الا فاضہ یوم النحر ص۴۲۲ نمبر ۳۱۶۵/۱۳۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ طواف زیارت کے بعد حضور واپس منی تشریف لے آئے۔ (۲) يسأل ابن عمر قال انا نبتاع باموال الناس فيأتى احدنا مكة فيبيت على المال؟ فقال
Thamaratun Najah Volume 2 p. 383 Chapter on the Arrangement of Hajj Actions. Seven circuits (1367) and women become permissible for him. (1368) And the best of these days is the first of them; and if he delays it, a sheep (as a sacrifice) is incumbent upon him for delaying the obligatory. (1369) Then he returns to Mina and stays there. Translation (1367): Now women also become permissible for him. Commentary: Before the Visitation Tawaf, the wife was forbidden, but when he performed the Visitation Tawaf, due to this Tawaf his wives become permissible. Proof: (1) That Abdullah ibn Umar said: ... until he completed his Hajj and sacrificed his offering on the Day of Nahr and went to the House and circumambulated, then everything that was forbidden became permissible for him. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) From this hadith, it is known that after the Visitation Tawaf, women also become permissible. Translation (1368): And for the Visitation Tawaf, the best of these days is the first; if he delays it, a sheep (dam) is obligatory due to the delay. Commentary: It was mentioned earlier that the time for the Visitation Tawaf begins from the dawn of the 10th and lasts until the evening after the 12th of Dhul Hijjah, i.e., until the evening of the 13th. Delaying it beyond that is makruh. Accordingly, Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is that if someone performs the Visitation Tawaf after the Days of Nahr, a dam is obligatory upon him. Proof: (1) Because these actions are time-bound, so delaying them beyond their time necessitates a dam. (2) There is a saying of a Companion: Ibn Abbas said, 'Whoever forgets any of his rituals or leaves it, let him spill blood.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) In this saying, it is stated that if one forgets or leaves something, a dam is obligatory. And since he left the Visitation Tawaf on time, even if he performs it later, a dam is obligatory. (3) Another saying: Ibn Abbas said, 'Whoever advances or delays any of his Hajj actions, let him spill blood for that.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) From this saying, it is learned that if one delays beyond the time, a dam is obligatory. Benefit: The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that if he performs Tawaf at any time within the month, it is valid, and therefore no dam is obligatory for delay. Translation (1369): Then he returns to Mina and stays there. Commentary: After performing the Visitation Tawaf on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, he returns to Mina and stays there, and continues stoning the Jamarat. Proof: (1) Hadith: Ibn Umar said that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ went to the House on the Day of Nahr, then returned and prayed Zuhr in Mina. (Muslim) In this hadith, it is mentioned that after the Visitation Tawaf, the Prophet returned to Mina. (2) Ibn Umar was asked: 'We trade with people's money, so one of us comes to Mecca and stays overnight with the money?' He replied: ...
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of Hajj actions after Tawaf al-Ziyarah. It presents three numbered rulings: (1367) After completing seven circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, women become permissible for the pilgrim. The proof is from a hadith of Ibn Umar narrated by Bayhaqi, stating that after circumambulating the House on the Day of Nahr, all prohibitions are lifted. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the wife was forbidden before Tawaf, but after it she becomes halal. (1368) The best day for Tawaf is the first (10th of Dhul Hijjah), and if one delays it beyond the prescribed time (until after the 13th), a dam (sacrifice of a sheep) becomes obligatory. The text explains that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah extends from the dawn of the 10th to the evening of the 13th (end of the Days of Tashriq). Delaying it beyond this period is makruh tahrimi and requires a dam. The evidence comes from qiyas (these are time-bound acts), and from sayings of Ibn Abbas that omitting or delaying any ritual incurs a dam. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that if one delays Tawaf but performs it within the month of Dhul Hijjah, it is still valid and no dam is required because the act is still considered ada (performance within its broad time). This is a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa’s view is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, as stated in the text. (1369) After Tawaf, the pilgrim returns to Mina to stay there for the remaining days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, optionally 13th) to perform the stoning of the Jamarat. The proof is the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, who returned to Mina after Tawaf and prayed Zuhr there. The last part of the page includes a question to Ibn Umar about trade, which is partially cut off and not directly relevant to the main ruling.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed during the Days of Nahr (10th-13th Dhul Hijjah) as part of Hajj.
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The days of sacrifice: 10th, 11th, 12th (and sometimes 13th) of Dhul Hijjah.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) offered as a penalty for omitting or delaying a wajib act of Hajj.
صاحبين (sahibayn): Refers to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main students of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the consequence of delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the Days of Tashriq according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) No consequence; it is still valid without penalty
B) The pilgrim must offer a sacrifice (dam)
C) The Tawaf must be repeated
D) The pilgrim's Hajj is invalid

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a fard act of Hajj performed from the 10th to the 13th of Dhul Hijjah; delaying it beyond the 13th incurs a wājib dam according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa).

Tawaf al-Ziyarah Permits Marital Relations
Ruling that Tawaf al-Ziyarah makes women permissible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that Tawaf al-Ziyarah makes marital relations permissible and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah lifts the prohibition of women; without it, the pilgrim remains in full ihram.

This lesson focuses on a critical moment in Hajj: when does the pilgrim become fully permissible for his spouse? The source clarifies that it is Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah) that completes the major tahallul, permitting marital relations. The evidence comes from the Prophet's practice as narrated by Abdullah ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the circumambulation on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah). The ruling is that after performing it, women (marital relations) become permissible for the pilgrim. Before this tawaf, the wife is forbidden.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar describing the Prophet's actions on the Day of Nahr. The key phrase is: 'ثم حل من كل شيء حرم منه' (then he became permissible from everything that was prohibited to him).
The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi, indicating that after Tawaf al-Ifadah, all restrictions of ihram were lifted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'من كل شيء حرم منه' includes the prohibition of women. Since the Prophet did this after Tawaf al-Ifadah, it proves that this tawaf is the action that removes the prohibition of marital relations.
4
Note the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn (fard) of Hajj and that it alone completes the major tahallul, making women permissible. Other actions like stoning and shaving only achieve minor tahallul.
This distinction is important for practical fiqh.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider a pilgrim who has stoned the Jamrah al-Aqabah and shaved his head but has not yet performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah. According to this ruling, marital relations are still prohibited until he completes the tawaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل تركيب افعال الحج
سبعة اشواط (۱۳۶۷) وحلّت له النساء.
ترجمه : (۱۳۶۷) اب عورتیں بھی اس کے لئے حلال ہو گئیں۔
شریح: طواف زیارت سے پہلے بیوی حرام تھی لیکن طواف زیارت کیا تو اس طواف کی وجہ سے اب بیویاں حلال ہو گئیں۔
وجه : (ا) ان عبد الله بن عمر قال فذكر الحديث ... حتى قضى حجه و نحر هديه يوم النحر وافاض فطاف بالبيت ثم حل من كل شيء حرم منه - ( سنن سبیھقی ، باب التحلل بالطواف اذا کان قدسعی عقیب طواف القدوم ج خامس ص ۲۳۷، نمبر ۹۶۴۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف زیارت کے بعد عورت بھی حلال ہو جائے گی۔
Chapter: Sequence of Actions of Hajj. Seven circuits (1367) and women become permissible for him. Translation: (1367) Now women also become permissible for him. Explanation: Before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the wife was forbidden, but after performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah, by virtue of this tawaf, wives become permissible. Evidence: (1) That Abdullah ibn Umar said, and he mentioned the hadith... until he completed his Hajj and sacrificed his animal on the Day of Nahr and performed ifadah and circumambulated the House, then he became permissible from everything that was prohibited to him. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi...). From this hadith it is learned that after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, women also become permissible.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah) makes women permissible for the pilgrim. Before this tawaf, the pilgrim is in a state of ihram and is prohibited from marital relations. The evidence is a hadith from Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's (peace be upon him) actions on the Day of Nahr. After performing Tawaf al-Ifadah, he solved everything that was prohibited. This shows that Tawaf al-Ziyarah completes the major part of the Hajj rituals and permits intimacy.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The circumambulation of the Ka'bah performed on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah after spending the night at Muzdalifah and stoning the Jamrah al-Aqabah, which is a pillar of Hajj.
حلت له النساء (hallat lahu al-nisa'): Women become permissible for him, meaning marital relations are permitted after Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After which action does the pilgrim become permitted to have marital relations according to this passage?
A) Stoning the Jamrah al-Aqabah
B) Shaving the head
C) Tawaf al-Ziyarah
D) Sacrificing the animal

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the decisive act that permits marital relations for the pilgrim, based on the clear hadith evidence.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
