Best Time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Obligation of Dam if Delayed
Ruling on the preferred time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah and obligation of a sheep if delayed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preferred and permissible time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah and identify when a dam becomes wajib according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the Days of Nahr incurs a dam according to Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn differ but the mufta bihi is the dam.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah, one of the pillars of Hajj. The preferred time is the first day of the Days of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), but the permissible time extends to the evening of the 13th. Delaying beyond that triggers a penalty (dam) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, though his two companions (Sahibayn) disagree. We will explore the evidence from the sayings of the Companions and understand the practical consequence of this intra-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time frame
The act is Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The preferred time is the first day (10th Dhul Hijjah), but the permissible window extends from dawn of the 10th until the evening of the 13th.
The Days of Nahr are 10th to 13th Dhul Hijjah.
2
State the ruling on the preferred vs. permissible time
The best day is the first (10th). Performing it on any day within the Days of Nahr is valid, but delaying until after the 13th is makruh and, according to Abu Hanifa, necessitates a dam.
Permissible time is not unlimited.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa rules that a dam is wajib if tawaf is performed after the Days of Nahr. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that no dam is required because the entire lifetime is the valid period for tawaf.
The Sahibayn view is mentioned as a fāʼidah (benefit).
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The text cites two qawl sahabi: (1) Ibn Abbas – 'Whoever forgets or leaves a ritual, let him offer a sacrifice.' (2) Abbas – 'Whoever brings forward or delays something of his Hajj, let him offer a sacrifice.' These indicate that delaying a time-bound rite requires a dam.
The qawl sahabi is used as evidence for the binding nature of time-bound rites in Hajj.
5
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A pilgrim who delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the 13th must offer a dam according to the mufta bihi view; according to the Sahibayn, no penalty is needed. The school relies on Abu Hanifa's view.
The difference affects whether a sacrifice is required, not the validity of the tawaf itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۶۸) اور طواف زیارت کے لئے ان دنوں میں پہلا دن افضل ہے، اگر مؤخر کیا تو تاخیر کی وجہ سے ایک بکری ( دم میں ) واجب ہے۔ تشریح : او پر آیا کہ طواف زیارت کا وقت دسویں تاریخ کے فجر کے وقت سے شروع ہوتا ہے،اور بارویں ذی الحجہ کے بعد جو شام ہے، یعنی تیرویں تاریخ کی شام وہاں تک وقت رہتا ہے، اس کے بعد مؤخر کرنا مکروہ ہے، چنانچہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی رائے ہے کہ ایام النحر کے بعد کوئی طواف زیارت کرے گا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا ۔
وجه : (۱) کیونکہ یہ چیزیں وقت کے ساتھ موقت ہیں اس لئے ان کو وقت سے مؤخر کرنے پر دم لازم ہوگا (۲) قول صحابی میں ہے ان عبد الله بن عباس قال من نسى من نسكه شيئا او تركه فليهرق دما سنن ، بھٹی ، باب من ترک شیئا من الرمی حتی یذ ہب ایام منی ، ج خامس ، ص ۲۴۸ نمبر ۹۶۸۸) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ کچھ بھول جائے یا چھوڑ دے تو دم لازم ہوگا ۔ اور چونکہ اس نے وقت پر طواف زیارت کو چھوڑ دیا چاہے بعد میں ادا کیا اس لئے اس کو دم لازم ہوگا۔ (۳) ایک اور قول صحابی ہے۔ عن عباس قال من قدم شيئا من حجه او اخره فليهرق لذلك دما (مصنف ابن ابی هیه ۳۵۳ فی الرجل يحلق قبل ان يذبح، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۴۵، نمبر ۱۴۹۵۴) اس قول صحابی سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقت سے مؤخر کیا تو دم لازم ہوگا۔ فائدہ: صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ عمر میں کبھی بھی طواف کرے گا وہ ادا ہی ہو گا اس لئے تاخیر کرنے سے دم لازم نہیں ہو گا۔
Translation: (1368) And for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the best of these days is the first. If he delays it, then due to the delay, one goat (dam) becomes obligatory. Explanation: It came earlier that the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah begins from the dawn of the tenth date, and lasts until the evening after the twelfth of Dhul Hijjah, i.e., the evening of the thirteenth date. After that, delaying is makruh. Thus, Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is that if someone performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah after the Days of Nahr, then a dam becomes incumbent on him. Evidence: (1) Because these matters are time-bound, so delaying them from their time necessitates a dam. (2) There is a saying of a companion: Ibn Abbas said: 'Whoever forgets or leaves something of his rituals, let him spill blood (offer a sacrifice).' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi...) From this saying of the Companion, it is learned that if he forgets or leaves something, a dam becomes necessary. And since he left Tawaf al-Ziyarah at its proper time - even if he performs it later - a dam becomes necessary for him. (3) Another saying of a Companion: From Abbas: 'Whoever brings forward or delays something of his Hajj, let him spill blood for it.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...) From this saying, it is learned that if he delays from the time, a dam becomes necessary. Benefit: The Sahibayn say that no matter when he performs the tawaf during the lifespan, it is considered performed on time (ada), so delaying does not necessitate a dam.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage discusses the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The preferred day is the first (10th Dhul Hijjah), but the permissible time extends until the evening of the 13th. After that, performing it becomes makruh, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a dam (sheep) becomes wajib if one delays it beyond the Days of Nahr. The evidence includes qawl sahabi (sayings of the Companions Ibn Abbas and Abbas) indicating that leaving or delaying any ritual requires a sacrifice. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold a different view: they consider the tawaf valid as ada without dam regardless of when it is performed, because the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the entire lifetime. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, i.e., a dam is required if delayed beyond the Days of Nahr.

Key Terms
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The Days of Sacrifice: 10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
دم (dam): A sacrifice (usually a sheep) offered as a penalty for leaving a wajib or delaying an action.
صاحبين (al-Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if a pilgrim delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the 13th of Dhul Hijjah?
A) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated
B) A dam (sheep) becomes wajib
C) No penalty, the tawaf is still ada
D) The pilgrim must repeat the entire Hajj

Key Takeaway
Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the Days of Nahr incurs a dam according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and this is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.

Returning to Mina and Stoning the Jamarat on the 11th
Combined rulings on the post-tawaf stay in Mina and the stoning ritual on the 11th.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on staying in Mina after Tawaf al-Ziyarah and stoning the three jamarat on the 11th, and identify the primary evidence for each.

Core Idea
Stoning after zawal in order is wajib; staying in Mina is a sunnah rooted in the Prophet's practice.

This lesson covers two connected actions after the Day of Nahr: returning to Mina and staying for the nights of tashreeq, and the precise method of stoning the jamarat on the 11th. Both are established by the Prophet's Sunnah and the practice of the Companions. Understanding the rulings and their proofs helps ensure the Hajj is performed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two distinct actions described: (1) returning to Mina after Tawaf al-Ziyarah and staying there during the nights of tashreeq, and (2) stoning the three jamarat on the 11th.
The passage is divided into sections numbered (1369) and (1370).
2
State the hukm for each
Determine the legal status: staying in Mina is sunnah muakkadah, while stoning the jamarat is wajib.
Stoning is wajib because it is established by mutawatir practice; staying is a strong sunnah.
3
Locate the dalil for stoning
Find the hadith of Ibn Umar regarding stoning after zawal and the hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's practice.
The evidence is quoted in the text with references to Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Locate the dalil for staying
Identify the evidence for staying in Mina: the Prophet's return to Mina, his spending the nights there, and Umar's instruction not to stay beyond al-Aqaba.
Multiple hadith and athar are cited, including from Abu Dawood and Bayhaqi.
5
Apply the conditions for stoning
List the conditions and sequence: after zawal, with seven pebbles, in order (small, middle, 'Aqabah), saying takbir, and supplicating at the first two.
These details are derived from the practice described in the text.

He stones it with seven pebbles while walking, saying takbir with each pebble. Then he stands by it supplicating as he wishes, praising Allah Most High and sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him), raising his hands in supplication, and seeking forgiveness for his parents... for the Messenger of Allah... except Allah, so he spent the night in Mina and remained. Translation: (1370) And on the second day of the Days of Nahr, when the sun declines, he stones the three jamarat, starting with the jamra that is adjacent to Masjid al-Khayf. He stones it with seven pebbles while walking, saying takbir with each pebble. Then he stands for supplication for what he loves, with praise of Allah and sending blessings on the Prophet, and he raises his hands in supplication, and seeks forgiveness for himself, his parents, and Muslim brothers. Explanation: On the 10th, only stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah was performed, but on the 11th (the second day of the 10th), he stones the three jamarat and does so after zawal. He starts with the jamra near Masjid al-Khayf, throws seven pebbles with takbir, and at the first and second jamra he stands, sends blessings on the Prophet, and supplicates; after the third jamra he does not stand or supplicate to avoid crowding. Evidence: (1) I asked Ibn Umar: When should I stone the jamarat? He said: When your Imam stones, then stone. I repeated the question. He said: We used to wait, and when the sun declined, we stoned. (Bukhari...) (2) This hadith, which the author of Hidayah presented: From Aisha... [cut off]
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This combined passage covers two actions: first, returning to Mina after Tawaf al-Ziyarah on the 10th and staying there; second, the procedure for stoning the three jamarat on the 11th. The evidence for returning to Mina comes from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions. The evidence for stoning after zawal comes from the practice of the Companions, particularly Ibn Umar. The stoning is performed in sequence: first the small jamra nearest to Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle, then the large (Jamrat al-Aqabah). At the first two, one should stand and make dua; at the third, one should not stand to avoid crowding. The preferred time is after zawal. The text also emphasizes that spending the nights of tashreeq in Mina is sunnah, based on multiple hadith.

Key Terms
الجمرات (al-jamarat): The three stone pillars representing the devil, located in Mina, which are stoned during Hajj.
زوال الشمس (zawal al-shams): The sun's declination from its zenith, marking the beginning of the time for the zuhr prayer and the preferred time for stoning.
مسجد الخيف (Masjid al-Khayf): A mosque in Mina near the small jamra, used as a landmark to identify the first jamra.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashreeq): The three days following the Day of Nahr (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) during which the pilgrim stays in Mina and stones the jamarat.

B) At zawal (sun's decline)

D) Any time regardless of zawal

Key Takeaway
Stoning after zawal in order is wajib; staying in Mina is sunnah; both are integral to completing Hajj properly and avoiding penalties.

Spending Nights in Mina During Days of Tashriq
Ruling that it is sunnah to spend nights in Mina during Tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on spending the nights of Tashriq in Mina and identify the dalil that supports it.

Core Idea
Staying in Mina on the nights of Tashriq is a confirmed sunnah, proven by the Prophet's practice and Umar's instruction.

The days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) are a special time when pilgrims remain in Mina for stoning. But what about the nights? The Hanafi school teaches that spending these nights in Mina is a sunnah muakkadah based on clear evidence from the Prophet's own actions and the directive of Caliph Umar. In this lesson, we will examine the proofs and understand why this practice is emphasized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
What is the legal status of spending the nights of Tashriq in Mina according to the Hanafi school? Look for the explicit statement in the Urdu commentary stating it is sunnah.
The text says 'سنت ہے' (it is sunnah).
2
Examine the First Hadith
The passage cites a hadith from Abu Dawud (no. 1958) that the Prophet spent the night in Mina. Why does this support the ruling? The commentary explains that 'ظل' means he continued doing so, indicating persistence.
This shows the Prophet consistently stayed in Mina during these nights.
3
Examine the Second Hadith
The hadith from Aisha (Abu Dawud no. 1973) states: 'The Messenger of Allah departed on his last day when he prayed Dhuhr, then returned to Mina and stayed there during the nights of the days of Tashriq, stoning the jamrah.' Identify the key action and its timing.
The Prophet returned specifically for the nights and stayed for stoning.
4
Examine the Athar from Umar
Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'None of the pilgrims should spend the nights of Mina beyond al-Aqaba.' What does this imply about the obligation? The commentary notes that even if one goes into Makkah's boundaries, it is not proper to stay behind al-Aqaba.
Umar's command emphasizes staying within Mina proper.
5
Summarize the Proofs
Combine the three evidences: the Prophet's practice (fi'l), his continuous action (istimrar), and Umar's directive (qawl al-sahabi). Conclude why the Hanafi school considers this sunnah muakkadah.
The multiple proofs strengthen the sunnah status.

But the Messenger of Allah, except Allah, spent the night in Mina and stayed. (Abu Dawud, chapter twenty, nights of Mina, p.277 no.1958). In this hadith, it is mentioned that he spent the night, and the meaning of 'ظل' is 'he continued'. From this it is understood that spending the night in Mina on the 10th, 11th, and 12th (the days of Tashriq) is sunnah. (3) In this hadith: Aisha said: The Messenger of Allah departed on his last day when he prayed Dhuhr, then returned to Mina and stayed there during the nights of the days of Tashriq, stoning the jamrah. (Abu Dawud, chapter on stoning, p.220 no.1973). In this hadith, the Prophet stayed in Mina during the days of Tashriq. (4) In this athar: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: None of the pilgrims should spend the nights of Mina beyond al-Aqaba. (Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on no permission to stay in Makkah during nights of Mina, vol.5 p.249 no.9690). In this athar, even if one goes into the boundaries of Makkah, it is not proper to spend the nights of the days of Tashriq behind al-Aqaba, which is the valley of Mina.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that spending the nights of the days of Tashriq in Mina is a sunnah of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. The author presents three proofs: first, a hadith from Abu Dawud indicating that the Prophet spent the night in Mina; second, a hadith from Aisha that the Prophet returned to Mina after Dhuhr and stayed there during the nights of Tashriq, stoning the jamarat; third, an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab prohibiting pilgrims from spending these nights beyond al-Aqaba, which reinforces the obligation to stay within Mina. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the intended nights are the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah (i.e., the nights following the Day of Nahr). However, note that the 10th night is spent in Muzdalifah, so this likely refers to the nights of the 11th, 12th, and 13th (the days of Tashriq). The Hanafi position is that staying in Mina on these nights is sunnah muakkadah, and leaving it without excuse is makruh. The proofs are from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions.

Key Terms
ايام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the Day of Nahr (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) during which pilgrims stay in Mina and perform stoning.
منى (Mina): A valley near Makkah where pilgrims spend the days of Tashriq and perform the stoning ritual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Spending the nights of the days of Tashriq in Mina is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) established by the Prophet's action and Umar's directive, and omitting it without excuse is makruh tanzihi.

Procedure for Stoning on the 11th and 12th of Dhul Hijjah
Detailed ruling on the procedure for stoning the three jamarat on the 11th and 12th of Dhul Hijjah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stoning the jamarat on the 11th and 12th of Dhul Hijjah and explain the prescribed sequence, distinguishing between wajib and sunnah actions.

Core Idea
Stoning the jamarat is wajib, but the specific sequence and supplications are sunnah established by the Prophet's practice.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed procedure for stoning the three jamarat on the second and third days of al-Nahr (11th and 12th Dhul Hijjah). The passage describes the actions of the pilgrim after zawal, including walking, saying takbir, making lengthy supplication at the first two jamarat, and stoning the third without stopping. Understanding this sequence ensures that the wajib act of ramy is performed correctly and that sunnah elements are not neglected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time and days for stoning
Determine on which days stoning is performed: the 11th and 12th (and 13th if staying), after zawal. This sets the temporal condition for the wajib act.
Zawal marks the beginning of the time for Dhuhr prayer.
2
Distinguish between wajib and sunnah actions
The stoning of each jamrah with seven pebbles is wajib. The specific sequence (starting with the nearest, walking, takbir, standing for du'a, raising hands, riding for the third) is sunnah.
Hanafi school: stoning is wajib; Shafi'i considers it sunnah.
3
Understand the sequence for the first two jamarat
On the 11th, after stoning the first jamrah (near Masjid al-Khayf), he stands facing qiblah, raises hands, and makes long supplication. Then does the same for the second. Details of supplication include praising Allah, sending blessings, and seeking forgiveness.
The hadith of Ibn Umar describes standing for a long time.
4
Learn the ruling for Jamrat al-Aqaba
Stone the third jamrah while riding (to avoid crowd) and do not stand for du'a there. This is based on the Prophet's practice.
Riding is not obligatory but was done in crowded conditions.
5
Apply the proofs
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar in Bukhari, which narrates the Prophet's method. A secondary proof is Ibn Abbas's statement about raising hands in seven places, including at the jamarat.
Both proofs are ahad but accepted in practice.

Source Text

النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويرفع يديه في الدعاء ويستغفر لوالديه واخوانه المؤمنين (۱۳۷۱) ثم يرمى الثانية التي تليها مثل ذلك ويقف عندها داعيا ثم يرمي جمرة العقبة راكبا ولا يقف عندها (۱۳۷۲) فاذا كان اليوم الثالث من ايام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث بعد الشمـس كـل جـمـرة بسبع حصيات يكبر مع كل حصاة ويقف عند الاولى والثانية فيطيل القيام ويتضرع ويرمى الثالثة ولا يقف عندها (ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی رمی الجمارص ۴۲۰ نمبر ۱۹۷۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوسرے اور تیسرے اور چوتھے دن کی رمی زوال کے بعد کرے۔ اور ہر کنکری کے ساتھ تکبیر کہے اور پہلے اور دوسرے جمرے کے پاس کھڑے رہ کر دعا کرے اور تیسرے جمرے کے پاس کھڑا نہ رہے۔ لغت: اليوم الثاني من ايام النحر : يوم نحر کا دسرا دن گیارہویں ذی الحجہ ہوتا ہے۔ المسجد الخیف: مسجد خیف جمرہ اولی سے کافی پیچھے کی جانب تھوڑی اونچائی پر ہے۔ اس وقت یہ بہت بڑی مسجد بنادی گئی ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۷۱) پھر دوسرے جمرے کی اسی طرح رمی کرے جو پہلے سے ملا ہوا ہے، اور وہاں دعا کے لئے رکے، پھر آخری جمرے کی رمی کرے سوار ہو کر اور وہاں نہر کے۔ صله الله تشریح : پہلے جمرے کے بعد جو اس سے ملا ہوا دوسرا جمرہ ہے اس کی رمی کرے اور وہاں دعا کے لئے رکے، پھر آخری جمرے کی رمی سوار ہو کرے اور وہاں دعا کے لئے نہ رکے ، تا کہ بھیڑ نہ ہو جائے۔ وجه : (۱) دعا کی تفصیل اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر انه كان يرمي الجمرة الدنيا بسبع حصيات يكبر على اثـر كـل حـصـاة ثم يتقدم حتى يسهل فيقوم مستقبل القبلة فيقوم طويلا ويدعو و يرفع يديه ثم يرمى الوسطى ثم ياخذ ذات الشمال فيستهل ويقوم مستقبل القبلة فيقوم طويلا ويدعو ويرفع يديه ويقوم طويلا ثم يرمي جمرة ذات العقبة من بطن الوادى ولا يقف عندها ثم ينصرف ويقول هكذا رايت النبى الله يفعله ( بخاری شریف، باب اذار مى الجمر تین یقوم مستقبل القبلة ويسهل ، ص۲۸۲، نمبر ۱ ۱۷۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہاتھ اٹھائے اور لمبی دعا کرے۔ (۲) اس قول صحابی میں ہاتھ اٹھانے کا ذکر ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال : لا ترفع الأيدى الا في سبع مواطن : [ا] اذا قام الى الصلوة [۲] و اذا رأى البيت [۳] و على الصفا [۴] و المروة [۵] و في عرفات [٦] و في جمع [۷] و عند الجمار - (مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ، من کان یرفع یدیہ فی اول تكبيرة ثم لا يعود، ج اول، ص ۲۱۴، نمبر ۲۴۵۰ رسنن بیهقی ، باب رفع الیدین اذارأی البیت ، ج خامس ،ص ۱۱۷، نمبر ۹۲۱۰) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ جمرہ کے پاس ہاتھ اٹھائے ، اور دعا کرے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۷۲) پس جب ایام نحر کا تیسرا دن ہو تو زوال کے بعد تینوں جمرات کی اسی طرح رمی کرے۔ تشریح : یوم نحر کے تیسرے دن سے مراد ۲ ارذی الحجہ کا دن ہے اس دن بھی تینوں جمرات کی رمی کرے، اور پہلے اور دوسرے
When the sun has passed its zenith on the second day of the days of Nahr, he stones the three jamarat. He begins with the jamrah that adjoins Masjid al-Khayf, stoning it with seven pebbles while walking, saying takbir with each pebble. Then he stands at it supplicating as he pleases, praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, raising his hands in supplication, and seeking forgiveness for his parents and the believing men and women. (1371) Then he stones the second jamrah that follows it similarly, and stands at it supplicating. Then he stones Jamrat al-Aqaba while riding, and does not stand at it. (1372) When it is the third day of the days of Nahr, he stones the three jamarat after the sun (has passed its zenith), each jamrah with seven pebbles, saying takbir with each pebble, and stands at the first and second, lengthening the standing and humbly supplicating, and stones the third and does not stand at it. (Abu Dawud, chapter on stoning, p.420 no.1973) From this hadith it is understood that the stoning of the second, third, and fourth days is done after zawal, and with each pebble he says takbir, and stands at the first and second jamrah supplicating, and does not stand at the third. Lexicon: The second day of al-Nahr: the second day of Nahr is the 11th of Dhul Hijjah. Masjid al-Khayf: Masjid al-Khayf is located behind the first jamrah on a slight elevation; now it has been made into a very large mosque. Translation of (1371): Then he stones the second jamrah that adjoins the first similarly, and stops there for prayer, then stones the last jamrah while riding and does not stop there. ... Commentary: After the first jamrah, he stones the second jamrah that adjoins it and stops for prayer, then stones the last jamrah while riding and does not stop for prayer, to avoid crowding. Proof: (1) The detail of supplication is in this hadith: Ibn Umar used to stone the first jamrah with seven pebbles, saying takbir after each pebble, then he would move forward until level, then stand facing the qiblah for a long time, supplicating and raising his hands, then stone the middle jamrah, then go to the left and stand facing the qiblah for a long time, supplicating and raising his hands, then stone Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley and did not stand at it, then depart saying: 'Thus I saw the Prophet do it.' (Bukhari, chapter on when one stones the jamrah he stands facing qiblah, p.282 no.1175). In this hadith, he raises his hands and makes a long supplication. (2) In this saying of a Companion, raising hands is mentioned: Ibn Abbas said: Hands are not raised except in seven places: when standing for prayer, when seeing the House, on Safa, on Marwa, in Arafat, in Muzdalifah, and at the jamarat. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, volume 1, p.214 no.2450; Bayhaqi, volume 5, p.117 no.9210). In this saying of a Companion, he raises hands at the jamrah and supplicates. Translation of (1372): Then when it is the third day of the days of Nahr, he stones the three jamarat after zawal similarly. Commentary: The third day of Nahr means the 12th of Dhul Hijjah; on this day he also stones the three jamarat, and at the first and second...
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed procedure for stoning the jamarat on the 11th and 12th of Dhul Hijjah (the second and third days of al-Nahr). The author describes three sequential actions numbered (1370), (1371), and (1372). On the 11th (second day), after zawal, the pilgrim stones all three jamarat starting with the one near Masjid al-Khayf, walking, saying takbir, and then making lengthy du'a with raised hands at the first jamrah, seeking forgiveness for himself, his parents, and all believers. Then he stones the second jamrah similarly and stands for du'a. Finally, he stones Jamrat al-Aqaba while riding (to avoid crowd) and does not stand for du'a there. On the 12th (third day), the same procedure is repeated: stone all three after zawal, stand at the first two for extended supplication, and do not stand at the third. The proofs include a hadith from Bukhari detailing Ibn Umar's practice, and a statement of Ibn Abbas listing the seven places where hands are raised in supplication, which includes at the jamarat. The Hanafi school holds that stoning the jamarat is wajib, and these specific actions (walking, saying takbir, standing for du'a at the first two) are sunnah. The ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet and his Companions.

Key Terms
رمي الجمار (ramy al-jimar): The act of throwing pebbles at the three stone pillars (jamarat) in Mina during the days of Tashriq.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-aqaba): The largest jamrah, located near the end of Mina, stoned on the Day of Nahr and the following days.
زوال (zawal): The passage of the sun from its zenith, i.e., the beginning of the time for Dhuhr prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On the 11th of Dhul Hijjah, after stoning the first jamrah, what must the pilgrim do?
A) Immediately stone the second jamrah without stopping
B) Stand and make lengthy supplication with raised hands
C) Walk quickly away to avoid the crowd
D) Proceed to stone Jamrat al-Aqaba on foot

Key Takeaway
Stoning the jamarat on 11th and 12th Dhul Hijjah is wajib, performed after zawal, with sunnah actions of walking, takbir, and extended supplication at the first two jamarat, but not at Jamrat al-Aqaba.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
12 min
Sequence and Timing of Ramy al-Jimar
Detail of sequence and timing of ramy al-jimar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of stoning each jamarah, including the option of ta'ajjul, and identify the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Stoning must be after zawal on 11th–13th; standing for supplication at first two jamarat is sunnah, not at third.

Stoning the jamarat is a wajib act of Hajj with specific timings and actions. This lesson walks through the sequence from the second jamarah onward, the ruling on timings after zawal, and the option to leave Mina early. The Hanafi position is supported by multiple hadith from Bukhari, Abu Dawud, and Bayhaqi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Stoning each jamarah is wajib. The text details the order: first, second, then third (Jamarat al-Aqabah).
Stoning is wajib, not fard, in Hanafi school.
2
Locate the timing evidence
The hadith specify: on the 10th, stoning is in the forenoon; on subsequent days, after zawal. Find the specific hadith cited: Jabir (Bukhari) and Aisha (Abu Dawud).
Zawal = midday when Dhuhr time begins.
3
Analyze the actions at each jamarah
At the first and second jamarah, the pilgrim stands long, faces qibla, raises hands, and supplicates. At the third, he does not stand (to avoid crowding).
This is based on Ibn Umar's practice (Bukhari).
4
Understand ta'ajjul (hastening departure)
If one wishes to leave Mina on the 12th, he must depart before sunset. If sunset catches him, it is makruh but no penalty; if Fajr of 13th rises, stoning becomes wajib.
Evidence from Quran 2:203 and hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'mar.
5
Note the ikhtilaf with other schools
Some Shafi'i scholars allow stoning before zawal on 12th/13th. Hanafi insists after zawal (except 10th). The thamarah al-khilaf is timing flexibility.
Hanafi relies on explicit hadith practice.

(مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ، من کان یرفع یدیہ فی اول تكبيرة ثم لا يعود، ج اول، ص ۲۱۴، نمبر ۲۴۵۰ رسنن بیهقی ، باب رفع الیدین اذارأی البیت ، ج خامس ،ص ۱۱۷، نمبر ۹۲۱۰) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ جمرہ کے پاس ہاتھ اٹھائے ، اور دعا کرے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۷۲) پس جب ایام نحر کا تیسرا دن ہو تو زوال کے بعد تینوں جمرات کی اسی طرح رمی کرے۔ تشریح : یوم نحر کے تیسرے دن سے مراد ۲ ارذی الحجہ کا دن ہے اس دن بھی تینوں جمرات کی رمی کرے، اور پہلے اور دوسرے الزوال کذلک (۱۳۷۳) واذا اراد ان يتعجّل نفر الى مكة قبل غروب الشمس وان اقام الى جمرات کے بعد ر کے اور دعا کرے اور تیسرے جمرہ کے بعد نہ رکے تا کہ بھیڑ نہ ہو۔ وجه (۱) اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ و قال جابر : رمى النبي الله يوم النحر ضحی و رمی بعد ذالک بعد الزوال - ( بخاری شریف ، باب رمی الجمار، ص ۲۳۵ نمبر ۱۷۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کے بعد زوال کے بعد رمی صلى الله کرے۔(۲) عن عائشة قالت افاض رسول الله له من آخر يومه حين صلى الظهر ثم رجع الى منى فـمـكـث بـهـا لـيـالـي ايام التشريق يرمي الجمرة اذا زالت الشمس كل جمرة بسبع حصيات يكبر مع كل حصاة ويقف عند الاولى والثانية فيطيل القيام ويتضرع ويرمى الثالثة ولا يقف عندها (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في رمی الجمار، ص ۴۲۰، نمبر ۱۹۷۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گیارہویں اور بارہوں کو زوال شمس کے بعد رمی کرے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۷۳) اور ( چوتھے دن کی رمی کے بغیر ) مکہ جانے کا ارادہ ہو تو غروب شمس سے پہلے ہی نکل جائے ، اگر غروب ہو جائے تو مکروہ ہے مگر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں۔ اور چوتھے دن منی ہی میں فجر طلوع ہو جائے تو (اس دن کی ) رمی لازم ہے۔ تشریح : اگر تین دن تک یعنی بارہویں تاریخ تک رمی جمار کر کے منی سے مکہ مکرمہ جانا چاہے تو جاسکتا ہے اور اگر بارہویں تاریخ کو مغرب ہوگئی تو اب بغیر رمی کے مکہ مکرمہ جانا مکروہ ہے لیکن اگر چلا گیا تو کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا لیکن اگر فجر طلوع ہو گیا تو اب تینوں جمرات کی رمی کر کے جائے۔ وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ واذكروا الله في ايام معدودات فمن تعجل في يومين فلا اثم عليه ومن تأخر فلا اثم عليه لمن اتقى ( آیت ۲۰۳ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو دن یعنی بارہویں تاریخ کو مکہ مکرمہ آئے تب بھی کوئی بات نہیں ہے، اور اگر اس کے بعد آئے تب بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الرحمن يعمر الديلي صلى الله قال اتيت النبي علة هو بعرفة ... ايام منى ثلثة فمن تعجل فى يومين فلا اثم عليه ومن تأخر فلا اثم عليه (ابو داؤد شریف، باب من لم یدرک عرفته ،ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۹۴۹) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ منی میں ٹھہرنے کے تین دن ہیں۔ لیکن دو دن میں بھی یعنی گیار ہوں اور بارہویں دن رمی جمار کر کے واپس آسکتا ہے (۳) اثر میں ہے۔عــن ابـن عـمـر كـان يقول من للبيهقى ، باب غربت عليه الشمس وهو بمنى اوسط ايام التشريق فلا ينفرن حتى يرمي الجمار من الغد. (سنن من غربت له الشمس يوم النفر الاول بمعنی حتی برمی الجمار يوم الثالث بعد الزوال، ج خامس ، ص ۲۴۸، نمبر ۶ ۹۶۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بارہویں کے بعد جو شام آتی ہے یعنی تیرہویں کی شام منی میں ہو جائے تو منی سے نہ جائے بلکہ وہاں ٹھہر جائے اور تیر ہوئیں کو رمی کر کے جائے ۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۷۴) اور ( چوتھے دن ) زوال سے پہلے بھی رمی کرنا جائز ہے مگر افضل زوال کے بعد ہے، اور آفتاب طلوع
Section: Structure of Hajj actions. (1371) Then he stones the second (jamarah) that is next to it similarly, and stands at it supplicating. Then he stones Jamarat al-Aqabah while riding and does not stand at it. (1372) When it is the third day of the days of sacrifice (al-Nahr), he stones the three jamarat after the sun [i.e., after zawal], each jamarah with seven pebbles, saying takbir with each pebble, and stands at the first and second, prolonging the standing and supplicating humbly, and stones the third and does not stand at it. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Ramy al-Jimar, p. 420, no. 1973) From this hadith it is learned that the stoning of the second, third, and fourth days is after zawal. And with each pebble he says takbir, and stands at the first and second jamarah supplicating, and does not stand at the third jamarah. Vocabulary: al-yawm al-thani min ayyam al-nahr: the second day of the day of sacrifice is the 11th of Dhul-Hijjah. Al-Masjid al-Khayf: Masjid Khayf is behind the first jamarah at a slight elevation. Now it has been made into a very large mosque. Translation: (1371) Then he stones the second jamarah that is adjacent to the first in the same manner, and stops there for supplication. Then he stones the last jamarah while riding and does not stop there. (salla Allah) Explanation: After the first jamarah, he stones the second jamarah that is adjacent to it and stops there for supplication. Then he stones the last jamarah while riding and does not stop there for supplication, so that there is no crowding. Proof: (1) The detail of the supplication is in this hadith: From Ibn Umar that he used to stone the first jamarah with seven pebbles, saying takbir after each pebble, then he would advance until he was on level ground, then stand facing the qibla, stand for a long time and supplicate and raise his hands. Then he would stone the middle (jamarah), then take the left side and stand on level ground, facing the qibla, stand for a long time and supplicate and raise his hands and stand for a long time. Then he would stone Jamarat Dhat al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley and not stand at it. Then he would depart and say, 'Thus I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) do.' (Bukhari, Bab Idha Rama al-Jimar al-Thalath, p. 282, no. 1175) In this hadith, (it mentions) raising hands and long supplication. (2) In this Companion's statement, raising hands is mentioned: From Ibn Abbas, he said: 'Do not raise hands except in seven places: [1] when standing for prayer, [2] when seeing the House (Ka'bah), [3] at Safa, [4] and Marwah, [5] at Arafat, [6] at Muzdalifah, [7] and at the jamarat.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Chapter on raising hands in the first takbir then not returning, vol. 1, p. 214, no. 2450; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on raising hands when seeing the House, vol. 5, p. 117, no. 9210) In this Companion's statement, (it mentions) raising hands at the jamarah and supplicating. Translation: (1372) So when it is the third day of the days of sacrifice, he stones the three jamarat after zawal in the same manner. Explanation: By the third day of the day of sacrifice is meant the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah. On this day also he stones the three jamarat, and after the first and second (jamarat) he stands and supplicates, and after the third jamarah he does not stand to avoid crowding. Proof: (1) The hadith for this: Jabir said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) stoned on the day of sacrifice in the forenoon, and after that he stoned after zawal.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Ramy al-Jimar, p. 235, no. 1746) In this hadith, (it mentions) stoning after zawal after the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah. (2) From Aisha, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) departed from (the final tawaf) on the last day of his stay after he prayed Dhuhr, then returned to Mina and stayed there the nights of the days of tashriq, stoning the jamarah when the sun passed the meridian, each jamarah with seven pebbles, saying takbir with each pebble, and standing at the first and second, prolonging the standing and supplicating humbly, and stoning the third and not standing at it.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Stoning the Jamarat, p. 420, no. 1973) In this hadith, (it mentions) stoning on the 11th and 12th after zawal. Translation: (1373) And if he wants to hasten (leave early), he should depart to Makkah before sunset. If he stays until sunset, it is disliked (makruh) but nothing is obligatory. And if Fajr rises on the fourth day while he is in Mina, the stoning (of that day) becomes obligatory. Explanation: If he has stoned for three days, i.e., until the 12th, and wants to go from Mina to Makkah, he may go. If Maghrib of the 12th occurs, then going to Makkah without stoning is disliked, but if he goes, nothing is obligatory. But if Fajr rises, he must stone all three jamarat before going. Proof: (1) In the verse: 'And mention Allah during the appointed days. But whoever hastens in two days, there is no sin upon him, and whoever delays, there is no sin upon him, for him who fears Allah.' (Quran 2:203) From this verse it is learned that coming to Makkah on the second day (12th) is fine, and coming after that is also fine. (2) In the hadith: From Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'mar al-Dayli, he said: 'I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he was at Arafah... The days of Mina are three: whoever hastens in two days, there is no sin upon him, and whoever delays, there is no sin upon him.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter: Whoever does not catch Arafah, p. 285, no. 1949) From this hadith it is also learned that staying in Mina is three days. But it is also possible to return after two days, i.e., after stoning on the 11th and 12th. (3) In the athar: From Ibn Umar, he used to say: 'Whoever the sun sets upon while he is in Mina on the middle of the days of tashriq (i.e., the 12th), he should not depart until he stones the jamarat the next day.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter: From whose sun set on the day of first departure, meaning he must stone on the third day after zawal, vol. 5, p. 248, no. 6968) From this athar it is learned that if the evening after the 12th (i.e., the evening of the 13th) finds him in Mina, he should not leave but stay and stone on the 13th and then leave. Translation: (1374) And on the fourth day, stoning before zawal is permissible, but the best is after zawal, and after sunrise...
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the stoning of the jamarat during Hajj, supported by hadith proofs. It covers the sequence, timing, and actions at each jamarah. The author begins by stating the ruling: after stoning the first jamarah, the pilgrim stones the second similarly and stands for supplication, then stones Jamarat al-Aqabah while riding without stopping (section 1371). On the third day of al-Nahr (i.e., 12th Dhul-Hijjah), he stones all three jamarat after zawal (midday), with seven pebbles each, saying takbir, standing long at the first two for supplication, and not standing at the third (1372). The commentary explains that the second day of al-Nahr is the 11th, and the third is the 12th. The hadith from Ibn Umar is cited to show the practice of raising hands and prolonged supplication. A statement from Ibn Abbas lists seven places where hands are raised, including the jamarat. Then the passage addresses the option to hasten (ta'ajjul): if one wants to leave Mina early, he must depart Makkah before sunset on the 12th; if sunset catches him, it is makruh but nothing is wajib; if Fajr of the 13th rises while he is in Mina, stoning becomes obligatory (1373). The commentary cites Quran 2:203 and the hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'mar to show the three-day stay and permission to hasten in two days. An athar from Ibn Umar indicates that if one is still in Mina at sunset of the 12th (i.e., entering the 13th), he must stay and stone on the 13th. Finally, the passage notes that on the fourth day (the 13th), stoning before zawal is permissible but better after zawal (1374). The entire ruling aligns with the Hanafi school, emphasizing the order, timing after zawal, and the distinction of not standing at the third jamarah to avoid crowding.

Key Terms
رمي الجمار (ramy al-jimar): The act of throwing pebbles at the three stone pillars (jamarat) in Mina during Hajj.
جمرة العقبة (jamarat al-aqabah): The largest pillar (also called al-jamrat al-kubra) located near the 'Aqabah, which is stoned on the 10th and subsequent days.
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes the meridian, i.e., midday, after which Dhuhr time begins.
ايام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The three days following Hari (10th Dhul-Hijjah): the 11th, 12th, and 13th.
تعجل (ta'ajjul): To hasten departure from Mina, i.e., to leave on the 12th after stoning instead of staying for the 13th.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a pilgrim on the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah does not depart Mina before sunset?
A) He must slaughter a dam (sacrifice).
B) It is makruh, but nothing obligatory; if fajr rises, he must stay and stone on the 13th.
C) His Hajj becomes invalid.
D) He must return to Makkah immediately without stoning.

Key Takeaway
Stoning the jamarat on the 11th–13th must be after zawal, except the 13th where before zawal is permissible; standing at the first two jamarat for supplication is sunnah, not wajib.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Departure from Mina on the 12th and Ramy on the 4th Day
Ruling on departure from Mina on 12th with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a pilgrim who remains in Mina after sunset on the 12th and after Fajr on the 13th, and cite the proofs from Quran, Hadith, and Athar.

Core Idea
Leaving Mina after sunset on the 12th is makruh but no penalty; but if Fajr comes, ramy becomes wajib.

This lesson covers the rulings concerning a pilgrim's departure from Mina on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah. You will learn when early departure is allowed, whether staying past sunset incurs a penalty, and what happens if dawn on the 13th finds you still in Mina. The lesson also presents the textual proofs that establish these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is departure from Mina on the 12th. The ruling: permissible if before sunset, makruh tanzihi if after sunset but before Fajr. If Fajr of 13th occurs while in Mina, ramy of all three jamarat becomes wajib.
The ruling distinguishes between makruh (no penalty) and wajib (required).
2
Locate the dalil
Three proofs are cited: Quran 2:203 (permission for early departure), Hadith of Abd al-Rahman Ya'mur (days of Mina are three), and Athar of Ibn Umar (sunset on 12th necessitates stoning next day).
The Quran establishes permissibility; the Athar imposes the condition for wajib.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic phrase 'man ta'ajjala fi yawmayn' indicates no sin for early departure. The Athar explicitly states that if sunset overtakes you on the middle day, you must stone the next day, making ramy wajib.
The Hanafi school gives the Athar a clear legal implication for the wajib ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may not consider post-sunset departure makruh or may require a penalty. The Hanafi position relies on the Athar and the absence of a penalty in the primary sources.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi tarjih is based on the strength of the evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts the view that staying after sunset is makruh but not sinful, and that Fajr on 13th triggers wajib ramy. This is based on the combination of the Quranic permissibility and the Athar's specific condition.
The mufta bihi position is as stated in the text.

الزوال کذلک (۱۳۷۳) واذا اراد ان يتعجّل نفر الى مكة قبل غروب الشمس وان اقام الى جمرات کے بعد ر کے اور دعا کرے اور تیسرے جمرہ کے بعد نہ رکے تا کہ بھیڑ نہ ہو۔ وجه (۱) اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ و قال جابر : رمى النبي الله يوم النحر ضحی و رمی بعد ذالک بعد الزوال - ( بخاری شریف ، باب رمی الجمار، ص ۲۳۵ نمبر ۱۷۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کے بعد زوال کے بعد رمی کرے۔(۲) عن عائشة قالت افاض رسول الله له من آخر يومه حين صلى الظهر ثم رجع الى منى فـمـكـث بـهـا لـيـالـي ايام التشريق يرمي الجمرة اذا زالت الشمس كل جمرة بسبع حصيات يكبر مع كل حصاة ويقف عند الاولى والثانية فيطيل القيام ويتضرع ويرمى الثالثة ولا يقف عندها (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في رمی الجمار، ص ۴۲۰، نمبر ۱۹۷۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گیارہویں اور بارہوں کو زوال شمس کے بعد رمی کرے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۷۳) اور ( چوتھے دن کی رمی کے بغیر ) مکہ جانے کا ارادہ ہو تو غروب شمس سے پہلے ہی نکل جائے ، اگر غروب ہو جائے تو مکروہ ہے مگر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں۔ اور چوتھے دن منی ہی میں فجر طلوع ہو جائے تو (اس دن کی ) رمی لازم ہے۔ تشریح : اگر تین دن تک یعنی بارہویں تاریخ تک رمی جمار کر کے منی سے مکہ مکرمہ جانا چاہے تو جاسکتا ہے اور اگر بارہویں تاریخ کو مغرب ہوگئی تو اب بغیر رمی کے مکہ مکرمہ جانا مکروہ ہے لیکن اگر چلا گیا تو کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا لیکن اگر فجر طلوع ہو گیا تو اب تینوں جمرات کی رمی کر کے جائے۔ وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ واذكروا الله في ايام معدودات فمن تعجل في يومين فلا اثم عليه ومن تأخر فلا اثم عليه لمن اتقى ( آیت ۲۰۳ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو دن یعنی بارہویں تاریخ کو مکہ مکرمہ آئے تب بھی کوئی بات نہیں ہے، اور اگر اس کے بعد آئے تب بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الرحمن يعمر الديلي قال اتيت النبي علة هو بعرفة ... ايام منى ثلثة فمن تعجل فى يومين فلا اثم عليه ومن تأخر فلا اثم عليه (ابو داؤد شریف، باب من لم یدرک عرفته ،ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۹۴۹) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ منی میں ٹھہرنے کے تین دن ہیں۔ لیکن دو دن میں بھی یعنی گیار ہوں اور بارہویں دن رمی جمار کر کے واپس آسکتا ہے (۳) اثر میں ہے۔عــن ابـن عـمـر كـان يقول من للبيهقى ، باب من غربت عليه الشمس وهو بمنى اوسط ايام التشريق فلا ينفرن حتى يرمي الجمار من الغد. (سنن من غربت له الشمس يوم النفر الاول بمعنی حتی برمی الجمار يوم الثالث بعد الزوال، ج خامس ، ص ۲۴۸، نمبر ۶ ۹۶۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بارہویں کے بعد جو شام آتی ہے یعنی تیرہویں کی شام منی میں ہو جائے تو منی سے نہ جائے بلکہ وہاں ٹھہر جائے اور تیر ہوئیں کو رمی کر کے جائے ۔
And if he wants to hasten, he should depart to Mecca before sunset. And if he stays until sunset, it is disliked but nothing is obligatory upon him. And if dawn appears while he is in Mina on the fourth day, then ramy becomes necessary. Explanation: If he has done ramy for three days until the 12th, he may go to Mecca. If sunset occurs on the 12th, it is disliked to go without ramy, but if he goes nothing is obligatory. If dawn appears, he must do ramy of all three jamarat. Proofs: (1) Quran: 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days. And whoever hastens [his departure] in two days, there is no sin upon him; and whoever delays [until the third] there is no sin upon him for those who fear Allah.' (2) Hadith from Abdur Rahman Ya'mur: 'The days of Mina are three; whoever hastens in two days, no sin; whoever delays, no sin.' (3) Athar from Ibn Umar: 'Whoever has the sun set on him while he is in Mina on the middle days of Tashriq should not leave until he has stoned the jamarat the next day.'
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This lesson presents the ruling regarding leaving Mina after the days of Tashriq. The passage begins by stating a ruling (hukm) from the matn: if a pilgrim wants to depart early (ta'ajjul) on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah, he may go to Mecca before sunset. If he stays until sunset, it is makruh (disliked) but no fidyah is required. However, if he stays until Fajr of the 13th, he must perform ramy of all three jamarat that day. The commentator then provides proofs: (1) A Hadith from Jabir that the Prophet stoned after zawal on the 10th and the following days. (2) A Hadith from Aisha detailing the Prophet’s actions in Mina. The Urdu translation and explanation (tashrih) clarify the practical application: leaving after sunset is makruh but not sinful; if Fajr comes, ramy becomes wajib. The proofs include a Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:203) allowing early departure in two days, a Hadith confirming the days of Mina are three, and an athar from Ibn Umar that one overtaken by sunset on the 12th must stay and stone the next day. This establishes the Hanafi position that the 13th is not an obligatory day of stay unless one is caught by sunset on the 12th.

Key Terms
نفر (nafar): Departure from Mina after the days of Tashriq.
رمي (ramy): Stoning of the jamarat (pillars) with pebbles.
ايام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, days of stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a pilgrim remains in Mina until Fajr on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah, what must he do?
A) He may leave without any additional acts.
B) He must perform ramy of all three jamarat.
C) He must sacrifice an animal.
D) He must stay until the 14th.

Key Takeaway
Leaving Mina after sunset on the 12th is makruh but not sinful; however, if Fajr of the 13th catches you, ramy becomes wajib.

Ruling on Timing of Ramy on the 13th Dhul Hijjah
Ruling with proof for ramy timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of ramy on 13th Dhul Hijjah and explain the preferred time based on the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Ramy before zawal on 13th is permissible but better after; before sunrise is disliked.

This lesson focuses on the timing of ramy (stoning) on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah, the last day of Tashriq. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet, provides a flexible ruling that balances permissibility and preference. Understanding this ruling helps pilgrims fulfill the rites correctly while avoiding disliked times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
Recognize that ramy on the 13th is a wajib act of Hajj within a specific time window. The ruling here addresses the permissibility of performing it before, at, or after certain times of the day.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on timing
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, ramy before zawal (noon) is permissible (ja'iz), but the preferred (afdal) time is after zawal. Stoning before sunrise is disliked (makruh).
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The proof (wajh) is the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet performed ramy after zawal on the Days of Tashriq. This indicates that after zawal is the sunnah practice, but it does not prohibit before zawal.
Hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that ramy on the 13th must be after zawal. The Hanafi school allows before zawal, citing that the hadith shows preference, not obligation.
This ikhtilaf affects when a pilgrim may ston before returning.
5
Apply the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that ramy before zawal is permissible but makruh before sunrise. Pilgrims should aim for after zawal to follow the best practice.
No fidyah is required for stoning before sunrise, but it is makruh tanzihi.

Source Text

Commentary
This lesson addresses the timing of ramy (stoning) on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah (the fourth day). The Urdu translation states that ramy before zawal (noon) is permissible, but the afdal (preferred) time is after zawal. It is makruh (disliked) to perform ramy before sunrise. The Hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud.

افضل (afdal): Better; recommended but not obligatory.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; blameworthy but not sinful enough to require penalty.

Ruling on Walking or Riding During Ramy
Ruling on walking vs riding during ramy, with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on walking vs riding during ramy and explain the evidence from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Walk for ramy where dua follows; ride for ramy without subsequent dua.

The manner of stoning (ramy) during Hajj includes a distinction between the first two jamarat and the third. The Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice, recommends walking for the jamarat where prolonged supplication is sunnah, and permits riding for the others. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ramy
Separate ramy that is followed by another ramy on the same day (first two jamarat on 11th-13th) from ramy that is not (jamrat al-aqaba on 10th, and the third jamarat on each day).
2
State the ruling for each type
For ramy with subsequent ramy: walk to enable dua afterwards. For ramy without: ride to leave without dua.
Riding is permissible for the third jamarat; walking is mustahabb for the first two.
3
Understand the wisdom
Walking facilitates extended standing and heartfelt supplication after stoning, which is a sunnah for the first two jamarat.
The Prophet stood and made long dua after the first and second jamarat.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith from Aisha (RA) in Sunan Abi Dawud describes the Prophet's practice: he stopped after the first and second jamarat for supplication, but not after the third.
Hadith reference: Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 1973.
5
Apply the Hanafi position
Walking is mustahabb (preferred) for the first two jamarat; riding is allowed but less virtuous. For jamrat al-aqaba and the third jamarat, riding is permitted and walking is not required.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۷۵) ہر وہ رمی جس کے بعد رمی ہے اس کی رمی چل کر کرے تا کہ اس کے بعد دعا کر سکے، ورنہ تو سوار ہو کر کرے تا کہ اس کے بعد بغیر دعا کے جاسکے۔ تشریح : دسویں تاریخ کو صرف جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرنی ہے اور اس کے بعد ٹھہرنا بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے سوار ہو کر رمی کرے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، اور دوسرے دن اور تیسرے دن اور چوتھے دن تینوں جمروں کی رمی کرنی ہے اس لئے اس میں بہتر یہ ہے کہ چل کر رمی کرتے جائے کیونکہ پہلی رمی اور دوسری رمی کے بعد ٹھہر کر دعا کرنی ہے اور دیر تک گڑ گڑا کر دعا کرنا چل کر آسان ہوگا کیونکہ سواری تو بھاگنے کی کوشش کرے گی اس لئے اس میں چل کر رمی کرنا افضل ہے۔ آج کل اتنی بھیٹر ہوتی ہے کہ سوار پر رمی کرنا مشکل ہے۔ وجه : (ا) عن عائشة قالت افاض رسول الله الله من آخر يومه حين صلى الظهر ثم رجع الى منى فمكث بها ليالي ايام التشريق يرمى الجمرة اذا زالت الشمس كل جمرة بسبع حصيات يكبر مع كل حصاة ويقف عند الاولى والثانية فيطيل القيام ويتضرع ويرمى الثالثة ولا يقف عندها (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی رمی الجمار، ص ۴۲۰، نمبر ۱۹۷۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گیارہویں اور بارہویں کو پہلی اور دوسری رمی چل کر کرے اور دعا کرے اور تیسری رمی کے بعد کھڑا نہ ہو۔ و کل رمی بعده رمى ترميه ماشيا لتدعو بعده والا راكبا لتذهب عقبه بلا دعاء (۱۳۷۶)
Translation of (1375): Every ramy after which there is another ramy, do it walking so that you can make dua afterwards; otherwise do it riding so that you can go away without dua. Explanation: On the 10th, only jamrat al-aqaba is stoned and there is no staying afterwards, so riding is no problem. On the second, third, and fourth days, three jamarat are stoned, so it is better to walk because you need to stand and make dua after the first and second, and walking makes it easier for prolonged dua. Today, overcrowding makes riding difficult. Proof: Hadith from Aisha: ... 'He used to stand at the first and second and make long supplication, and stone the third without standing.' So on the 11th and 12th, walk for first two and make dua, and for the third do not stand. Arabic matn: 'And every ramy after which there is ramy: stone it walking to make dua afterwards; otherwise riding to go away without dua (1376).'
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This lesson explains the manner of performing the ramy (stoning). The ruling distinguishes between two types: (1) ramy that is followed by another ramy on the same day (i.e., the first and second jamarat on the 11th, 12th, and 13th) – for these, one should walk to the jamarat and after stoning, stand and make prolonged dua. (2) ramy that is not followed by another ramy (i.e., jamrat al-aqaba on the 10th, and the third jamarat on the 11th-13th) – for these, one may ride and is not required to make dua afterwards. The commentary explains the wisdom: walking facilitates extended supplication. The proof is a Hadith from Aisha describing the Prophet's practice: he would stand and make dua after the first and second jamarat, but not after the third. The Arabic matn from the running text (1376) is included: 'و کل رمی بعده رمى ترميه ماشيا لتدعو بعده والا راكبا لتذهب عقبه بلا دعاء' – every ramy that is followed by another, stone walking to make dua; otherwise ride to go without dua.

Key Terms
جمرة عقبہ (jamrat al-aqaba): The large pillar near al-Aqaba, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
دعا (du'a): Supplication after stoning the first two jamarat, performed while standing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because riding is forbidden on those days.
B) Because one should make dua after them, and walking makes it easier.
C) Because all ramy must be done on foot.
D) Because the Prophet always walked.

Key Takeaway
Walk for the first two jamarat to fulfill the sunnah of dua; riding is permissible for the third and for jamrat al-aqaba.

Ruling on Staying Overnight Outside Mina During Ramy Nights
Ruling that spending nights outside Mina is makruh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on spending the nights of ramy outside Mina and cite the hadith proof from Aisha (RA).

Core Idea
Spending the nights of ramy outside Mina is makruh tanzihi, based on the Prophet's practice.

During Hajj, the days of Tashriq involve stoning the jamarat. The question arises: where should the pilgrim stay overnight? This lesson addresses the ruling based on the Prophet's practice (sunnah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is spending the nights of the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah (the nights of ramy) outside Mina. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
The Hanafi school classifies this as makruh tanzihi.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Aisha (RA) narrated in Sunan Abi Dawud, stating that the Prophet (PBUH) performed ifadah, returned to Mina, and stayed there during the nights of Tashriq.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), hence the ruling is not wajib.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's staying (mabit) in Mina during those nights establishes a sunnah. Leaving it without valid reason is makruh.
The Hanafi principle: al-fil al-nabawi yufidu al-sunnah (the Prophet's action indicates sunnah).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider staying in Mina as wajib, but the Hanafi school considers it sunnah, so leaving it is only makruh and does not invalidate Hajj.
The practical consequence: no fidyah required in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۷۶) اور رمی کی راتوں میں منی کے علاوہ ( دوسری جگہ ) رات گذارنا مکروہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن عائشة قالت افاض رسول الله له من آخر يومه حين صلى الظهر ثم رجع الى منى فمكث بها ليالى ايام التشريق يرمى الجمرة (ابوداؤ د شریف ، باب فی رمی الجمارص ۴۲۰ نمبر ۱۹۷۳) اس وكره المبيت بغیر منى ليالي الرمی (۱۳۷۷)

Proof: (1) In this hadith: from Aisha, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah performed ifadah from the last day after praying Zuhr, then returned to Mina and stayed there the nights of the days of Tashriq, stoning the jamrat.' (Sunan Abi Dawud). Arabic matn: 'And it is disliked to spend the night outside Mina during the nights of ramy (1377).'
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This lesson discusses the rule regarding where to stay overnight during the days of Tashriq. The ruling states that it is makruh (disliked) to spend the nights (i.e., the nights of the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah) outside of Mina. The proof is a hadith from Aisha that the Prophet stayed in Mina during those nights. The Arabic matn from the running text (1377) is included: 'وكره المبيت بغیر منى ليالي الرمی'. The reasoning is that the Prophet's practice was to stay in Mina, so deviating from it is disliked. The commentary does not explicitly state a penalty, but the ruling is makruh tanzihi according to the Hanafi school, meaning it is blameworthy but not sinful enough to require a sacrifice (dam).

Key Terms
مبيت (mabit): Spending the night; staying overnight in a place.
ليالي الرمي (layali al-ramy): The nights of the days of ramy: the nights of the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Ruling on Tawaf al-Wada' and Its Two Rak'ahs
States ruling with proof and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib, identify its proof, and apply the exception for residents of Makkah.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib on all pilgrims except Makkans; omitting it requires a dam.

This passage clarifies the obligation of Tawaf al-Wada' (Farewell Tawaf) and the accompanying two rak'ahs. The Hanafi school ranks this as wajib, not fard, due to the nature of the evidence. Understanding this ruling is crucial for performing Hajj correctly and avoiding penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib for pilgrims leaving Makkah.
Wajib in Hanafi is a binding duty established by zanni evidence.
2
Note the exception
The ruling excludes people of Makkah and those who reside there.
Residents are not required to perform a farewell tawaf.
3
Identify the associated obligation
After this tawaf, one must pray two rak'ahs.
This is also wajib according to the text.
4
Locate the proof
The evidence is a hadith from Bukhari where al-Zuhri states the Prophet always prayed two rak'ahs after tawaf.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
5
Understand the evidentiary weight
Hanafi usul treats the Prophet's constant practice without omission as an indicator of obligation (wujub). Since the hadith is zanni, the ruling is wajib not fard.
This distinction affects the consequence of omission: compensation (dam) not invalidation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسعى ان قدمهما وهذا طواف الوداع ويسمى ايضا طواف الصدر وهذا واجب الا على اهل مكة ومن اقام بها (۱۳۷۹) ويصلي بعده الركعتين (۱۳۸۰) تشریح : طواف وداع کے بعد اسی طرح طواف قدوم کے بعد دو رکعت نماز پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے ۔ قلت للزهرى ان عطاء يقول تجزئه المكتوبة من ركعتي الطواف فقال السنة افضل لم يطف النبي الالا لاله اسبوعا قط الاصلی رکعتین بخاری شریف، باب طاف النبي ما وصلى السبوع رکعتین ص ۲۲۰، نمبر ۱۶۲۳) اس حدیث مرسل میں ہے کہ جب جب طواف کیا تو دورکعت نماز پڑھی۔
And Sa'i, if he performed it before it, and this is Tawaf al-Wada', also called Tawaf al-Sadr, and this is wajib except for the people of Makkah and those who reside there (1379). And he prays two rak'ahs after it (1380). Explanation: After Tawaf al-Wada', similarly after Tawaf al-Qudum, he should pray two rak'ahs. Evidence: (1) The hadith is: I said to al-Zuhri, 'Indeed Ata' says that the obligatory prayer suffices for the two rak'ahs of tawaf,' so he said, 'The Sunnah is better. The Prophet never performed a tawaf except that he prayed two rak'ahs.' (Bukhari, chapter: The Prophet performed tawaf and prayed two rak'ahs after seven circuits, p.220, no.1623) This mursal hadith states that whenever he performed tawaf, he prayed two rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on Tawaf al-Wada' (Farewell Tawaf) and the obligation of praying two rak'ahs after it. It begins by stating that if one performed Sa'i before Tawaf, then this is Tawaf al-Wada', also called Tawaf al-Sadr, and it is wajib for all pilgrims except the people of Makkah and those who have taken up residence there. The Hanafi school distinguishes 'wajib' from 'fard'; 'wajib' here indicates a binding duty established by a zanni proof. After performing this tawaf, one must pray two rak'ahs. The commentary explains that this two-rak'ah prayer is also performed after Tawaf al-Qudum (Arrival Tawaf). The proof is a hadith from Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri, where he states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) always prayed two rak'ahs after every tawaf, establishing it as a sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed practice). This hadith is cited as evidence for the obligation of the two rak'ahs after Tawaf al-Wada'.

Key Terms
طواف الوداع (Tawaf al-Wada'): The farewell circumambulation of the Kaaba performed before leaving Makkah after completing Hajj or Umrah.
طواف الصدر (Tawaf al-Sadr): Another name for Tawaf al-Wada', meaning the departing tawaf.
واجب (wajib): An obligation established by a zanni (probable) proof; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, for whom is Tawaf al-Wada' not wajib?
A) Pilgrims performing Hajj tamattu'
B) People of Makkah and those residing there
C) Women only
D) Those who have already performed Tawaf al-Qudum

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib on all pilgrims except residents of Makkah, and its omission requires a dam; the two rak'ahs after it are also wajib.

Etiquettes and Virtues of Drinking Zamzam Water
Etiquettes and proofs for drinking Zamzam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the recommended etiquettes of drinking Zamzam water and EXPLAIN the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Drink Zamzam to satiation facing qibla; it is for whatever you intend.

The Prophet ﷺ and his Companions established specific etiquettes for drinking Zamzam water, combining devotion and intention. This lesson examines the sunnan practices and the hadith that support them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is drinking Zamzam water. Identify its hukm level according to the Hanafi school: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah?
The hadith use imperatives, but other proofs show these are recommendations, not obligations.
2
List the recommended etiquettes
From the passage, enumerate all the sunnan acts mentioned: facing qibla, mentioning Allah's name, breathing three times, drinking to satiation, looking at the Kaaba, pouring water on body, etc.
These are all mustahabb (recommended).
3
Locate the dalil for each etiquette
For each sunnah, find the specific hadith cited. For example, the instruction of Abbas, the Prophet drinking while standing, the Prophet drawing water himself, etc.
The passage provides multiple hadith references.
4
Understand the meaning of 'Zamzam water is for whatever it is drunk for'
This hadith indicates that one should make a sincere intention before drinking, and Allah will bring about that purpose.
It is recommended to recite the du'a of Ibn Abbas.
5
Note the Hanafi position on obligation
The Hanafi school holds these etiquettes as sunnah muakkadah, not wajib. Missing them does not invalidate the act or require compensation.
The evidence is that the Prophet himself did not always perform all these acts in every instance.

Translation (1380): Then he goes to Zamzam and drinks from its water. If able, he extracts water himself from the well, faces the House (Kaaba), drinks to satiation, taking multiple breaths, and at each breath he raises his gaze towards the House. If possible, he pours it on his body; otherwise, he wipes his face and head. He may intend whatever he wishes while drinking. Explanation: Drink Zamzam water to satiation, while sitting and looking towards the Kaaba, and while standing. Evidence: (1) I was sitting with Abbas when a man came and he asked, 'Where have you come from?' He said, 'From Zamzam.' He said, 'Did you drink from it properly?' He said, 'How?' He said, 'When you drink from it, face the qibla, mention Allah's name, breathe three times, and drink to satiation. When finished, praise Allah Almighty. For indeed the Messenger of Allah said: The sign between us and the hypocrites is that they do not drink Zamzam to satiation.' (Ibn Majah, no. 306) This statement of a Companion indicates to drink to satiation and while facing the qibla. (2) And for drinking while standing, there is this hadith: Ibn Abbas narrated that he gave the Prophet (peace be upon him) water from Zamzam and he drank while standing. (Bukhari, no. 1636) This hadith indicates drinking Zamzam while standing. (3) The Prophet drank Zamzam water and also said, 'I myself would draw water.' So if able, one should draw water from the well himself. For this there is a hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... and he went to the House, prayed Zuhr in Makkah, then came to the Banu Abdul Muttalib who were drawing water from Zamzam. He said, 'Draw water, O Banu Abdul Muttalib! Were it not that people would overcome you in drawing water, I would draw with you.' So they handed him a bucket and he drank from it. (Muslim, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, no. 1905) (4) And to take some with him: Aisha used to carry water from Zamzam and informed that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to carry it. (Tirmidhi, no. 963) This indicates taking water home. (5) From Ka'b: When he entered Zamzam, he entered with his camel, then drank from it and poured water on his clothes. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, no. 9180) This action of a Tabi'i indicates sprinkling water on clothes. Translation (1381): And Abdullah ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) when he drank used to say, 'O Allah, I ask You for beneficial knowledge, abundant provision, and healing from every disease.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Zamzam water is for whatever it is drunk for.' Evidence: (1) The du'a of Ibn Abbas: Ibn Abbas drank Zamzam and then said, 'I ask You for beneficial knowledge, abundant provision, and healing from every disease.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, no. 9175) (2) The hadith that Zamzam is for what it is drunk for: I heard Jabir ibn Abdullah say, 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Zamzam water is for whatever it is drunk for.' (Ibn Majah, no. 3062)
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage details the sunnan etiquettes of drinking Zamzam water and its virtues. It begins by recommending that after finishing the farewell tawaf, the pilgrim should approach the well of Zamzam, preferably draw the water himself if able, face the Kaaba, drink to satiation in three breaths, and at each breath look towards the Kaaba. It is also recommended to pour some water on his body or wipe his face and head. He may make any intention for the water. The commentary provides evidence from various hadith: the instruction of Abbas to face qibla and drink in three breaths, the Prophet drinking while standing, the Prophet drawing water himself, and the Companions carrying Zamzam water home and sprinkling it on clothes. Then the passage mentions the du'a of Ibn Abbas when drinking: 'O Allah, I ask You for beneficial knowledge, abundant provision, and healing from every disease.' It also quotes the famous hadith, 'Zamzam water is for whatever it is drunk for,' indicating that one should make intention for a specific purpose and it will be fulfilled by Allah's will. These etiquettes are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory, but they are part of the sunnah of the Prophet and the practice of the righteous predecessors.

Key Terms
زمزم (Zamzam): The blessed well near the Kaaba in Makkah, from which water is drunk for its spiritual and physical benefits.
يتضلع (yatadalla'): To drink to satiation, filling the stomach.
ملتزم (Multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba, where it is recommended to press one's chest and face.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is only permissible to drink it for religious intentions
B) The drinker should make a specific intention, and Allah will fulfill it
C) It is a medicine that works for all diseases
D) It is only for quenching thirst

Key Takeaway
The sunnan of drinking Zamzam transform a simple act into an act of worship, and the water achieves whatever is intended by the drinker.

The Mustahabb Acts After Drinking Zamzam
Recommended acts after drinking Zamzam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts after drinking Zamzam and identify the hadith evidence for them.

Core Idea
After drinking Zamzam, press your chest at the Multazam—a sunnah from the Prophet himself.

This passage covers the beautiful sunnah acts that complete the experience of drinking Zamzam water. While not obligatory, these actions—kissing the threshold, clinging to the Multazam, and supplicating—are deeply rooted in the Prophet's practice and carry great reward. They are especially recommended when one is about to depart from Makkah.

Guided Path
1
List the Recommended Acts
Identify each action the text prescribes after drinking Zamzam: kissing the 'Utbah (threshold), going to the Multazam, placing chest and face on it, holding the curtain, and supplicating.
These acts are performed in sequence.
2
Define the Multazam
Understand that the Multazam is the area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba. Its name comes from 'iltizam' (to cling).
It is a specific, sacred spot.
3
Examine the Hadith Evidence
Read the hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb, where Abdullah ibn Umar demonstrates the action and says he saw the Prophet do it. Note that this is a sahih hadith (Sunan Abi Dawud).
The Prophet's action is the primary basis.
4
Determine the Ruling Level
Recognise that these acts are mustahabb (sunnah muakkadah) — recommended, not obligatory. The hadith's chain is ahad (zanni), so it cannot impose obligation in Hanafi usul.
Leaving them is permissible, but performing them is rewarding.
5
Note the Context
The text specifies that these acts are performed after drinking Zamzam, especially when one is about to return home. This shows they are part of the farewell adab.
They are not part of tawaf itself.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: (۱۳۸۲) اور زمزم پینے کے بعد مستحب ہے کہ کعبہ کے دروازے پر آئے اور عقبہ (خانہ کعبہ کا آستانہ ) کو بوسہ دے، پھر ملتزم جو حجر اسود اور دروازے کے درمیان ہے، پر آئے ، اور اپنے سینہ اور چہرہ کو اس پر رکھے، اور کعبہ کے پردہ کوتھوڑی دیر کے لئے پکڑے تشریح : حجر اسود سے لیکر کعبہ کے دروازے تک کے درمیان کو ملتزم کہتے ہیں، ملتزم کا ترجمہ ہے لپیٹنا، چونکہ یہاں لپٹتے ہیں اس لئے اس کو ملتزم کہتے ہیں ۔ مستحب یہ ہے کہ جب وطن واپس جانے لگے تو آب زمزم پینے کے بعد ملتزم پر آکر اپنا سینہ اور چہرہ رکھے اور کعبہ کا جو پردہ اوپر سے لڑکا ہوا ہے اس کے ساتھ تھوڑی دیر لیٹ کر روئے۔ وجه : اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے . عن عمر و بن شعیب عن ابيه قال طفت مع عبد الله فلما جئنا دبر الكعبة قلت ألا تتعوذ ؟ قال نعوذ بالله من النار ثم مضى حتى استلم الحجر و اقام بين الركن و الباب فوضع صدره و وجهه و ذراعيه و كفيه هكذا و بسطهما بسطا ثم قال هكذا رأيت رسول الله عله يفعله (ابوداؤد شریف،
Translation (1382): And after drinking Zamzam, it is mustahabb to go to the door of the Kaaba and kiss the 'Utbah (threshold), then go to the Multazam, which is between the Black Stone and the door, and place his chest and face on it, and hold the curtain of the Kaaba for a short while. Explanation: The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba is called Multazam. The word Multazam means 'to cling', because one clings there. It is mustahabb that when one is about to return to his homeland, after drinking Zamzam water, he goes to the Multazam and places his chest and face on it, and lies for a short while crying while holding the hanging curtain of the Kaaba. Evidence: For this there is a hadith: from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father, he said: I performed tawaf with Abdullah (ibn Umar). When we came to the back of the Kaaba, I said, 'Will you not seek refuge?' He said, 'We seek refuge in Allah from the Fire.' Then he went on until he touched the Black Stone and stood between the corner and the door, and placed his chest, face, arms, and palms like this, spreading them out. Then he said, 'This is how I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) do it.' (Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage covers the mustahabb (recommended) acts to be performed after drinking Zamzam water, particularly when one is about to depart from Makkah. It recommends going to the door of the Kaaba, kissing the threshold (called 'Utbah), then proceeding to the area between the Black Stone and the door known as the Multazam. At the Multazam, one should press his chest and face against the wall, hold the covering curtain of the Kaaba, and supplicate, preferably while weeping. The term 'Multazam' derives from 'iltizam', meaning to cling or embrace, because the pilgrim embraces the wall. The commentary provides evidence from a hadith where Abdullah ibn Umar demonstrated this practice, reporting that he saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) do exactly that. This practice is considered a recommended sunnah at the conclusion of Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms
ملتزم (Multazam): The area between the Black Stone (al-Hajar al-Aswad) and the door of the Kaaba, where it is recommended to press one's chest and face.
عقبة ('Utbah): The threshold of the door of the Kaaba, which is kissed as a sign of respect.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended act; reward for doing it, no sin for leaving it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The Multazam acts are a beautiful sunnah of the Prophet, performed after drinking Zamzam, and are mustahabb, not wajib.

The Multazam: A Place of Supplication
Describes the Multazam and the sunnah actions upon entering the Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended actions at the Multazam and state the evidence for its virtue.

Core Idea
The Multazam is a sunnah place to supplicate with chest and face during Hajj.

This lesson explains the sunnah acts upon entering the Kaaba, specifically at the Multazam. You will learn the physical actions, the supplication, and the hadith evidence that establishes this practice as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Multazam location
The Multazam is the area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba. Understand its exact location and significance.
Some confuse it with the Black Stone itself; it is a distinct area.
2
Describe the recommended actions
The pilgrim places his chest and face on the Multazam, clings to the curtains, and supplicates earnestly.
These actions are based on the Prophet's practice.
3
Recite the prescribed du'a
The text provides a specific supplication asking for acceptance and return. Learn it and its meaning.
Any sincere du'a is also permissible.
4
Cite the hadith evidence
The hadith from Ibn Majah and others show the Prophet placing his chest and face on the Multazam.
The chain is hasan; the act is considered sunnah.
5
Note the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, this action is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed recommended) based on the Prophet's example.
It is not wajib; omitting it does not invalidate Hajj.
