فصل تركيب افعال الحج باب الكعبة ويُقبل العتبة ثم يأتى الى الملتزم وهو ما بين الحجر الاسود والباب فيضع صدره ووجهه عليه و يتشبث باستار الكعبة ساعة ( ۱۳۸۳ ) يتضرع الى الله تعالى بالدعاء بما احبّ من امور الدارين ويقول اللهم ان هذا بيتك الذى جعلته مباركا وهدى للعلمين اللهم كما هديتنى له فتقبل منى ولا تجعل هذا آخر العهد من بيتک وارزقنی العود اليه حتى ترضی عنّی برحمتک یا ارحم الراحمين. (۱۳۸۴) والملتزم من الاماكن التى يستجاب فيها الدعاء بمكة المشرفة وهي خمسة عشر موضعا نقلها الكمال بن الهمام عن رسالة الحسن البصري رحمه الله بقوله في الطواف وعند باب الملتزم، ص۲۷۶ نمبر ۱۸۹۹ رابن ماجه شریف، باب الملتزم، ص ۴۲۹، نمبر ۲۹۶۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے ملتزم پر اپنا سینہ اور چہرہ رکھا اور ہاتھ کو پھیلایا۔ لغت : عقبة : چوکھٹ۔ بینشبت : چھٹے ۔ استار: ستر کی جمع ہے، پردہ۔ساعتۃ : ایک گھڑی۔ بیتشبث : چھٹے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۸۳) اللہ تعالی سے دنیا آخرت کے محبوب امور کی دعا تضرع سے مانگے ، اور یہ ( بھی ) کہے: اے اللہ یہ آپ کا گھر جسے آپ نے سارے جہاں کے لئے با برکت اور ہدایت بنایا ہے، اے اللہ جیسے آپ نے مجھے یہاں آنے کی ہدایت دی پس قبول فرما لیجئے ، اور اپنے گھر کی حاضری کو آخری حاضری نہ بنا ، اس کی طرف دوبارہ آنے کی توفیق دیجئے، یہاں تک کہ اے ارحم الراحمین آپ اپنی رحمت سے مجھ سے راضی ہو جا۔ وجه :(۱) اس حدیث میں دعا کا ذکر ہے۔ حدیث ہے۔ طارق ابن علقمة اخبره عن امه ان النبي الله كان اذا جاء مـكـانـا فـي دار يـعـلـى استقبل القبلة و دعا - ( نسائی شریف، باب الدعا عند رویۃ البیت ،ص ۳۹۹،نمبر ۲۸۹۹)(۲) انبأ الشافعي قال احب له اذا ودع البيت ان يقف فى الملتزم و هو بين الركن و الباب فيقول: اللهم البيت بیتک و العبد عبدک و ابن عبدک و ابن امتک حملتني على ما سخرت لى من خلقک حتی سیرتنی فی بلادک و بلغتنی بنعمتک حتی اعنتنی علی قضاء مناسکک فان کنت رضیت عنی فازدد عنی رضا و الا فمن الان قبل ان تنای عن بیتک داری فهذا اوان انصرافي ان اذنت لی غیر مستبدل بک و لا ببیتک و لا راغب عنك و لا عن بيتك اللهم فاصحبنی با لعافیة فی بدنی و العصمة في ديني و احسن منقلبی و ارزقنی طاعتک ما ابقیتی ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب الوقوف في الملتزم، ج خامس، ص ۲۶۸، نمبر ۹۷۶۷) اس قول تابعی میں دعا کا ذکر ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۸۴) اور ملتزم مکہ مکرمہ کے ان مقامات میں سے ہے جہاں دعا قبول ہوتی ہے۔ اور ایسی پندرہ جگہیں ہیں جنہیں علامہ ابن ہمام نے حضرت حسن بصری کے رسالے سے نقل کیا ہے۔ ان کے فرمان کے مطابق ( وہ پندرہ مقامات یہ ہیں ) قبولیت دعا کے مقامات ...... حالت طواف میں۔ ..... ملتزم کے پاس۔ میزاب (رحمت) کے نیچے۔ ..... بیت اللہ کے اندر۔ زمزم کے پاس۔ مقام ابراہیم کے پیچھے۔ ... صفا پر۔ ....... مروه پر۔ ...... حالت سعی میں ۔ ۱۰ عرفات میں ۔ اا... منی میں ۔ ۱۲ جمرہ اولی۔ ....... جمرہ ثانیہ۔ جمره ثالثہ کے پاس ( رمی کے وقت ) ۔ ... چوتھے دن کی رمی کے وقت ۔ نوٹ : حدیث میں جن مقامات پر دعا کرنے کا ذکر ہے مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ وہاں دعا قبول ہوتی ہے، چنانچہ اوپر کے تمام مقامات پر حضور سے دعا ثابت ہے۔
Section: Combining the actions of Hajj. Chapter: He approaches the Kaaba, kisses the threshold, then goes to the Multazam, which is between the Black Stone and the door. He places his chest and face upon it and clings to the curtains of the Kaaba for a while (1383), supplicating to Allah Almighty with whatever beloved matters of this world and the Hereafter he wishes, and says: 'O Allah, this is Your House which You have made blessed and guidance for all worlds. O Allah, just as You guided me to it, then accept it from me, and do not make this my last visit to Your House, and grant me return to it until You are pleased with me, by Your mercy, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' (1384) And the Multazam is among the places where supplication is answered in Mecca the Noble. There are fifteen such places, transmitted by Kamal ibn al-Humam from the treatise of al-Hasan al-Basri, may Allah have mercy on him, who said: during Tawaf, at the Multazam (page 276, number 1899 of Ibn Majah, chapter on Multazam, page 429, number 2962). In this hadith, it is mentioned that the Prophet placed his chest and face on the Multazam and spread his hands. Lexicon: 'Uqbah: threshold. Yatasannad: catches hold. Astar: plural of sitr, curtain. Sa'atan: an hour. Tatashabbath: clings. Translation: (1383) He earnestly supplicates to Allah with beloved matters of this world and the Hereafter, and also says: 'O Allah, this is Your House which You have made blessed and guidance for all worlds. O Allah, just as You guided me to it, then accept it from me, and do not make this my last visit to Your House, and grant me return to it until You are pleased with me, by Your mercy, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' Evidence: (1) This hadith mentions supplication. The hadith is: Tariq ibn 'Alqamah reported from his mother that when the Prophet came to a place in the house of Ya'la, he faced the Qibla and supplicated. (Sunan al-Nasa'i, chapter on supplication at the sight of the House, page 399, number 2899) (2) Al-Shafi'i said: 'I prefer that when he bids farewell to the House, he stands at the Multazam, which is between the corner and the door, and says: 'O Allah, this House is Your House, and the servant is Your servant, the son of Your male servant and the son of Your female servant. You have carried me upon what You have subjected to me of Your creation until You caused me to travel through Your lands and reached me with Your bounty until You helped me to perform Your rituals. If You are pleased with me, then increase in pleasure; otherwise, now before my house takes me far from Your House, this is the time of my departure if You permit, not changing You nor Your House, nor turning away from You nor from Your House. O Allah, accompany me with health in my body and protection in my religion, and make my return good, and grant me obedience to You as long as You keep me alive.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on standing at the Multazam, volume 5, page 268, number 9767) This saying of a Tabi'i mentions supplication. Translation: (1384) And the Multazam is among the places in Mecca where supplication is answered. And there are fifteen such places, which Allamah Ibn al-Humam narrated from the treatise of Hasan al-Basri, may Allah have mercy on him. According to his saying (those fifteen places are): Places of answered prayer: ... during Tawaf; ... near the Multazam; under the spout (of mercy); ... inside the Kaaba; near Zamzam; behind the Maqam; ... on Safa; ... on Marwa; ... during Sa'y; 10: in Arafat; 11: in Mina; 12: at the first Jamra; ... at the second Jamra; near the third Jamra (at the time of stoning); ... at the time of stoning on the fourth day. Note: In the hadith, the places where supplication is mentioned, the author says that supplication is answered there. Thus, it is proven that the Prophet supplicated at all the above places.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling about the sunnah acts upon entering the Kaaba, specifically the Multazam. It begins by describing the physical actions: kissing the threshold, then proceeding to the Multazam (the area between the Black Stone and the door). The pilgrim is to place his chest and face on it, cling to the curtains, and supplicate fervently. The text provides a sample supplication (du'a) asking for acceptance, continued visitation, and divine pleasure. It then affirms that the Multazam is one of the places where du'a is answered, and lists fifteen such locations in Makkah based on the transmission of Kamal ibn al-Humam from Hasan al-Basri's treatise. The author includes a hadith from Ibn Majah showing the Prophet's action at the Multazam, and further supports the practice with a hadith from Nasa'i and a statement from Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a farewell du'a at the Multazam. The commentary also provides a glossary of difficult words. In the Hanafi school, these practices are considered sunnah mu'akkadah based on the Prophet's example and the consensus of scholars. The list of places where du'a is answered includes the Kaaba itself, Zamzam, Safa and Marwa, Arafat, Mina, and the Jamarat. The passage emphasizes the virtue of supplicating at these sites.

Key Terms
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba; also the general area near the door from the inside.
الميزاب (al-mīzāb): The spout of mercy, located on the roof of the Kaaba on the side of the Hijr Ismail, used for rainwater drainage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of placing one's chest and face on the Multazam and supplicating there?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Mubah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The Multazam is a confirmed sunnah place for du'a, with prophetic evidence and scholarly consensus.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
The Fifteen Places of Answered Prayer in Hajj
Lists fifteen places of answered supplication in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the fifteen places where du'a is answered during Hajj and explain their significance.

Core Idea
Fifteen specific locations in Makkah and Mina are established for answered supplication.

This lesson enumerates the fifteen places of answered prayer derived from Hasan al-Basri's treatise and transmitted by Kamal ibn al-Humam. Each location has prophetic precedent, and knowing them helps pilgrims maximise the spiritual benefits of their journey.

Guided Path
1
Understand the list's source
The list is transmitted from Hasan al-Basri via Kamal ibn al-Humam. Recognise that later scholars compiled these based on hadith and practice.
The list is not from a single hadith but a collection of evidences.
2
Memorise the fifteen places in order
Commit the list to memory: during Tawaf, near the Multazam, under the spout, inside the Kaaba, near Zamzam, behind Maqam Ibrahim, on Safa, on Marwa, during Sa'y, in Arafat, in Mina, at the first Jamra, at the second Jamra, near the third Jamra, and at the stoning on the fourth day.
Some versions may have slight variations; this is the standard list.
3
Recognise their occurrence in the Hajj sequence
Map each place to the stage of Hajj: Tawaf and Sa'y in Makkah, then Arafat, Mina, and Jamarat.
This helps in planning supplications.
4
Note the prophetic evidence for each
The text states that supplication at these places is proven from the Prophet's practice. Understand that each location has associated hadith.
Not all hadith are cited, but the author asserts their existence.
5
Appreciate the virtue of supplication at these spots
These are places where du'a is more likely to be accepted. The pilgrim should make sincere du'a combining humility and hope.
The list is not exhaustive but covers the major sites.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling about the sunnah acts upon entering the Kaaba, specifically the Multazam. It begins by describing the physical actions: kissing the threshold, then proceeding to the Multazam (the area between the Black Stone and the door). The pilgrim is to place his chest and face on it, cling to the curtains, and supplicate fervently. The text provides a sample supplication (du'a) asking for acceptance, continued visitation, and divine pleasure. It then affirms that the Multazam is one of the places where du'a is answered, and lists fifteen such locations in Makkah based on the transmission of Kamal ibn al-Humam from Hasan al-Basri's treatise. The author includes a hadith from Ibn Majah showing the Prophet's action at the Multazam, and further supports the practice with a hadith from Nasa'i and a statement from Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a farewell du'a at the Multazam. The commentary also provides a glossary of difficult words. In the Hanafi school, these practices are considered sunnah mu'akkadah based on the Prophet's example and the consensus of scholars. The list of places where du'a is answered includes the Kaaba itself, Zamzam, Safa and Marwa, Arafat, Mina, and the Jamarat. The passage emphasizes the virtue of supplicating at these sites.

Key Terms
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba; also the general area near the door from the inside.
الميزاب (al-mīzāb): The spout of mercy, located on the roof of the Kaaba on the side of the Hijr Ismail, used for rainwater drainage.

Fifteen Places of Acceptance of Supplication During Hajj
Enumerates places of accepted du'a during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the fifteen places where du'a is accepted during Hajj and explain their significance.

Core Idea
Fifteen sacred spots during Hajj where supplication is especially answered.

The Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) specified particular locations during Hajj where du'a is more likely to be accepted. This list, transmitted from Hasan al-Basri and recorded by Allama Ibn Humam, helps pilgrims focus their supplications. The passage enumerates these places, from the Multazam to the Jamarat, as opportunities for increased devotion.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the Sequence
Learn the fifteen places in the order given: start with al-Multazam, then under the Mizab, inside the Kaaba, at Zamzam, behind Maqam Ibrahim, on Safa, on Marwa, during Sa'i, in Arafat, in Mina, and at each of the three Jamarat (including the fourth day's stoning).
The list is divided into groups: near the Kaaba, during Sa'i, at Arafat/Mina, and at the Jamarat.
2
Understand Each Location
For each place, recall its significance in Hajj rituals. For example, al-Multazam is between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba; the Mizab is the golden spout; Zamzam is the well; Maqam Ibrahim is the station of Ibrahim; Safa and Marwa are hills for Sa'i; Arafat is the plain for standing; Mina is the valley for stoning; and the Jamarat are the pillars for rami.
The passage emphasizes that du'a at these places is proven from the Prophet's practice.
3
Apply the Knowledge
When planning a Hajj itinerary, mark these spots to intentionally make du'a. For instance, after Tawaf, go to al-Multazam and supplicate; after drinking Zamzam, make du'a; during the stay at Arafat, raise your hands; and at each Jamrah, supplicate after stoning.
The acceptance is from Allah, but these places are blessed for du'a.

الملتزم وتحت الميزاب وفى البيت وعند زمزم وخلف المقام وعلى الصفا وعلى المروة وفي السعي وفي عرفات وفى منى وعند الجمرات (انتهى)

Section: Composition of acts of Hajj. Al-Multazam, under the spout, in the house, at Zamzam, behind the Maqam, on Safa, on Marwa, in Sa'i, in Arafat, in Mina, at the Jamarat (end). Allama Ibn Humam narrated from Hasan al-Basri's treatise: according to his statement, these are the fifteen places: Places of acceptance of du'a: during Tawaf, near Multazam, under the Mizab (mercy), inside the Kaaba, near Zamzam, behind Maqam Ibrahim, on Safa, on Marwa, during Sa'i, in Arafat, in Mina, at first Jamra, at second Jamra, near third Jamra (during rami), during the fourth day's rami. Note: The author says that in hadith, the places where supplication is mentioned are where du'a is accepted, thus at all the above places supplication from the Prophet is proven.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage defines and enumerates fifteen specific locations during Hajj where supplication (du'a) is particularly encouraged and accepted. The list begins with the Arabic terms for these places, then the Urdu commentary expands them with descriptive details. The author emphasizes that the Prophet's practice confirms the virtue of supplication at each of these spots. The places include the Multazam (the area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba), under the Mizab (the golden spout of the Kaaba), inside the Kaaba itself, near Zamzam, behind Maqam Ibrahim, on the hills of Safa and Marwa, during the Sa'i, at Arafat, Mina, and at each of the three Jamarat during stoning, including the fourth day (the thirteenth of Dhul Hijjah). This is not a legal obligation but a recommended practice to seek blessings and acceptance of du'a.

Key Terms
ملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba where pilgrims press their bodies and supplicate.
ميزاب (mīzāb): The golden spout of the Kaaba from which rainwater drains, located on the roof.
جمرات (jamarāt): The three stone pillars at Mina where pilgrims throw pebbles during the days of Tashreeq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
There are fifteen specific places during Hajj where du'a is especially accepted, and pilgrims should strive to make supplications at these locations.

The Four Days of Rami (Stoning)
Specifies the four days for rami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four specified days for rami and explain that rami is wajib on each of those days in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Rami is wajib on four specific days: Yawm al-Nahr and the three Days of Tashreeq.

In the Hajj, the act of stoning the jamarat (rami) is an essential rite. This passage clarifies the exact days on which this obligation must be performed. Knowing this timeframe is crucial for fulfilling the Hajj correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is rami (stoning the three jamarat). In Hanafi fiqh, rami is classified as wajib (necessary), not fard, because it is proven by ahad hadith and consensus of the scholars.
Wajib means omission requires compensation (dam), but does not invalidate Hajj entirely.
2
Determine the number of days
The text states that rami is performed on four days. Count them: the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah) and three days after it.
The three days after are the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, known as Ayyam al-Tashreeq.
3
Memorize the specific dates
Commit the dates to memory: 10th, 11th, 12th, 13th. The 10th is Yawm al-Nahr, and the 11th-13th are the Days of Tashreeq.
Some pilgrims only stay until the 12th, but the full sunnah is to stay until the 13th.
4
Understand the practical consequence
A pilgrim must perform rami on each of these days. Missing rami on any day without a valid excuse requires a dam (sacrifice) as compensation.
If a pilgrim departs Mina on the 12th before sunset, they are excused from the 13th day's rami.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۸۵) والـجـمـرات تُرمى فى اربعة ايام يوم النحر وثلاثة بعده كما تقدّم ترجمه : (۱۳۸۵) اور جمرات کی رمی چار دن ہوتی ہے یوم نحر اور تین دن اس کے بعد جیسا کہ پہلے بیان ہوا۔ تشریح : پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ چار دنوں تک رمی کی جاتی ہے، پہلا دن ۱۰۔ دسویں ذی الحجہ، ۱۱ ۱۲ ۱۳۔ ذی الحجہ ہے۔
(1385) The jamarat are stoned on four days: the Day of Sacrifice and three days after it, as previously mentioned. Translation: (1385) And the stoning of the jamarat occurs on four days: the Day of Sacrifice and three days after it, as previously stated. Explanation: It has passed that stoning is done for four days: the first day is the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, then 11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This is a ruling statement specifying the time period for the obligatory stoning (rami) of the three jamarat. The text confirms that rami is performed over four days: the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr, 10th Dhul Hijjah) and the three following days (11th, 12th, 13th), collectively known as the Days of Tashreeq. This is a fixed ruling in the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice. The commentary reiterates the dates.

Key Terms
رمی (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the three jamarat during Hajj.
یوم النحر (yawm al-naḥr): The Day of Sacrifice, the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, when the sacrificial animal is slaughtered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Rami is performed on four specific days: 10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Supplication When Seeing the Kaaba
States the recommendation and provides two hadiths as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplication upon seeing the Kaaba and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Seeing the Kaaba is a moment of accepted du'a; it is sunnah, not obligatory.

When a pilgrim first catches sight of the Kaaba, it is a time of great spiritual significance. This passage reaffirms that making supplication at that moment is a recommended practice, supported by the Prophet's own example. We will examine the evidence and the specific du'a transmitted from him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act (supplication upon seeing the Kaaba) and its hukm level (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
This is a recommended act, not obligatory.
2
Locate the evidence
Identify the two hadiths cited: from Nasa'i and Bayhaqi, showing the Prophet's practice.
Both are ahad hadith, but sufficient for establishing istihbab.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit action of the Prophet making du'a at this moment indicates recommendation, as there is no evidence of obligation.
In Hanafi usul, an action of the Prophet is interpreted as istihbab unless evidence shows obligation.
4
Note the consensus
All schools agree on the recommendation; there is no dispute.
This is muttafaq alayh.
5
Apply the ruling
When you see the Kaaba for the first time, make du'a with the transmitted words or your own, in any language.
The specific du'a from the hadith is recommended but not required.

(۱۳۸۶) وذكرنا استجابته ايضا عند رؤية البيت المكرّم ترجمه : (۱۳۸۶) بیت اللہ کی زیارت کے وقت بھی دعا کا قبول ہونا ہم نے بیان کیا ہے۔ وجه : (۱) بیت اللہ دیکھتے وقت دعا قبول ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ طارق ابن علقمة اخبره عن امه ان النبي لالالالالالالي كان اذا جاء مكانا في دار يعلى استقبل القبلة و دعا ۔ (نسائی شریف، باب الدعا عند رویتہ البیت، ص ۱۳۹۹، نمبر ۲۸۹۹) دار یعلی کے سامنے سے بیت اللہ نظر آتا تھا اس لئے جب حضور دار یعلی کے سامنے آتے اور بیت اللہ پر نظر پڑتی تو دعا کرتے کیونکہ یہاں دعا قبول ہوتی ہے۔ (۲) بیت اللہ دیکھتے وقت یہ دعا منقول ہے۔ عن مكحول قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا دخل مكة

(1386) And we mentioned its acceptance also at the sight of the honored House. Translation: (1386) We have mentioned that supplication is accepted at the time of seeing the Kaaba. Evidence: (1) The proof that supplication is accepted when seeing the Kaaba is this hadith: Tariq ibn 'Alqamah informed him from his mother that the Prophet ... used to, when he came to a place in the house of Ya'la, face the qibla and supplicate. (Nasa'i, Bab al-Du'a 'inda Ru'yat al-Bayt, p. 1399, no. 2899) (2) This supplication is transmitted when seeing the Kaaba: from Makhul, he said: The Prophet, when he entered Mecca, ... when he saw the House, he raised his hands and said, 'O Allah, You are Peace and from You is peace, so grant us, our Lord, life with peace. O Allah, increase this House in honor, greatness, and awe, and increase in honor, respect, and piety those who perform Hajj or Umrah.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Qawl 'inda Ru'yat al-Bayt, vol. 5, p. 18, no. 9213) This hadith mentions supplication when seeing the Kaaba.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage reaffirms the recommendation (istihbab) of supplication upon first seeing the Kaaba, supporting it with two hadiths. The first hadith from Nasa'i indicates that the Prophet would turn to the qibla and pray when he saw the Kaaba from a specific location in Dar Ya'la. The second, from Bayhaqi, records a specific du'a the Prophet made upon seeing the Kaaba, raising his hands and praising Allah. The commentary explains that these narrations establish that such moments are times of acceptance. In Hanafi fiqh, this is considered a sunnah (recommended act), not obligatory.

Key Terms
استجابة (istijābah): The acceptance of supplication by Allah, particularly at blessed times and places.
رؤية البيت (ru'yat al-bayt): The first sighting of the Kaaba upon arriving in Mecca.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Supplication upon seeing the Kaaba is a recommended sunnah supported by Prophetic practice.

Entering the Kaaba and Praying Inside
Ruling on entering Kaaba and prayer spot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for entering the Kaaba and identify the Prophet's recommended prayer spot inside, including its precise location.

Core Idea
Entering the Kaaba is a sunnah, not an obligation; the Prophet's prayer spot is about three cubits from the wall opposite the door.

This lesson examines the ruling on entering the Kaaba (the House of Allah) and performing prayer inside. The Hanafi school considers it a recommended act (mustahabb) provided it does not cause inconvenience to others. The passage also identifies the exact spot where the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) prayed, located about three cubits from the wall opposite the door, and clarifies that praying elsewhere inside is still permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being discussed and its hukm (legal classification). The act is entering the Kaaba and praying inside. The ruling stated in the passage is 'mustahabb' (recommended), conditioned on not harming anyone.
In Hanafi fiqh, mustahabb is synonymous with sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Identify the proof cited for this ruling. The passage references the practice of Ibn Umar (a companion) as a hadith. This dalil is a verbal report (qawl) or action (fi'l) of a companion, which is classified as Sunnah ahad (single narration) and thus provides a zanni (probable) proof.
The hadith is not directly quoted in full, but its meaning is referenced.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
Analyze how the evidence indicates the ruling. Ibn Umar's action of walking forward upon entering the Kaaba and the Prophet's own practice at that spot show that entering and praying there is a recommended emulation, not an obligatory command.
The absence of an explicit command (amr) indicates the act is not wajib.
4
Note conditions and exceptions
The passage adds a condition: entering is recommended only if it does not cause harm (e.g., crowding or disturbing others). Additionally, if the exact spot cannot be found, prayer anywhere inside remains valid.
The condition reflects the Hanafi principle of avoiding harm (darar).
5
Evaluate practical application
Consider the current situation: the Kaaba's door is usually kept closed, limiting access. The ruling becomes relevant when the door is opened (e.g., during cleaning) or for those permitted to enter. The recommendation remains in principle, but practice is subject to feasibility.
This step connects classical fiqh to modern circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۸۷) ويستحب دخول البيت الشريف المبارك ان لم يوذ احدا وينبغي ان يقصد مصلّى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيه وهو قِبَلَ وجهه وقد جعل الباب قِبَلَ ظهره حتى يكون بينه وبين الجدار الذي قبل وجهه قرب ثلاثة اذرع ثم يصلّى ترجمه : (۱۳۸۷) اگر کسی کو تکلیف نہ دیجائے تو بیت اللہ شریف کے اندر داخل ہو نا مستحب ہے، اور مناسب ہے کہ اس میں بنی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے نماز پڑھنے کی جگہ کا قصد کرے، اور وہ جگہ چہرے کے سامنے ہے جب پیٹھ کے پیچھے دروازہ کیا جائے یہاں تک کے اس کے اور اس دیوار کے درمیان جو اس کے چہرے کے سامنے ہیں تین گز کا فاصلہ رہ جائے ( یعنی دروازے کے سامنے کی دیوار سے تقریبا تین گز پیچھے وہ جگہ ہے ) پھر نماز پڑھے۔ تشریح : اگر کسی کو تکلیف نہ ہو اور بیت اللہ کے اندر جاسکتا ہو تو اندر جائے اور جس جگہ حضور نے نماز پڑھی اس جگہ نماز پڑھے، اگر دوسری جگہ پڑھ لی تب بھی جائز ہے۔ بیت اللہ کے دروازے میں داخل ہو تو سیدھا دیوار کی طرف جائے اور دیوار سے تین ہاتھ [ ساڑھے چارفٹ] پیچھے رہے اس جگہ پر حضور نے نماز پڑھی ہے۔ آج کل بیت اللہ کا دروازہ مکمل بند رہتا ہے اس لئے بیت اللہ کے اندر داخل ہونا مشکل ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عمر انه كان اذا دخل الكعبة مشى قبل الوجه حين يدخل
(1387) And it is recommended to enter the blessed noble House if it does not harm anyone, and one should aim for the prayer place of the Prophet inside it, which is in front of his face when he makes the door behind his back, until there is a distance of about three cubits between him and the wall in front of his face, then pray. Translation: (1387) If no one is harmed, entering the Kaaba is recommended, and it is appropriate to seek the place where the Prophet prayed inside. That place is in front of the face when the door is behind the back, until there remains a distance of three yards between him and the wall in front of his face (i.e., about three yards back from the wall opposite the door), then pray. Explanation: If there is no harm and one can enter, he should enter and pray at the place where the Prophet prayed; if he prays elsewhere, it is also permissible. When entering the door of the Kaaba, he should go straight to the wall and stay three hand-spans (about four and a half feet) behind that wall; that is where the Prophet prayed. Nowadays the door of the Kaaba is always closed, so entering is difficult. Evidence: (1) This hadith proves it: from Ibn Umar, that when he entered the Kaaba, he walked forward upon entering.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of entering the Kaaba. The text states it is mustahabb (recommended) provided it does not cause inconvenience to others. It further describes the specific spot inside where the Prophet prayed: one should enter, turn so the door is behind the back, then walk forward about three cubits until reaching a spot in front of the opposite wall, and there pray. The commentary adds that if one cannot locate that precise spot, praying anywhere inside is still valid. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's practice. In Hanafi fiqh, entering the Kaaba is not obligatory but a virtuous sunnah, especially for men (women do not enter due to crowding). Today, since the door is usually locked, the ruling is practically limited to those with access.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustaḥabb): A recommended act; doing it is rewarded, leaving it is not sinful.
مصلّى النبي (muṣallā al-nabī): The specific spot inside the Kaaba where the Prophet prayed; located about three cubits from the wall opposite the door.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One cubit
B) Three cubits
C) Five cubits
D) Ten cubits

Key Takeaway
Entering the Kaaba is a recommended sunnah, and the specific spot of the Prophet's prayer is identified, but praying anywhere inside is still acceptable.

Supplication Upon Seeing the Kaaba
States the desirability of supplication when seeing the Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on making supplication upon seeing the Kaaba and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Seeing the Kaaba is a moment of exceptional mercy — the Prophet made du'a there, and so should you.

The Kaaba is the most sacred site in Islam. When a pilgrim lays eyes on it, the heart is filled with awe and devotion. The Prophet ﷺ taught us to seize this moment for supplication, as it is a time when duas are especially accepted. In this lesson, we examine the evidence from the Sunnah and the recommended practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making supplication (du'a) upon seeing the Kaaba. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed recommended).
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet consistently did it and encouraged it.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: the Prophet's practice at Dar Ya'la facing the qiblah and praying, and the specific supplication reported by Makhul upon entering Makkah and seeing the House.
These hadith are authentic, though ahad (single transmitted), establishing the practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates desirability (sunnah) because he did it repeatedly without commanding it as an obligation. The command is implicit in his practice.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action indicates recommendation unless there is a qarinah elevating it to obligation.

Source Text

وذكرنا استجابته ايضا عند رؤية البيت المكرّم

And we mentioned its acceptance also at the sight of the honored House. Translation: (1386) We have stated that supplication is accepted at the time of visiting the House of Allah. Proof: (1) The evidence for acceptance of supplication when seeing the House of Allah is this hadith: Tariq ibn Alqamah reported from his mother that the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he came to a place in the house of Ya'la, he faced the qiblah and made supplication. (Nasa'i, chapter on supplication when seeing the House, p. 1399, no. 2899) From in front of Dar Ya'la, the House of Allah was visible, so when the Prophet came in front of Dar Ya'la and saw the House of Allah, he would make supplication because supplication is accepted here. (2) This supplication is transmitted when seeing the House of Allah: From Makhul, he said: When the Prophet (peace be upon him) entered Makkah and saw the House, he raised his hands and said, 'Allahumma anta as-salam wa minka as-salam, fahayyina rabbana bi as-salam, allahumma zid hadha al-bayta tashrifan wa ta'ziman wa mahaba, wa zid man hajjahu aw i'tamarahu takriman wa tashrifan wa ta'ziman wa birra.' (Sunan, chapter on saying when seeing the House, vol. 5, p. 18, no. 9213) This hadith mentions supplication when seeing the House of Allah.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage confirms that seeing the Kaaba is a special time for supplication. The author has previously mentioned this; here he provides proofs. Two hadiths are cited: first, the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) at the house of Ya'la, and second, a specific supplication reported by Makhul. The Hanafi school encourages making du'a at this moment, as the Kaaba is the most sacred site and supplications are more likely to be accepted. The commentary explains that the place at Dar Ya'la had a view of the Kaaba, and the Prophet would face the qiblah and pray there.

Key Terms
رؤية البيت (ru'yat al-bayt): Seeing the Kaaba, specifically upon entering Makkah or approaching it.

Key Takeaway

Entering the Kaaba and Praying at the Prophet's Spot
States the Hanafi ruling and description of the Prophet's prayer spot inside the Kaaba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering the Kaaba and describe the specific prayer spot inside.

Core Idea
Entering the Kaaba is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation, and praying at the Prophet's spot earns extra reward.

Many pilgrims wonder about the virtue of entering the Kaaba and the best place to pray inside. This lesson clarifies that it is a sunnah recommended act, contingent on not causing harm to others, and describes the precise location where the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) prayed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that entering the Kaaba is a recommended (mustahabb) act, not obligatory. The text uses 'yustaḥabbu' indicating istihbab.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, a strongly recommended sunnah.
2
Determine the conditions
Note the condition: 'if one does not harm anyone.' This shows the act is contingent on not causing inconvenience to others.
Harm includes physical crowding or blocking others.
3
Locate the Prophet's prayer spot
The passage describes the spot: enter, make the door behind your back, and stand about three cubits from the opposite wall. This is the musalla an-nabi.
Three cubits ≈ 4.5 feet. The spot is opposite the door.
4
Understand the evidence
The ruling is based on the practice of Ibn Umar (as reported in hadith) and by extension the Prophet's own action.
The hadith is a dalīl naqlī (textual proof) for the recommendation.
5
Apply to modern context
Today, the Kaaba door may be closed or crowded. The ruling remains: enter if possible without harm; otherwise, the reward is still attainable in intention.
One may pray elsewhere inside if the exact spot is inaccessible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمه : (۱۳۸۷) اگر کسی کو تکلیف نہ دیجائے تو بیت اللہ شریف کے اندر داخل ہو نا مستحب ہے، اور مناسب ہے کہ اس میں بنی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے نماز پڑھنے کی جگہ کا قصد کرے، اور وہ جگہ چہرے کے سامنے ہے جب پیٹھ کے پیچھے دروازہ کیا جائے یہاں تک کے اس کے اور اس دیوار کے درمیان جو اس کے چہرے کے سامنے ہیں تین گز کا فاصلہ رہ جائے ( یعنی دروازے کے سامنے کی دیوار سے تقریبا تین گز پیچھے وہ جگہ ہے ) پھر نماز پڑھے۔ تشریح : اگر کسی کو تکلیف نہ ہو اور بیت اللہ کے اندر جاسکتا ہو تو اندر جائے اور جس جگہ حضور نے نماز پڑھی اس جگہ نماز پڑھے، اگر دوسری جگہ پڑھ لی تب بھی جائز ہے۔ بیت اللہ کے دروازے میں داخل ہو تو سیدھا دیوار کی طرف جائے اور دیوار سے تین ہاتھ [ ساڑھے چارفٹ] پیچھے رہے اس جگہ پر حضور نے نماز پڑھی ہے۔ آج کل بیت اللہ کا دروازہ مکمل بند رہتا ہے اس لئے بیت اللہ کے اندر داخل ہونا مشکل ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عمر انه كان اذا دخل الكعبة مشى قبل الوجه حين يدخل
And it is recommended to enter the blessed noble House if one does not harm anyone, and one should intend the prayer place of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in it, which is opposite his face when he makes the door behind his back, until there is about three cubits between him and the wall that is in front of his face, then he prays. Translation: (1387) If no one is caused inconvenience, then entering the noble House of Allah is recommended, and it is appropriate to aim for the place where the noble Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed, and that place is in front of the face when the door is made behind the back, until there remains a distance of three yards between him and the wall in front of his face (i.e., about three yards back from the wall opposite the door is that place), then he prays. Explanation: If no one is inconvenienced and he can enter the House of Allah, he should enter and pray in the place the Prophet prayed; if he prays elsewhere it is also permissible. Upon entering the door of the House of Allah, he should go straight to the wall and remain three hands (about 4.5 feet) behind the wall; that is where the Prophet prayed. Nowadays, the door of the House of Allah remains completely closed, so entering the House of Allah is difficult. Proof: This hadith provides evidence: from Ibn Umar that when he entered the Kaaba, he walked to the front when he entered...
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended act (mustahabb) of entering the Kaaba. The Hanafi school considers it a sunnah to enter if doing so does not cause harm or inconvenience to others. The specific spot where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed is described: one should enter, face the wall with the door behind, and stand about three cubits from the opposite wall. This is based on the practice of Ibn Umar and hadith. The Urdu commentary adds that it is permissible to pray anywhere inside, but the specific spot is superior. Today, entry is often restricted, but the virtue remains.

Key Terms
مصلّى النبي (musalla an-nabi): The specific spot inside the Kaaba where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed.
يستحب (yustaḥabbu): It is recommended (ruling of istihbab).

Placing the Cheek on the Kaaba Wall After Prayer
States the act of placing the cheek after prayer inside Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing the cheek on the wall after praying inside the Kaaba and identify the hadith evidence for its recommendation.

Core Idea
The Companions placed cheeks on the Kaaba; the Hanafi school recommends it after prayer inside.

After performing prayer inside the Kaaba, a specific act of devotion is encouraged: placing the cheek on the wall and engaging in dhikr. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence from the Prophet's practice, and how the Hanafi school classifies it as a recommended act (mustahabb).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Pinpoint exactly what action is being described and when it occurs: after praying inside the Kaaba facing the wall, placing the cheek on the wall and seeking forgiveness.
The text specifies 'when he prays facing the wall' — this is inside the Kaaba.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
Determine the legal classification of this act: mustahabb (recommended), meaning it is encouraged but not obligatory.
Hanafi position box confirms hukm_level = mustahabb.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the hadith of Abdur-Rahman ibn Safwan: the Companions placed their cheeks on the Kaaba after the conquest, in the Prophet's presence, and he did not forbid it.
This indicates tacit approval, which in Hanafi usul implies recommendation.
4
Understand the evidence of action
The Prophet's silence and presence during the Companions' action is considered a proof of permissibility and merit (dalālat al-taqrīr).
Wajh al-dalalah: the Prophet did not object, so the action is taken as recommended.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
When performing the act, follow the practice: after prayer inside the Kaaba, place your cheek on the wall between the door and al-Hatim, and recite istighfar and praise.
The act is specific to the Kaaba wall, not general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا صلّى الى الجدار يضع خده عليه ويستغفر الله ويحمده
ترجمه : (۱۳۸۸) جب دیوار کی طرف چہرہ کر کے نماز پڑھ چکے تو اپنے رخسار کو اس پر رکھدے اور اللہ سے استغفار کرے اس کی حمد کرے۔
وجه : (ا) عن عبد الرحمن بن صفوان قال لما فتح رسول الله مكة قلت لالبسن ثیابی و كانت داری على الطريق فلانظرن كيف يصنع رسول الله فانطلقت فرأيت النبي قد خرج من الكعبة هو و اصحابه قد استلموا البيت من الباب الى الحطيم وقد وضعوا خدودهم على البيت و رسول الله عليه وسطهم ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب الملتزم ص ۲۷۶، نمبر ۱۸۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کعبہ سے نکلنے کے بعد اپنے گالوں کو بیت اللہ کے دروازے سے حطیم تک کے درمیان میں رکھا۔
Then when he prays facing the wall, he places his cheek on it and seeks forgiveness from Allah and praises Him. Translation: (1388) When one has prayed facing the wall, he places his cheek on it and seeks forgiveness from Allah and praises Him. Proof: (1) From Abdur-Rahman ibn Safwan: 'When the Messenger of Allah conquered Makkah, I said I will put on my clothes, and my house was on the road, so I can see what the Messenger of Allah does. So I went and saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) come out of the Kaaba, he and his companions, they had touched the House from the door to al-Hatim, and placed their cheeks on the House, and the Messenger of Allah was among them.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on al-Multazam, p. 276, no. 1898) This hadith mentions that after coming out of the Kaaba, they placed their cheeks on the House of Allah between the door and al-Hatim.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
After performing prayer inside the Kaaba facing the wall, it is recommended to place the cheek on the wall, seeking forgiveness and praising Allah. The proof is the hadith of Abdur-Rahman ibn Safwan, which describes the Companions after the conquest of Makkah placing their cheeks on the Kaaba between the door and al-Hatim. The Hanafi school considers this an act of veneration and a sunnah practice, though not obligatory. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this act is done specifically after praying inside the Kaaba.

Key Terms
الحطيم (al-hatim): The semicircular wall adjacent to the Kaaba; also known as al-Hijr Ismail.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Recommended Acts at the Black Stone and al-Multazam
Describes the recommended acts at the rukn and al-multazam with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the recommended acts at the Black Stone and al-multazam, cite the hadith proof, and describe the proper manner of iltizam.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice at al-multazam establishes a recommended sunnah for pilgrims to supplicate and press against the wall.

After completing tawaf and praying at the Station of Ibrahim, the pilgrim is encouraged to approach the Black Stone and the area between it and the door. The Hanafi school holds that these acts are mustahabb, based on clear evidence from the Sunnah. In this lesson, we will examine the specific etiquettes and the hadith that establishes them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
Read the passage to list the actions described: praising Allah, saying la ilaha illallah, glorifying, saying Allahu akbar, supplicating, maintaining adab, and performing iltizam (standing between the rukn and door, pressing chest, face, and hands).
The acts are performed after entering the Kaaba and praying at the Prophet's prayer spot.
2
Determine the ruling
Identify the hukm level from the text. The Hanafi school classifies these acts as mustahabb (recommended), not wajib, as indicated by the permissive language and lack of command.
The phrase 'no harm on anyone to pray in any part...' suggests flexibility.
3
Locate the proof
Find the hadith cited: from Amr ibn Shu'ayb, describing Ibn Umar's practice of iltizam, which he attributes to the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), but its meaning is clear and acted upon by Companions.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the sunnah: the explicit statement 'Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah do it' shows direct emulation, making the act a confirmed practice (sunnah).
The Hanafi school accepts such ahad hadith for non-obligatory acts.
5
Note the thamarah
Consider the practical benefit: performing iltizam and supplication at this blessed place brings spiritual reward and acceptance of duas, though not obligatory.
This practice continues today at the Kaaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يأتى الاركان فيحمد ويهلل ويسبح ويكبر ويسأل الله تعالى ما شاء ويلزم الادب ما استطاع بظاهره وباطنه و يجعل الباب قبل الظهر يمشى حتى يكون بينه و بين الجدار الذي قبل وجهه قريبا من ثلاث اذرع فيصلى يتوخى المكان الذى اخبره بلال ان رسول الله صلى فيه و ليس على احد باس ان يصلي في اي نواحي البيت شاء
ترجمه : (۱۳۸۹)، پھر ارکان کے پاس آئے ، استغفار کرے، حمد کرے تہلیل کرے تسبیح کرے، تکبیر کہے، اللہ تعالی سے جو چاہے دعا کرے، ظاہر و باطن سے جتنا ہو سکے ادب کو لازم پکڑے۔
تشریح : یہاں ارکان سے مراد حجر اسود ہے، یعنی حجر اسود کے پاس آئے اور استغفار وغیرہ کرے اور دعا کرے۔ اس کے لئے حدیث گزرچکی ہے۔
وجه : (۱) اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے . عن عمر و بن شعیب عن ابيه قال طفت مع عبد الله فلما جئنا دبر الكعبة قلت ألا تتعوذ ؟ قال نعوذ بالله من النار ثم مضى حتى استلم الحجر و اقام بين الركن و الباب فوضع الله صدره و وجهه و ذراعیه و كفيه هكذا و بسطهما بسطا ثم قال هكذا رأيت رسول الله يفعله - ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب الملتزم، ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۱۸۹۹ رابن ماجه شریف، باب الملتزم ، ص ۴۲۹، نمبر ۲۹۶۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور
Then he comes to the rukn (corner), and praises Allah, says la ilaha illallah, glorifies Him, says Allahu akbar, and asks Allah Almighty for what he wishes, and maintains good manners as much as possible outwardly and inwardly, and makes the door behind his back, walking until there is between him and the wall in front of his face about three cubits, then he prays, aiming for the place that Bilal told him the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed there, and there is no harm on anyone to pray in any part of the House he wishes. Translation: (1389) Then he comes to the rukn, seeks forgiveness, praises, says la ilaha illallah, glorifies, says Allahu akbar, and asks Allah Almighty for what he wishes, and maintains adab as much as possible outwardly and inwardly. Explanation: Here 'arkan' refers to the Black Stone, i.e., he comes to the Black Stone and does istighfar, etc., and supplicates. The hadith for this has passed. Proof: (1) The hadith for this is: from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father: I performed tawaf with Abdullah, and when we came to the back of the Kaaba, I said, 'Will you not seek refuge?' He said, 'We seek refuge with Allah from the Fire.' Then he went until he touched the Black Stone and stood between the rukn and the door, and placed his chest, face, arms, and hands like this, spreading them out, then said, 'Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah do it.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on al-Multazam, p. 276, no. 1899; Ibn Majah, chapter on al-Multazam, p. 429, no. 2962) This hadith mentions that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did this.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage describes the acts after entering the Kaaba and praying at the Prophet's spot. The pilgrim should then go to the rukn (corner where the Black Stone is located) and engage in various forms of dhikr: seeking forgiveness, praising Allah, declaring His oneness, glorifying Him, and making takbir. Then he should supplicate for whatever he wishes, maintaining proper adab (etiquette) both outwardly and inwardly. The Urdu commentary clarifies that 'arkan' here specifically means the Black Stone. The proof is the hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb describing how Abdullah ibn Umar (and by extension the Prophet) would stand between the rukn and the door of the Kaaba, placing his chest and face and spreading his hands. This act is known as iltizam (clinging to the Kaaba). The Hanafi school considers this a recommended practice during tawaf or when visiting the Kaaba.

Key Terms
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba, where one stands and presses their body against the wall.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abdullah ibn Umar do at the Black Stone according to the hadith?
A) He kissed it and moved on
B) He stood between the rukn and the door, placing his chest, face, and hands
C) He performed two rak'ahs there
D) He recited the Talbiyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends iltizam and supplication at the Black Stone and al-multazam, based on the Prophet's practice as reported by Ibn Umar.

Recommended Acts Inside the Kaaba After Prayer
Rulings on placing cheek and visiting the corner with dhikr and dua

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts inside the Kaaba after prayer and identify the Hanafi ruling (mustahabb) with supporting evidence.

Core Idea
Placing the cheek on the wall and supplicating at the corner are recommended, not obligatory.

This lesson covers the sunan (recommended acts) to perform after entering the Kaaba and offering the initial prayer. Drawing on hadith reports from the Prophet's practice, the Hanafi school classifies these actions as mustahabb. Understanding this distinction between obligatory and recommended actions is essential for correct fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific actions are described after the initial prayer inside the Kaaba? Determine the Hanafi legal classification (hukm) for these actions.
The actions: placing cheek on wall, seeking forgiveness, praising Allah, then going to the corner for dhikr and dua.
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence does the author cite for these actions? Identify the hadith and its source.
Hadith from Abdur Rahman ibn Safwan (Abu Dawud 1898) and from Amr ibn Shu'ayb (Abu Dawud 1899, Ibn Majah 2962).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does the hadith prove the ruling? Examine the nature of the evidence.
The Prophet and companions placed their cheeks on the wall; this action indicates recommendation (istihbab) not obligation because the evidence is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there any difference of opinion on these acts? How does the Hanafi school respond?
Some other schools consider these acts as part of the Sunnah of tawaf; Hanafis consider them mustahabb but not integral.

(1388) فاذا صلّى الى الجدار يضع خده عليه ويستغفر الله ويحمده (1389) ثم يأتى الاركان فيحمد ويهلل ويسبح ويكبر ويسأل الله تعالى ما شاء ويلزم الادب ما استطاع بظاهره وباطنه و يجعل الباب قبل الظهر يمشى حتى يكون بينه و بين الجدار الذي قبل وجهه قريبا من ثلاث اذرع فيصلى يتوخى المكان الذى اخبره بلال ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى فيه و ليس على احد باس ان يصلي في اي نواحي البيت شاء. (بخاری شریف، باب الصلاة في الكعبة، ص ۲۵۹، نمبر ۱۵۹۹) - اتى ابن عمر فقيل له هذا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قد دخل الكعبة فقال ابن عمر فاقبلت و النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قد خرج و اجد بلالا قائما بين البابين فسالت بلالا فقلت اصلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الكعبة ؟ قال نعم ركعتين بين الساريتين اللتين على يساره اذا دخلت ثم خرج فصلى في وجه الكعبة ركعتين. (بخاری شریف، باب قولہ تعالی واتخذوا من مقام ابراہیم مصلى، ص۷۰، نمبر ۳۹۷) اس حدیث میں بھی بیت اللہ میں نماز پڑھنے کا تذکرہ ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۳۸۸) جب دیوار کی طرف چہرہ کر کے نماز پڑھ چکے تو اپنے رخسار کو اس پر رکھدے اور اللہ سے استغفار کرے اس کی حمد کرے۔
وجه : (ا) عن عبد الرحمن بن صفوان قال لما فتح رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مكة قلت لالبسن ثیابی و کانت داری على الطريق فلانظرن كيف يصنع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فانطلقت فرأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قد خرج من الكعبة هو و اصحابه قد استلموا البيت من الباب الى الحطيم وقد وضعوا خدودهم على البيت و رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وسطهم. (ابوداود شریف، باب الملتزم ص ۲۷۶، نمبر ۱۸۹۸)
ترجمه : (۱۳۸۹)، پھر ارکان کے پاس آئے ، استغفار کرے، حمد کرے تہلیل کرے تسبیح کرے، تکبیر کہے، اللہ تعالی سے جو چاہے دعا کرے، ظاہر و باطن سے جتنا ہو سکے ادب کو لازم پکڑے۔
تشریح : یہاں ارکان سے مراد حجر اسود ہے، یعنی حجر اسود کے پاس آئے اور استغفار وغیرہ کرے اور دعا کرے۔ اس کے لئے حدیث گزرچکی ہے۔
وجه : (۱) اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے . عن عمر و بن شعیب عن ابيه قال طفت مع عبد الله فلما جئنا دبر الكعبة قلت ألا تتعوذ ؟ قال نعوذ بالله من النار ثم مضى حتى استلم الحجر و اقام بين الركن و الباب فوضع صدره و وجهه و ذراعیه و كفيه هكذا و بسطهما بسطا ثم قال هكذا رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يفعله - ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب الملتزم، ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۱۸۹۹ رابن ماجه شریف، باب الملتزم ، ص ۴۲۹، نمبر ۲۹۶۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور
When he prays facing the wall, he places his cheek on it and seeks forgiveness and praises Allah. Then he goes to the corners, praises, says la ilaha illallah, glorifies, says takbir, asks Allah whatever he wishes, and adheres to etiquette outwardly and inwardly as much as possible. He places the door behind his back and walks until there is about three cubits between him and the wall in front of him, then he prays, aiming for the place where Bilal informed him that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed. There is no harm for anyone to pray in any part of the Kaaba they wish.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage presents the recommended acts (sunan) inside the Kaaba after entering and performing the first prayer. The author, a Hanafi jurist, details two actions: first, after praying facing the wall, one places their cheek on the wall, seeking forgiveness and praising Allah. This is based on the hadith of Abdur Rahman ibn Safwan who saw the Prophet and his companions place their cheeks on the Kaaba from the door to al-Hatim. Second, one goes to the 'arkan' (plural of rukn, meaning corner), which the commentator explains refers specifically to the Black Stone (al-Hajar al-Aswad). There, one engages in various forms of dhikr: praise (hamd), declaration of tawhid (tahlil), glorification (tasbih), takbir, and any personal supplication. The commentator stresses maintaining outward and inward respect. The passage also mentions that after this, one should pray two rak'ahs at a specific spot about three cubits from the wall in front, positioning the Kaaba door behind them. The location is the one indicated by Bilal in a hadith of Ibn Umar, where the Prophet prayed between two pillars on the left upon entering. However, the author clarifies that it is permissible to pray anywhere inside the Kaaba. The Hanafi school considers these actions as mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory, as the supporting evidence is from ahad hadith.

Key Terms
الاركان (al-arkan): The corners of the Kaaba; in this context, specifically the Black Stone corner (al-rukun al-yamani) where the Black Stone is placed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a pilgrim do immediately after praying inside the Kaaba, according to the passage?
A) Leave the Kaaba quickly
B) Place his cheek on the wall and seek forgiveness
C) Perform sajda al-tilawa
D) Recite Quran loudly

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that acts like placing the cheek on the Kaaba wall and supplicating at the corner are recommended (mustahabb) based on ahad hadith, not obligatory.

Green Pavement Not Prophet’s Prayer Place
Clarifying a specific historical location inside the Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the green pavement inside the Kaaba is not the Prophet’s prayer place and identify the correct location slightly to the left.

Core Idea
The green pavement is not the Prophet's prayer place; the true spot is slightly left.

Many people mistakenly believe that a specific green tile inside the Kaaba marks the spot where the Prophet prayed. This lesson clarifies the correct location based on authentic reports, ensuring that our knowledge of sacred spaces is accurate and free from common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the misconception
Recognize that some people claim the green pavement between the two pillars is where the Prophet prayed.
2
State the correction
The Hanafi text explicitly denies this claim: the green pavement is not the prayer place.
3
Locate the correct spot
The actual prayer place of the Prophet is slightly to the left of the green pavement.
This shows the importance of precise knowledge.
4
Appreciate the lesson’s value
Such clarifications protect against baseless traditions and uphold authentic practice.
Even a single spot can be subject to error; fiqh corrects it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۹۰) وليست البلاطة الخضراء التي بين العمودين مصلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم 
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۰) اور سبز فرش جو دو ستونوں کے درمیان ہے وہ نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کے نماز کی جگہ نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : بیت اللہ کے اندر دو ستونوں کے درمیان سبز فرش ہے ، لوگ کہتے ہیں اس جگہ حضور نے نماز پڑھی ہے لیکن یہ غلط ہے، بلکہ اس سے تھوڑا بائیں ہٹ کر حضور کی نماز کی جگہ ہے۔
The green pavement that is between the two pillars is not the prayer place of the Prophet, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This is a short but important clarification about the interior of the Kaaba. The author refutes a common misconception: the green tile or pavement located between two columns inside the Kaaba is falsely believed by some to be the exact spot where the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed his prayer. The author states that this is incorrect. The actual prayer place of the Prophet is slightly to the left of this green pavement. The Hanafi school affirms the authentic reports about the Prophet's prayer location and rejects baseless traditions. This is a ruling-statement that corrects a prevalent error, emphasizing the importance of factual accuracy in matters of ritual.

Key Terms
البلاطة الخضراء (al-balata al-khadra): A green stone or tile pavement inside the Kaaba, specifically between two columns (عمودين).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is the place of the Prophet's birth.

Key Takeaway
The green pavement inside the Kaaba is not the Prophet's prayer place; the authentic location is slightly to the left.

Refuting the Innovation of al-Urwat al-Wuthqa
Condemning a popular belief as innovation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the belief in 'al-urwat al-wuthqa' inside the Kaaba and identify why it is considered a bid'ah.

Core Idea
Calling a raised spot inside the Kaaba 'al-urwat al-wuthqa' is an innovation with no basis in Islam.

Pilgrims and visitors to the Kaaba sometimes attach special significance to a high place on its interior wall, calling it 'al-urwat al-wuthqa'. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on this belief, which declares it a false innovation. Understanding this ruling protects the sanctity of the House of Allah from unfounded practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object of the claim
Recognize what the common people refer to: a high spot on the interior wall of the Kaaba they call 'al-urwat al-wuthqa'.
2
Understand the claim itself
The claim is that this specific spot is 'the firm handle' (al-urwat al-wuthqa) implying special virtue or religious significance.
3
Receive the Hanafi ruling
The author states it is 'بدعة باطلة لا أصل لها' — a false innovation with no basis. Commit this phrase to memory.
4
Recognize the authority
This is the ruling of the Hanafi school as transmitted in reliable texts. It is based on the principle that any claim of religious merit without evidence is bid'ah.
5
Apply the lesson
When encountering similar claims about specific parts of the Kaaba or other sacred sites, apply the same test: is there authentic evidence? If not, reject it as bid'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۹۱) وما تقوله العامة من انة العروة الوثقى وهو موضع عال في جدار البيت بدعة باطلة لا اصل لها 
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۱) اور عوام جسے عروۃ وثقی کہتے ہیں جو بیت اللہ کی دیوار میں ایک بلند جگہ ہے اس کی کوئی اصل نہیں بلکہ بدعت باطلہ ہے۔ تشریح : بیت اللہ کے اندر دیوار میں ایک اونچی جگہ ہے ، لوگ اس کو عروۃ الوسقی [ مضبوط حلقہ ] کہتے ہیں اس کی کوئی اصل نہیں ہے، بیکار باتیں ہیں۔
And what the common people say that it is the firm handle (al-urwat al-wuthqa) — a high place on the wall of the Kaaba — is an innovation, false, having no basis.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage identifies and rejects a specific innovation (bid'ah). The general public erroneously calls a certain high spot on the interior wall of the Kaaba 'al-urwat al-wuthqa' (the firm handle), a term that originally refers to a stronghold or reliable support in the Quran (al-Baqarah 2:256). They attach special significance to it. The Hanafi author declares this belief to be a false innovation with no basis in the Quran, Sunnah, or the practice of the Salaf. This ruling serves to protect the sanctity of the Kaaba from superstition and unsubstantiated practices. The commentator explains that such claims are worthless.

Key Terms
العروة الوثقى (al-urwat al-wuthqa): A term used by common people for a high place inside the Kaaba wall; literally 'firm handle' or 'strong bond', but here a baseless designation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a confirmed sunnah
B) It is an innovation with no basis
C) It is recommended to touch it
D) It is mustahabb to pray there

Key Takeaway
Believing a specific spot inside the Kaaba is 'al-urwat al-wuthqa' is a baseless innovation (bid'ah) with no support from the Quran, Sunnah, or practice of the Salaf.

Prohibition of Exposing Awrah Inside the Kaaba: The Nail of Surrat al-Dunya
Ruling that exposing private parts at the nail is foolish and impermissible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exposing the awrah inside the Kaaba and explain why the practice of pressing the navel against the nail is haram.

Core Idea
Exposing awrah inside the Kaaba is haram – even if done out of reverence for a superstitious nail.

This passage addresses a false popular practice associated with a nail in the center of the Kaaba, which some call the 'navel of the world.' It rules that uncovering one's awrah to touch it is an act of ignorance, not knowledge, and is impermissible in the Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What exactly is being done? Some people uncover their private parts (awrah) and navel and place them on the nail.
2
Recognize the false belief
The nail is called 'surrat al-dunya' (navel of the world), a superstitious claim with no basis in the Shari'ah.
3
Understand the ruling
Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam describes it as 'an act of one who has no intellect, let alone knowledge.' This implies prohibition (haram) because it involves unnecessary exposure of awrah.
4
Apply the general principle
Exposing awrah unnecessarily is haram in fiqh, and this prohibition is not lifted by the sanctity of the place or superstitious intentions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۹۲) والمسمار الذى فى وسط البيت يُسمّونه سرّة الدنيا يكشف احدهم عورته وسرته ويـضـعـهـا عليه فعل من لا عقل له فضلا عن علم كما قاله الكمال.
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۲) اور وہ کیل جو بیت اللہ کے درمیان میں ہے جس کا لوگ سرۃ الدنیا ( دنیا کی ناف ) نام رکھتے ہیں بعض تو اپنا ستر اور ناف کھول کر اس پر رکھتے ہیں، بقول علامہ کمال کے یہ علم سے عاری اور عقل کے کورے لوگوں کا فعل ہے۔ تشریح : بیت اللہ کے درمیان کوئی کیل ہے، لوگ یہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ دنیا کی ناف ہے، دنیا کے بالکل بیچ کا حصہ ہے،اور پرانے زمانے میں بعض لوگ اس پر ناف کھول کر اور ستر کھول کر رکھتے تھے، یہ جاہلانہ رسم ہے، شریعت ایسی بیحیائی کی اجازت نہیں دیتی۔
And the nail that is in the middle of the Kaaba, they call it the navel of the world; some of them uncover their private parts and their navel and place it upon it — an act of one who has no intellect, let alone knowledge, as al-Kamal said.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage addresses a particularly objectionable practice. Inside the Kaaba, there is a nail on the floor that some people call 'surrat al-dunya' (the navel of the world), claiming incorrectly that it marks the center of the earth. The author condemns those who, in misguided reverence, uncover their private parts (awrah) and navel and place them against this nail. The Hanafi scholar al-Kamal ibn al-Humam (commonly known as al-Kamal) is quoted as saying that such an act is devoid of intellect, let alone religious knowledge. The commentator adds that this is a foolish custom from ancient times and that the Shari'ah does not permit such indecency. The ruling is that this practice is haram (prohibited) because it involves exposing one's awrah unnecessarily without any valid basis.

Key Terms
المسمار (al-mismar): A nail fixed in the floor at the center of the Kaaba, falsely believed to be the world's navel.
سرّة الدنيا (surrat al-dunya): A name given by laymen to the nail, meaning 'navel of the world'; considered superstitious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Mustahabb
B) Mubah
C) Haram
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Exposing the awrah for a superstitious practice like pressing the navel against the nail is haram and represents an ignorant custom not sanctioned by the Shari'ah.

Recommended Exit from the Kaaba after Tawaf al-Wada'
Ruling on recommended exit etiquette after farewell tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended manner of leaving the Kaaba after tawaf al-wada', including the direction, posture, and emotional state, and distinguish between the ruling of tawaf al-wada' (wajib) and the recommended exit etiquette (sunnah).

Core Idea
Exit the Kaaba backwards, facing it, weeping — a sunnah expressing love and reverence.

After completing Hajj or Umrah, a pilgrim performs tawaf al-wada'. This lesson explains the recommended etiquette for departing from the Holy Sanctuary, as derived from Hanafi fiqh. The author describes a specific posture and emotional state that embodies the pilgrim's deep attachment to the Kaaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action
Recognize that this lesson covers the recommended manner of exiting the Kaaba after performing tawaf al-wada'.
Tawaf al-wada' itself is wajib in the Hanafi school.
2
Note the ruling level
The author uses 'مناسب' (appropriate) indicating a sunnah muakkadah, not a wajib. This is a recommended practice.
It is not sinful to omit, but fulfilling it completes the spiritual experience.
3
Describe the physical manner
The pilgrim should walk backwards, keeping his face towards the Kaaba, until he exits the mosque.
This ensures he faces the Kaaba as long as possible.
4
Describe the emotional state
He should be weeping or at least feigning tears, expressing sorrow at leaving the Sacred House.
This shows profound love and reverence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۹۳) واذا اراد العود الى اهله 
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۳) اور جب اپنے اہل کی طرف واپسی کا ارادہ ہو تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ طواف وداع کے بعد اس طرح لوٹے کہ چہرہ بیت اللہ کی طرف ہو اور پیچھے کی جانب چلتا جائے ، روتا ہوا یا رونے والوں کی شکل بنا تا ہوا بیت اللہ کی جدائی میں حسرت کرتا ہوا چلے ، اور اسی حال میں مسجد حرام سے باہر نکلے۔
And when he intends to return to his family...
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage describes the recommended manner of departing from the Masjid al-Haram when one intends to return home after completing Hajj or Umrah. The author, using the phrase 'مناسب یہ ہے' (it is appropriate), indicates this is a sunnah or mustahabb action. The recommendation is to perform tawaf al-wada' (farewell tawaf) and then leave the Kaaba by walking backwards, facing the Kaaba, so that one's face remains towards it until exiting. One should be weeping or at least feigning tears, expressing deep sorrow at parting from the Sacred House. This displays the profound love and reverence the believer should have for Allah's house. The Hanafi school considers this part of the etiquettes of tawaf and departure.

Key Terms
طواف وداع (tawaf al-wada'): The farewell circumambulation performed before leaving Mecca.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Walk normally facing the door
B) Walk backwards while facing the Kaaba and weeping
C) Run quickly
D) Prostrate at the door

Key Takeaway
The recommended exit from the Kaaba after tawaf al-wada' is to walk backwards facing it, with a weeping heart.

The Green Pavement Is Not the Prophet's Prayer Place
Factual correction of a common misconception about a location inside the Ka'bah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct location of the Prophet's prayer inside the Ka'bah and explain why the common belief about the green pavement is incorrect.

Core Idea
The green pavement inside the Ka'bah is NOT the Prophet's prayer place; the true spot lies slightly left.

Many pilgrims and visitors to the Ka'bah mistakenly believe that the green tile between the two pillars marks where the Prophet ﷺ prayed. This lesson corrects that error based on authentic historical reports. Understanding such details helps preserve the accuracy of our sacred heritage and prevents the spread of unfounded legends.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Find the statement in the text that describes the common belief: that the green pavement between the two pillars is the Prophet's prayer place.
The text explicitly says 'ليس مصلى النبي' (not the Prophet's prayer place).
2
Locate the correct information
Read the Urdu commentary to discover the actual location: slightly left of the green pavement.
The text says 'تھوڑا بائیں ہٹ کر' (slightly to the left).
3
Note the reasoning
Understand that this correction is based on historical knowledge, not fiqh deduction. The source relies on authentic reports about the Prophet's actions.
No legal reasoning (qiyas etc.) is given; it is a factual report.
4
Recognize the importance of accuracy
Realize that spreading unverified claims about sacred sites can lead to bid'ah or disrespect. The Hanafi school emphasizes authentic transmission in matters of history and ritual.
This lesson is a reminder to verify such claims before accepting them.

Source Text

(۱۳۹۰) وليست البلاطة الخضراء التي بين العمودين مصلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم

Commentary
This is a factual correction of a common misconception. The text states that the green tile between the two pillars inside the Ka'bah is not the spot where the Prophet ﷺ prayed. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the actual prayer spot is slightly to the left. This ruling is based on historical knowledge and serves to prevent false beliefs and practices. It is a reminder that not every legend about sacred sites is authentic.

Key Terms
بلاطة (balāṭah): A stone pavement, specifically the green tile inside the Ka'bah
مصلى (muṣallā): Place of prayer; here referring to a specific spot where the Prophet prayed

Refuting the 'Urwat al-Wuthqa Innovation
Ruling refuting a popular belief about a Ka'bah structure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the belief in a physical 'urwat al-wuthqa on the Ka'bah is a baseless innovation and explain why it is rejected.

Core Idea
The 'urwat al-wuthqa is a Quranic metaphor for faith, not a physical place on the Ka'bah.

This passage addresses a common misconception among pilgrims who associate a high spot on the Ka'bah's interior wall with the Quranic term 'urwat al-wuthqa. The text declares this belief a baseless innovation, emphasizing that the term in the Quran is metaphorical, not literal. Understanding this helps protect the purity of Islamic worship from unfounded practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
What do the common people say about the high place on the Ka'bah wall? They claim it is the 'urwat al-wuthqa.
The claim is about a physical location, not a concept.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on this claim
The text categorically calls this claim a 'baseless innovation with no origin' (بدعة باطلة لا أصل لها).
This is a strong condemnation, indicating prohibition.
3
Analyze the key term 'urwat al-wuthqa
Literally, 'urwah means loop or handle, and wuthqa means strong or reliable. In the Quran, it refers to the firm handhold of faith, not a physical object.
The Urdu commentary explains the linguistic meaning, reinforcing the metaphorical usage.
4
Explain why this belief is a bid'ah
It has no basis in the Quran, Sunnah, or early practice. Believing in a physical 'urwat al-wuthqa on the Ka'bah adds to religion without authority, making it a rejected innovation.
Hanafi methodology: any practice not rooted in authentic sources is bid'ah.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
A Muslim should not propagate or act upon this belief. If asked, they should correct it and explain the true meaning of 'urwat al-wuthqa.
This protects the sanctity of Hajj from unwarranted innovations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۹۱) وما تقوله العامة من انة العروة الوثقى وهو موضع عال في جدار البيت بدعة باطلة لا اصل لها
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۱) اور عوام جسے عروۃ وھی کہتے ہیں جو بیت اللہ کی دیوار میں ایک بلند جگہ ہے اس کی کوئی اصل نہیں بلکہ بدعت باطلہ ہے۔ تشریح : بیت اللہ کے اندر دیوار میں ایک اونچی جگہ ہے ، لوگ اس کو عروۃ الوثقی [ مضبوط حلقہ ] کہتے ہیں اس کی کوئی اصل نہیں ہے، بیکار باتیں ہیں۔ لغت : عروۃ: لوٹے کا دستہ، یہاں مراد ہے حلقہ ۔ ٹھی: وثیقہ سے مشتق ہے، معاہدہ۔ عروۃ وثقی ، مضبوط حلقہ مضبوط سہارا۔

Vocabulary: عروۃ: handle of a pot, here meaning loop. وثقی: derived from wathīqah, pact. 'Urwat wuthqa: strong loop, strong support.

This ruling debunks another common misconception: that a specific high spot on the interior wall of the Ka'bah is the 'urwat al-wuthqa (the strong handhold mentioned in the Quran). The text categorically states that this belief is a baseless innovation (bid'ah bāṭilah). The Urdu commentary reinforces that it has no authentic source. This is a typical Hanafi approach of safeguarding the faith by rejecting unfounded practices.

Key Terms

بدعة باطلة (bid‘ah bāṭilah): A baseless innovation in religion with no foundation

The Prohibition of Exposing 'Awrah for the Nail in the Ka'bah
Condemns an improper practice related to a nail in the Ka'bah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the practice of exposing the 'awrah to the nail inside the Ka'bah and identify the elements that make it prohibited.

Core Idea
Uncovering the 'awrah for veneration of a nail is a haram innovation with no basis in Shari'ah.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah condemns a practice associated with a nail in the Ka'bah known as 'surrat al-dunya'. Some people would expose their navel and private parts and place them on the nail. The author, citing al-Kamal, declares this an act of the ignorant. In this lesson, we will explore why this act is prohibited in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Elements
Determine what the text describes: a person uncovers their private parts (awrah) and navel and places them on a specific nail in the Ka'bah.
The 'awrah for men in Hanafi is from navel to knees.
2
Determine the Ruling from the Text
The text explicitly calls this an act of those devoid of intellect and knowledge, and the commentary says Shari'ah does not permit it. Thus, the ruling is haram.
The ruling is based on general principles of modesty and prohibition of bid'ah.
3
Identify the Basis of Prohibition
The prohibition stems from the obligation to cover the 'awrah (fard) and the general prohibition of innovations that lead to shamelessness.
No specific Quran or hadith is cited in the text; the ruling is derived from qiyas on broader principles.
4
Contrast with Proper Practice
During Tawaf or inside the Ka'bah, one must remain covered and avoid any act that violates modesty or has no basis in Shari'ah.
The Ka'bah is a place of respect, not for superstitious practices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۹۲) والمسمار الذى فى وسط البيت يُسمّونه سرّة الدنيا يكشف احدهم عورته وسرته ويـضـعـهـا عليه فعل من لا عقل له فضلا عن علم كما قاله الكمال.
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۲) اور وہ کیل جو بیت اللہ کے درمیان میں ہے جس کا لوگ سرۃ الدنیا ( دنیا کی ناف ) نام رکھتے ہیں بعض تو اپنا ستر اور ناف کھول کر اس پر رکھتے ہیں، بقول علامہ کمال کے یہ علم سے عاری اور عقل کے کورے لوگوں کا فعل ہے۔ تشریح : بیت اللہ کے درمیان کوئی کیل ہے، لوگ یہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ دنیا کی ناف ہے، دنیا کے بالکل بیچ کا حصہ ہے، اور پرانے زمانے میں بعض لوگ اس پر ناف کھول کر اور ستر کھول کر رکھتے تھے، یہ جاہلانہ رسم ہے، شریعت ایسی بیحیائی کی اجازت نہیں دیتی۔ لغت : مسمار: کیل۔ سرة : ناف سرۃ الدنیا دینا کی ناف، دنیا کی بیچ ۔ عورة: شرمگاہ ،ستر ۔

According to Allamah Kamal, this is the act of people devoid of intellect, let alone knowledge. Explanation: There is a nail in the middle of the Ka'bah. People say it is the navel of the world, the exact center. In ancient times, some people would uncover their navel and private parts and place them on it. This is an ignorant custom; the Shari'ah does not permit such shamelessness. Vocabulary: مسمار: nail. سرة: navel. سرۃ الدنیا: navel of the world, center of the world. عورة: private parts, satr.

Commentary
This passage condemns an inappropriate act associated with a nail inside the Ka'bah. According to the text, some people would expose their private parts and place them on the nail, calling it 'surrat al-dunya'. The author (citing al-Kamal) declares this to be an act of those devoid of intellect and knowledge. The commentary explains that this is an ignorant custom that Shari'ah does not permit, as it involves uncovering the 'awrah unnecessarily and is a bid'ah. The Hanafi ruling is that such acts are haram (impermissible) due to the violation of modesty and lack of basis.
