Recommended Manner of Exiting the Ka'bah After Tawaf al-Wada'
Describes recommended adab of exiting after farewell tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mustahabb) manner of exiting the Masjid al-Haram after tawaf al-wada' and explain the evidence from the two athar.

Core Idea
Walk backwards facing the Ka'bah, crying or showing regret – that is the sunnah adab of farewell.

After completing the wajib tawaf al-wada', the Hanafi school recommends a specific manner of departing from the Ka'bah. This adab expresses deep love and reverence for the House, and is supported by narrations from early authorities. In this lesson you will learn the precise practice described by the classical scholars and the reasons behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The act is exiting the Masjid al-Haram after performing tawaf al-wada'. Tawaf al-wada' itself is wajib (obligatory) for a pilgrim leaving Mecca. This lesson deals with the recommended way of performing the exit, not with the obligation of the tawaf.
Remember: the adab (etiquette) does not affect the validity of the tawaf.
2
List the elements of the recommended manner
The text prescribes three elements: (1) walking backwards, (2) keeping one's face towards the Ka'bah, and (3) crying or pretending to cry out of regret for leaving the House. Continue in this state until you leave the mosque.
These elements are mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.
3
Examine the first evidence (Ibrahim an-Nakha'i)
The Urdu commentary cites an athar from Ibrahim that leaning one's back against the Ka'bah or turning one's back to it is makruh (disliked). Thus, facing the Ka'bah while retreating avoids this disliked action and is better.
Ibrahim an-Nakha'i was a prominent tabi'i. His saying is considered a qawl sahabi in Hanafi usul, though not as strong as marfu' hadith.
4
Examine the second evidence (Tawus)
Another athar from Tawus states that looking at the Ka'bah is an act of worship. Therefore, one should exit while looking at it, thereby gaining reward from the last look.
Tawus ibn Kaysan was also a tabi'i. The athar is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
5
Distinguish between wajib and mustahabb
Tawaf al-wada' itself is wajib; if a pilgrim leaves without performing it, a dam (sacrifice) becomes due. However, the manner of exiting the mosque after the tawaf is merely recommended. If one exits normally, the tawaf is still valid, but the recommended reward is missed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۹۳) ينبغي ان ينصرف بعد طوافه للوداع وهو يمشى الى ورائه ووجهه الى البيت باكيا او متباكيا متحسّرا على فراق البيـت حـتـى يخرج من المسجد
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۳) اور جب اپنے اہل کی طرف واپسی کا ارادہ ہو تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ طواف وداع کے بعد اس طرح لوٹے کہ چہرہ بیت اللہ کی طرف ہو اور پیچھے کی جانب چلتا جائے ، روتا ہوا یا رونے والوں کی شکل بنا تا ہوا بیت اللہ کی جدائی میں حسرت کرتا ہوا چلے ، اور اسی حال میں مسجد حرام سے باہر نکلے۔ تشريح : طواف وداع کے بعد جب گھر واپس ہونے لگے تو چہرہ بیت اللہ کی طرف ہو اور پیچھے ہٹتا جائے اور چلتا جائے، بیت اللہ کی جدائیگی پر روتا جائے یا کم سے کم رونے والوں کی طرح شکل بنائے ، اس طرح پیچھے ہٹتے ہوئے مسجد حرام سے نکلے۔ وجه : (1) اس اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے . عن ابراهیم قال يكره أن يسند الانسان ظهره الى الكعبة يستدبرها ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی الرجل لسند ظهر و الی الکعبة ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۹۱ نمبر ۱۵۴۲۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بیت اللہ کی طرف پیٹھ کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ اس لئے بیت اللہ کی طرف چہرہ کرتے ہوئے پیچھے ہے تو بہتر ہے (۲) عن طاوس قال : النظر الى البيت عبادة و الطواف بالبيت صلاة (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، باب فی فضل النظر الى البيت، ج ثالث ص ۱۳۲۷، نمبر ۱۴۷۵۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بیت اللہ کی طرف دیکھنا عبادت ہے، اس لئے بیت اللہ کو دیکھتے ہوئے باہر نکلے ۔ لغت : عود: واپس لوٹنا۔ وراء: پیچھے کی طرف۔ با کیا: روتے ہوئے، متبا کیا: رونے کی شکل بناتے ہوئے متحسر : حسرت سے مشتق ہے، افسوس کرتے ہوئے ۔
(1393) He should depart after his tawaf for farewell, walking backwards with his face towards the House, crying or pretending to cry, regretful over leaving the House, until he exits the mosque. Translation: (1393) And when he intends to return to his family, it is appropriate to depart after tawaf al-wada' in such a way that his face is towards the Ka'bah and he walks backwards, crying or making the appearance of crying, feeling regret at leaving the Ka'bah, and in this state he exits the Masjid al-Haram. Explanation: After tawaf al-wada', when leaving to go home, he should keep his face towards the Ka'bah and walk backwards, crying or at least making a crying face, and exit the Masjid al-Haram while retreating. Reason: (1) This is indicated by the athar from Ibrahim: 'It is makruh for a person to lean his back against the Ka'bah or to turn his back to it' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). This athar states that turning one's back to the Ka'bah is makruh. Therefore, keeping face towards the Ka'bah while walking backwards is better. (2) From Tawus: 'Looking at the House is worship, and tawaf around the House is prayer' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). This athar states that looking at the Ka'bah is worship, so one should exit while looking at it. Vocabulary: عود: returning. وراء: backwards. باکيا: crying. متباکيا: pretending to cry. متحسر: derived from hasrah, regretting.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage gives the recommended (yambaghi = sunnah/adab) manner of leaving the Ka'bah after performing the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-wada'). The text prescribes walking backwards facing the Ka'bah, crying or appearing to cry, and expressing regret at leaving the sacred house until exiting the mosque. The Urdu commentary provides two evidences: (1) an athar from Ibrahim that it is makruh to turn one's back to the Ka'bah, so facing it while walking backwards is better; (2) an athar from Tawus that looking at the Ka'bah is worship, so one should keep looking. These are not primary proofs from Quran and Sunnah but rely on narrations from early authorities (athar), which in Hanafi usul are considered as evidence when not conflicting with stronger sources. The recommended act is an expression of love and respect for the Ka'bah.

Key Terms
ينبغي (yanbaghī): It is appropriate/recommended; indicates a sunnah or mustahabb action
طواف الوداع (ṭawāf al-wadā‘): Farewell tawaf, the final circumambulation before leaving Mecca
متباكيا (mutabākiyan): Pretending to cry; making the appearance of crying as an expression of regret
أثر (athar): A narration from a Companion or early authority (tabi'i), often used as supporting evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended manner of exiting the Masjid al-Haram after tawaf al-wada'?
A) Walk normally facing away from the Ka'bah.
B) Walk backwards facing the Ka'bah, crying or pretending to cry.
C) Run quickly to show zeal.
D) Exit without any specific manner.

Key Takeaway
After tawaf al-wada', the sunnah adab is to exit the mosque walking backwards facing the Ka'bah, crying or showing regret, out of love and reverence for the House.

Exiting Mecca via Bab Bani Shaybah and al-Thaniyah al-Sufla
Specifies the recommended route for leaving Mecca after Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended route for leaving Mecca after Hajj and identify the hadith evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The Prophet entered Mecca from the upper pass and exited from the lower pass; following this is a recommended Sunnah.

Completing Hajj includes leaving Mecca with the same devotion you entered. The Prophet ﷺ established a specific route for departure—one that mirrors the entrance route. This lesson explains the recommended exit path and the hadith that guides it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine whether the instruction to exit via a specific route is obligatory (wajib) or recommended (sunnah). The passage uses 'yakhruj' in an imperative form, but the context and evidence show it is a recommended practice (mustahabb).
Hanafi fiqh classifies following the Prophet's specific routes as sunnah, not wajib.
2
Locate the recommended route
Note the two elements: exiting from Bab Bani Shaybah (a gate of Masjid al-Haram) and proceeding via al-Thaniyah al-Sufla (the lower mountain pass). Understand that this contrasts with the entrance route (al-Thaniyah al-'Ulya).
Bab Bani Shaybah is located near the lower pass (al-Thaniyah al-Sufla).
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the hadith from Ibn 'Umar: the Prophet entered from al-Thaniyah al-'Ulya and exited from al-Thaniyah al-Sufla. This is the primary evidence. Confirm it is sahih (from Bukhari and Nasa'i).
The hadith establishes the precedent; following it is considered emulation (ittiba') of the Prophet.
4
Understand the wisdom
Reflect on why a specific route is recommended. It ensures the pilgrim's journey mirrors the Prophet's and adds a spiritual dimension to the departure. It also distinguishes the sacred precincts by using distinct entry and exit points.
This practice is part of the Hajj rituals and reinforces the Sunnah.
5
Connect to the Hajj sequence
Recall that the pilgrim entered Mecca at the beginning of Hajj from the upper pass. Now, after completing all rites (including tawaf al-wada'), they depart from the lower pass. This completes the symbolic journey.
This symmetry is a recommended completion of the Hajj experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۹۴) ويخرج من مكة من باب بني شيبة من الثنية السفلى.
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۴) اور مکہ سے باب بنی شیبہ سے ثنیہ سفلی سے ہوتا ہوا نکلے۔ تشریح : باب بنی هيت تکیه سفلی کی طرف ہے اس لئے باب بنی شیبہ سے مسجد حرام سے باہر آئے ، اور ثنیہ سفلی سے مکہ مکرمہ سے باہر آئے۔ یہ آدمی حج کے لئے شروع میں ثنیہ علیا سے مکہ مکرمہ میں داخل ہوا تھا اب تنبیہ سفلی سے باہر آئے۔ وجه : (۱) عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله الله يدخل مكة من الثنية العليا و يخرج من الثنية السفلى ۔ بخاری شریف، باب من این یدخل مکه؟ ، ص ۲۵۶، نمبر ۱۵۷۵ رنسائی شریف ، باب من این یدخل مکته ، ص ۱۳۹۵، نمبر ۲۸۶۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ثنیہ علیا سے مکہ مکرمہ میں داخل ہو اور ثنیہ سفلی سے باہر نکلے۔ لغت : ثنیہ گھائی ، شبیه علیا مکہ مکرمہ میں اونچائی کی جانب کی گھائی۔ یہ سفلی بجلی گھاٹی ، آج کل اس کو مسفلہ، کہتے ہیں، اسی طرف باب بنی شیبہ ہے۔
(1394) And he should exit from Mecca from Bab Bani Shaybah via al-Thaniyah al-Sufla. Translation: (1394) And he should leave Mecca from Bab Bani Shaybah via al-Thaniyah al-Sufla. Explanation: Bab Bani Shaybah is towards al-Thaniyah al-Sufla, so he should come out of the Masjid al-Haram from Bab Bani Shaybah, and leave Mecca from al-Thaniyah al-Sufla. He entered Mecca at the beginning of Hajj from al-Thaniyah al-'Ulya, so now he should exit from al-Thaniyah al-Sufla. Evidence: (1) From Ibn 'Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ would enter Mecca from al-Thaniyah al-'Ulya and exit from al-Thaniyah al-Sufla.' (Bukhari, chapter on from where to enter Mecca; Nasa'i). This hadith states that he entered from al-Thaniyah al-'Ulya and exited from al-Thaniyah al-Sufla. Vocabulary: ثنیہ: mountain pass. علیا: the upper. سفلی: the lower. Today, al-Sufla is called Musfalah, and in that direction is Bab Bani Shaybah.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage outlines the recommended route for leaving Mecca after completing Hajj. The text instructs exiting from Bab Bani Shaybah (a gate of the Masjid al-Haram) and proceeding via al-Thaniyah al-Sufla (the lower mountain pass). The Urdu commentary explains that the pilgrim entered Mecca from al-Thaniyah al-'Ulya (the upper pass) at the start of Hajj, following the Sunnah, and now should exit from the lower pass. The evidence is a hadith from Ibn 'Umar confirming the Prophet's practice of entering from one pass and exiting from another. In Hanafi fiqh, following the Prophet's routes is mustahabb (recommended), as it shows emulation (ittiba') and is part of the Hajj rituals.

Key Terms
ثنية: A mountain pass; specifically al-Thaniyah al-'Ulya (upper) and al-Thaniyah al-Sufla (lower) near Mecca
باب بني شيبة: A gate of the Masjid al-Haram named after the Banu Shaybah tribe

Women's Dress in Hajj: Head Covering and Face Veil
States the rule for women's dress during Hajj, differing from men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two exceptions to the general rule that women perform Hajj like men, and explain the proper manner of face covering for women in ihram according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Women in ihram cover their heads and may cover their faces with a cloth that does not touch the skin, using a support.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text clarifies how women's dress during Hajj differs from men's. While the basic actions are the same, two key exceptions relate to modesty: women must keep their heads covered, and when covering the face, they must do so in a way that avoids direct contact. Understanding these rules ensures the validity of a woman's ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Note that the rule begins with an overarching principle: 'The woman in all actions of Hajj is like the man.' This establishes equality in rituals, but exceptions follow.
The exceptions are based on the unique rulings for women's 'awrah.
2
Spot the first exception
The text says: 'she does not uncover her head'. Unlike men, who are required to be bareheaded in ihram, women must cover their hair. This is wajib (obligatory) for her.
If a woman uncovers her head intentionally, she must pay fidya (compensation).
3
Spot the second exception with its condition
The second exception: 'she lets down over her face a cloth such that underneath it is a stick like a dome that prevents the cloth from touching the face.' She may cover her face, but the cloth must not touch the skin.
The 'stick' (عود) is a frame or support to keep the cloth away. Using a hand or a cap can also work.
4
Understand the rationale
The condition prevents the covering from becoming a prohibited face veil (niqab) that touches the face, which is not allowed in ihram. At the same time, it allows a woman to conceal her face from non-mahram men when needed.
This balances the prohibition of covering the face entirely (which would invalidate ihram) with the need for modesty.
5
Apply the ruling
Summarize: A woman in ihram must wear a head cover (like a hijab) and may wear a loose cloth over her face that does not touch the skin, using a support. If she covers her face directly or uncovers her head, she would need to offer fidya.
This ruling applies throughout the state of ihram, including during tawaf and sa'y.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۹۵) والـمـرأة في جميع افعال الحج كالرجل غير انها لا تكشف رأسها وتسدل على
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۵) عورت حج کے تمام افعال میں مرد کی طرح ہے مگر یہ کہ اپنے سرکو نہ کھولے۔ اور اپنے چہرے پر کپڑا ڈالے گی اس طرح کہ اس کے نیچے لکڑی ہو قبہ کی طرح ہو جو کپڑے کو چہرے پر لگ جانے سے مانع ہو
تشریح جس طرح احکام مردوں پر لازم ہیں اسی طرح عورتوں پر بھی لازم ہیں۔ البتہ جہاں ان کے ستر یا نسوانیت کے خلاف ہے وہاں عورتوں کا مسئلہ مردوں سے الگ ہے۔ اسی میں یہے۔ مسائل ہیں جو ذکر کئے جارہے ہیں۔
[Arabic fragment: And the woman in all actions of Hajj is like the man, except that she does not uncover her head and she lets down over...] Translation: (1395) A woman in all actions of Hajj is like a man, except that she does not uncover her head, and she will put cloth over her face in such a way that there is a stick underneath like a dome that prevents the cloth from touching the face. Explanation: Just as rulings are binding on men, similarly they are binding on women. However, where it is against their modesty or femininity, women's rulings are different from men. Among these are the issues being mentioned.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage establishes the general principle that women perform all actions of Hajj similarly to men, with two specific exceptions: (1) they do not uncover their heads (i.e., they must cover their hair, unlike men who are required to be bareheaded in ihram), and (2) they cover their faces with a cloth, but in a manner that prevents the cloth from touching the face, typically using a stick or frame (like a dome) to hold it away. This is to avoid violating the prohibition of covering the face during ihram. The Hanafi ruling: for women in ihram, it is impermissible to wear a face veil (niqab) that touches the face, so they may drape a cloth over the face using a support to keep it away. This is based on hadith that women in ihram should not wear niqab or gloves, but may cover their faces with a cloth when non-mahram men are present, provided it does not touch the skin. The commentary emphasizes that the basic equality of men and women in Hajj rulings is maintained, except where modesty or femininity necessitates a difference.

Key Terms
لا تكشف رأسها (lā takshif ra’sahā): She does not uncover her head; women must cover their hair during ihram
تسدل على وجهها ثوبا (tusdil ‘alā wajhihā thawban): She lets down a cloth over her face; i.e., covers her face with a veil
عود (‘ūd): A stick used as a frame to keep the cloth away from the face

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Women perform all actions differently.
B) Women do not uncover their heads and cover their face with a cloth on a stick.
C) Women must uncover their faces while men cover theirs.
D) Women cannot perform tawaf.

Key Takeaway
Women in ihram must cover their heads and may cover their faces with a cloth that does not touch the skin, using a support to avoid the prohibition of direct face covering.

Manner of Farewell Tawaf and Exiting Mecca
Ruling on performing farewell tawaf and exiting the mosque and Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the farewell tawaf and describe the sunnah method of exiting Mecca, citing the relevant proof.

Core Idea
The farewell tawaf is wajib; the manner of exiting Mecca is sunnah based on the Prophet's practice.

In this passage, we learn the etiquette of leaving the Kaaba after completing the farewell tawaf. The pilgrim is instructed to demonstrate deep reverence by walking backwards, facing the Kaaba, and departing through a specific gate and pass. This practice is rooted in the actions of the Prophet ﷺ and the early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is the farewell tawaf and the manner of exiting. The farewell tawaf is wajib; the manner is sunnah muakkadah.
The distinction between wajib and sunnah is critical in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's entering and exiting routes.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Nasa'i, ahad riwayah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this proof indicate the ruling? The Prophet's action is a demonstration of sunnah; it shows the recommended method but does not indicate obligation.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates sunnah unless there is a qarina for wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Yes, the Shafi'i school holds the farewell tawaf as sunnah, not wajib.
This ikhtilaf affects whether a dam (penalty) is required for omission.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The Hanafi school considers the farewell tawaf wajib based on other evidences; the exiting manner is sunnah as per the hadith.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ينبغي ان ينصرف بعد طوافه للوداع وهو يمشى الى ورائه ووجهه الى البيت باكيا او متباكيا متحسّرا على فراق البيـت حـتـى يخرج من المسجد (۱۳۹۴) ويخرج من مكة من باب بني شيبة من الثنية السفلى. (۱۳۹۵) عن ابراهيم قال يكره أن يسند الانسان ظهره الى الكعبة يستدبرها (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ) وعن طاوس قال: النظر الى البيت عبادة والطواف بالبيت صلاة (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة) وعن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله ﷺ يدخل مكة من الثنية العليا ويخرج من الثنية السفلى (بخاری، نسائی)
He should depart after his farewell tawaf walking backwards with his face towards the House, weeping or pretending to weep, grieving over separation from the House, until he leaves the mosque (1394). And he leaves Mecca from the Gate of Bani Shaybah via the lower mountain pass (1395). From Ibrahim: he said it is disliked for a person to lean his back against the Kaaba turning his back to it. From Tawus: he said looking at the House is worship and tawaf around the House is prayer. From Ibn Umar: he said the Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to enter Mecca from the upper pass and exit from the lower pass.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs regarding the etiquette of leaving after the farewell tawaf. First, the pilgrim should walk backwards facing the Kaaba until exiting the mosque, expressing sorrow at leaving the sacred precincts. This is based on an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that it is disliked to turn one's back to the Kaaba, and from Tawus that looking at the Kaaba is worship. Second, the pilgrim should exit Mecca specifically from the Gate of Bani Shaybah via the lower mountain pass (Thaniyah Sufla), as per the hadith of Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's ﷺ practice. This is the established sunnah.

Key Terms
طواف الوداع (tawaf al-wada'): The farewell circumambulation performed before leaving Mecca after completing Hajj.
الثنية السفلى (al-thaniyah al-sufla): The lower mountain pass through which one exits Mecca, located near the Gate of Bani Shaybah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The farewell tawaf is wajib in the Hanafi school, and the sunnah is to exit walking backwards through the Gate of Bani Shaybah via the lower pass.

Women's Specific Rulings in Hajj
Rulings specific to women during Hajj: covering, face veil, voice, and pace.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four specific actions in which women differ from men during Hajj and apply the Hanafi ruling for each.

Core Idea
Women in Hajj are like men except in modesty: cover head, veil face gently, lower voice, walk normally.

The source passage outlines four key differences for women in Hajj, derived from hadith and the practice of the Companions. Understanding these rules ensures that women perform Hajj correctly while maintaining the modesty required in ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four differences
Read the passage and list the four actions where women differ from men: head covering, face veil, voice level during talbiyah, and pace during tawaf/sa'ee.
These are the specific exceptions to the general rule that women are like men in Hajj.
2
Find the dalil for each ruling
For each difference, locate the hadith or athar cited. The main evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The ihram of a woman is in her face', and the practice of Aisha and Ali.
The hadiths are from Darqutni, Bayhaqi, Abu Dawud, and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Understand the illa (reason)
The underlying cause for these differences is modesty and avoiding fitna. Women must cover the body except face, and refrain from actions that attract attention.
The illa explains why raml and loud voice are prohibited for women.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a scholarly difference on whether women should raise their voice in talbiyah. Hanafis prohibit loud voice, while other schools allow it. The Hanafi position is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and the practice of Aisha.
The ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference of ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمرأة في جميع افعال الحج كالرجل غير انها لا تكشف رأسها وتسدل على وجهها شيئا تحته عيدان كالقبة تمنع مسّه بالغطاء (۱۳۹۶) ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية (۱۳۹۷) ولا ترمل ولا تهرول في السعى بين الميلين الاخضرين بل تمشى على هيئتها في جميع السعى بين الصفا والمروة. عن ابن عمر ان النبي عليه السلام قال ليس على المرأة احرام الا في وجهها (دارقطني، بيقهى) وعن عائشة قالت كان الركبان يمرون بنا ونحن مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاذا محرمات حاذوا بنا سدلت احدانا جلبابها من رأسها على وجهها فاذا جاوزونا كشفناه (أبو داؤد، ابن ماجه) وان عليا كان ينهي النساء عن النقاب و من حرم و لكن يسدلن الثوب عن وجوههن سدلا (مصنف ابن ابی شيبة) وعن ابن عمر قال لا تصعد المرأة فوق الصفا والمروة ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية (دارقطني، بيقهى) وعن ابن عمر قال ليس على النساء رمل بالبيت ولا بين الصفا والمروة (دارقطني)
The woman in all actions of Hajj is like the man except that she does not uncover her head, and she lets down over her face something with sticks underneath like a dome that prevents the covering from touching it (1396). And she does not raise her voice in talbiyah (1397). And she does not do raml nor jog between the two green markers, but she walks at her normal pace in all the sa'ee between Safa and Marwah. From Ibn Umar that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'The ihram of a woman is in her face.' From Aisha: she said 'Riders would pass by us while we were with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ; when they came near, one of us would let down her cloak from her head over her face, and when they passed we would uncover it.' And that Ali used to forbid women from the niqab and from covering the face in ihram, but they should let down the cloth over their faces loosely. From Ibn Umar: he said 'The woman should not ascend above Safa and Marwah nor raise her voice in talbiyah.' From Ibn Umar: he said 'There is no raml for women around the House nor between Safa and Marwah.'
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings for women performing Hajj, supported by hadith and athar. The general principle is that women are like men in all Hajj actions except where modesty or fitna dictate otherwise. First, women must cover their heads in ihram (unlike men who uncover). For the face, they should let down a cloth with a structure (like a small dome) so it does not touch the face, based on the hadith 'her ihram is in her face' meaning it should remain uncovered but screened. The practice of Aisha confirms this. Second, women do not raise their voices in talbiyah to avoid fitna. Third, women do not perform raml (quick, proud walk) in tawaf nor jog between the green markers in sa'ee; they walk normally throughout, as these actions were prescribed for men to show strength. All these rulings are established from the Prophet's ﷺ practice and the actions of the Companions.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, involving specific dress and prohibitions.
رمل (raml): A quick, brisk walk with short steps and chest out, performed by men in the first three circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They do not walk, they are carried
B) They walk normally without jogging between the green markers
C) They run faster than men
D) They do not perform sa'ee at all

Key Takeaway
Women in Hajj follow men's rites except: they cover head and face with a loose veil, do not raise voice, and walk normally in sa'ee.

Women's Head and Face Covering in Ihram
Ruling on women's head and face covering during ihram with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a woman in ihram regarding head and face covering, and explain the evidence from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
A woman in ihram must cover her head but leave her face uncovered; a tight veil is prohibited, but loose cloth may be hung for necessity.

The rulings for men and women differ significantly in ihram. While a man uncovers his head, a woman must cover it as part of her 'awrah. However, her face must remain open, and wearing a niqab (tight face veil) is forbidden. This lesson presents the evidence from the Prophet's statements and the practice of the Companions, detailing the method of permissible temporary covering when non-mahram men pass by.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific act being ruled upon: covering the head (wajib) and covering the face with a tight veil (haram) for a woman in ihram.
Also note the permissible method: loose hanging cloth without touching.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the three pieces of evidence cited: hadith of Ibn Umar, hadith of Aisha, and the athar of Ali.
Each evidence addresses a different aspect: the general rule, the method of temporary covering, and the prohibition of niqab.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For each evidence, explain how the text or practice leads to the ruling. For Ibn Umar: 'la ihrama illa fi wajhiha' implies the face must be exposed. For Aisha: the action shows covering when needed but without direct contact. For Ali: the instruction to 'let down loosely' confirms the method.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that the Shafi'i school permits covering the face if needed, whereas the Hanafi school strictly prohibits tight covering.
This difference is a matter of practical application (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that a woman must cover her head, leave her face uncovered, and may only temporarily hang a cloth away from the face when necessary.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

وجهها شيئا تحته عيدان كالقبة تمنع مسّه بالغطاء (۱۳۹۶) [1] پہلا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مرد احرام میں سر کو کھلا رکھے گا، لیکن عورت سرڈھانکے گی، کیونکہ یہ ستر کے خلاف ہے۔ البتہ چہرہ کھولے رکھے گی لیکن پردہ بھی کرنا ہے، اس لئے جو کپڑا چہرے پر لٹکائے گی اس کے نیچے لکڑی اس طرح باندھے کہ وہ قبہ کی طرح ہو جائے اور کپڑا اس کے اوپر لٹک جائے اور پردہ ہو جائے اور چہرے کو بھی نہ چھوئے۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان النبي عل الله قال ليس على المرأة احرام الا في وجهها ( دارقطني ، کتاب الحج ، ج ثانی، ص ۲۵۷، نمبر ۲۷۳۴ رسنن بیہقی ، باب المرأة لا تنتقب في احرامها ولا تلبس القفازين ، ج خامس ،ص ۷۵، نمبر ۹۰۴۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کا احترام اس کے چہرے میں ہے اس لئے وہ کپڑا چہرے سے دور رکھے گی۔ اور سر ڈھانکے گی ۔(۲) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن عائشة قالت كان الركبان يمرون بنا ونحن مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاذا صلى الله محرمات حاذوا بنا سدلت احدانا جلبابها من رأسها على وجهها فاذا جاوزونا کشفناه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی المحرمة تغطي وجهها ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۱۸۳۳ رابن ماجہ شریف، باب المحرمة تسدل الثوب على وجھا ص ۴۲۵، نمبر ۲۹۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرمہ عورت چہرہ کھلا رکھے اور کوئی اجنبی مرد سامنے آئے تو چہرے سے دور کر کے چادر وغیرہ چہرے پر لٹکا دے اس طرح سے کہ کپڑا چہرے سے مس نہ ہو۔ (۳) چہرے پر کپڑا کس طرح لٹکائے گی اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے . أن عـلـيـا كـان ينهي النساء عن النقاب و من حرم و لكن يسدلن الثوب عن وجوههن سدلا - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب في النقاب للمحرمة ، ج ثالث ص ۲۸۱، نمبر ۱۴۳۲۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ چہرے سے دور رکھ کر کپڑا لٹکالے۔
Her face: a thing under it sticks like a dome to prevent its touching by the covering (1396). [1] The first issue is that a man will keep his head uncovered in ihram, but a woman will cover her head, because this is against her covering. However, she will keep her face open, but she also must cover; therefore, the cloth she hangs over her face, underneath she ties sticks so that it becomes like a dome and the cloth hangs over it and it becomes a veil and does not touch her face. Evidence: (1) This hadith: From Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no ihram for a woman except in her face' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, vol. 2, p. 257, no. 2734; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Mar'ah la tantaqib fi ihramiha wa la talbas al-qafazayn, vol. 5, p. 75, no. 9049). From this hadith it is known that a woman's ihram is in her face, so she will keep cloth away from her face, and she will cover her head. (2) In this hadith: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: 'The riders used to pass by us while we were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in ihram. When they approached us, one of us would let down her garment from her head over her face, and when they passed by, we would uncover it' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-muhrimah tughatti wajhaha, p. 261, no. 1833; Ibn Majah, Bab al-muhrimah tasdul al-thawb 'ala wajhiha, p. 425, no. 2935). From this hadith it is known that a woman in ihram keeps her face open, and when a non-mahram man comes, she distances the cloth and hangs the sheet over her face in such a way that the cloth does not touch her face. (3) How she will hang cloth over her face, for this is the saying of a companion: 'Ali used to forbid women from the niqab and from covering (the face) in ihram, but (he said) they should let down the cloth over their faces loosely' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab fi al-niqab li-al-muhrimah, vol. 3, p. 281, no. 14326). In this effect it is that she keeps the cloth away from her face and hangs it.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for women in ihram regarding head and face covering. The author first states that a woman should make a dome-like structure beneath her cloth to prevent it from touching her face, then summarizes the prohibition of covering the face with a tight veil. The Urdu explanation clarifies: a man uncovers his head in ihram, but a woman must cover her head because her head is part of her 'awrah. However, she must keep her face uncovered, but if a non-mahram man approaches, she may lower a cloth over her face in such a way that it does not touch her skin. To achieve this, she can tie twigs underneath the cloth like a small dome. The evidence includes: (1) The hadith of Ibn 'Umar that the Prophet (s) said, 'There is no ihram for a woman except in her face,' meaning her face is the only part she must leave uncovered. (2) The hadith of 'A'ishah describing how they would lower their garments over their faces when male riders passed by, and remove them when they left. (3) The athar of 'Ali that he forbade women from wearing the niqab in ihram but instructed them to hang the cloth loosely away from the face. This demonstrates that the face must not be covered with a tight veil, but a loose covering for necessity is permitted.

Key Terms
ستر (satr): The part of the body that must be covered; for a woman, the whole body except face and hands is 'awrah in public.
نقاب (niqab): A face veil that covers the face, often touching the skin; prohibited in ihram for women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a woman in ihram regarding covering her face?
A) She must cover it with a tight veil.
B) She must leave it uncovered but may hang a cloth without touching.
C) She must cover it with a cloth touching the skin.
D) She may cover it with any cloth she likes.

Key Takeaway
In ihram, a woman must cover her head but keep her face uncovered; a tight veil is haram, but a loose cloth may be hung for necessity without touching the skin.
